Ear Gate

Huangdi's Suwen

The Theory of Vital Energy Connecting to Heaven

The yang energy expands when overworked, becoming depleted, and obstructs accumulation in the summer, causing people to suffer heatstroke, resulting in blindness and inability to see, and ear closure leading to incapacity to hear, feeling dazed as if the city is collapsing, and gushing continuously without stopping.

Note: This indicates that overwork injures the yang energy. The essence of yin and yang lies in yang being dense and stable. Overwork causes the yang energy to spread outward, preventing yin from obtaining the warmth and stability of yang, thus the essence escapes and becomes depleted internally. In autumn and winter, the yang energy is stored internally, while in summer it expands outward, hence leading to increased deficiency and heatstroke. With the essence and energy being deficient, blindness occurs, preventing sight, and ear closure leads to inability to hear.

Additionally, it is said: If the yang cannot overcome its yin, then the energies of the five organs contend, and the nine orifices will be blocked.

Note: The five organs represent yin, while the nine orifices are vessels that receive the energy. If the yin is excessive and the yang cannot overcome it, then the energies of the five organs clash internally, causing the nine orifices to be obstructed.

Jinkui's True Words Treatise

The southern region is red, entering and connecting to the heart, opening up to the ears.

Note: The section on diseases of the organs states: the separate energy flows to the ears to create hearing. The separate energy is governed by the heart's energy. Hence, it is said that the heart opens up to the ears.[1p]
On the Correspondence of Yin and Yang

The north brings cold; in the organs, it relates to the kidneys; in the orifices, it relates to the ears.

Note: The qi of the kidneys communicates with the ears; when the kidneys are harmonious, the ears can hear the five tones. Thus, the qi of the kidneys opens to the ears.

At the age of fifty, a person's body becomes heavy, and the ears and eyes no longer perceive clearly.

Note: At fifty, both the essence and blood become deficient. When deficient, they cannot ascend, leading to unclear hearing and sight.

The wise possess surplus energy; with surplus energy, the ears and eyes become perceptive.

Note: With surplus energy, the yang is abundant, hence the clarity of the ears and eyes.

The heavens are insufficient in the northwest, therefore the northwest is considered yin; and the right ear and eye of a person are not as bright as the left.

Note: The insufficiency of the heavens in the northwest indicates a deficiency of yin among the yang. In humans, the left side represents yang, while the right side represents yin. When yin is deficient above, the right ear and eye are not as bright as the left.

The east is yang; that which is yang gathers essence above. When it gathers essence above, the upper part thrives while the lower part becomes deficient, resulting in perceptive ears and eyes, but the hands and feet are not as agile. The west is yin; that which is yin gathers essence below. When it gathers essence below, the lower part thrives while the upper part is deficient, resulting in unclear ears and eyes but agile hands and feet. Hence, when subjected to pathogens, the affliction is more pronounced in the right if affected above, and more pronounced in the left if affected below. This is something that cannot be entirely fulfilled by the yin and yang of heaven and earth, hence pathogens reside there.

Note: This indicates that the yin and yang of heaven, earth, and the human body’s left and right sides cannot be entirely fulfilled. Therefore, humans ought to align with heaven and earth to nourish their heads and feet, and not allow pathogens to reside.[2p]
On the Generation of the Five Organs

Those afflicted with confusion and turmoil suffer from blurred vision and hearing loss. The lower portion is full while the upper portion is empty, leading to stagnation in the lesser yang and the jueyin, which may even extend to the liver.
[Note: The jueyin liver is connected to the eyes, and the lesser yang channel extends to the ears. When there is excess at the lower portion, the vital energy cannot ascend, resulting in blurred vision and hearing loss. The deficiency above causes movement in sight to become dim and confused, creating great disruption. This initially injures the vital energy and leads to a deficiency above, with subsequent worsening of the excess below.]

Conclusion of the Essentials of Diagnosis

When the lesser yang is exhausted, hearing loss occurs, and all joints become slack. Vision becomes utterly disconnected. When this disconnection happens, death is imminent in a day and a half. In death, the complexion first turns blue and white, and thereafter one passes away.
[Note: The channels of the lesser yang in the hands and feet trace to the ears, hence the hearing loss when the vital energy is cut off. The lesser yang governs the bones, and since all joints relate to bones, slackness in all joints occurs when the lesser yang energy is exhausted. The lesser yang channel reaches the sharp corners of the eyes, and when it is finished, it pulls at the eyes, causing startled and distorted vision. The lesser yang is associated with the kidney, which houses the will; if the connection to the eyes is severed, the will is lost first, leading to imminent death within a day and a half. The blue color represents the energy of wood, while the white color signifies the internal loss of the essence of the triple burner.]

On the True Organ of the Jade Mechanism[3p]
When the spleen is insufficient, it causes the nine orifices to become obstructed, leading to a condition known as "heavy strength." The commentary states: if the five organs are not harmonious, the nine orifices will not be unblocked. Now that the energy of the spleen is insufficient, the energies of the five organs are also not harmonious. The stomach, as the Yang of the earth, has strong energy, while the spleen, as the Yin of the earth, has weak energy. When the spleen is weak and unable to take in the essential energies from food and water, the stomach's energy becomes even stronger; hence, it is called "heavy strength." This means the spleen's deficiency prevents it from transporting fluids for the stomach. The stomach is strong while the spleen is weak, resulting in disharmony between the organs.

In cases of sudden faintness and deafness, where there is obstruction and inability to communicate internally, the internal energy must be greatly diminished. This does not arise from wind-induced conditions inside or outside; therefore, the patient is left weak. The commentary notes: faintness and deafness arise from reversed energy rising upwards, obstructing the upper orifices. When there is blocking and stagnation below, reversed energy descends, resulting in the obstruction of the lower orifices. This indicates both internal and external afflictions leading to obstructed orifices. If one does not succumb to internal worries and anger or external wind leading to severe illness or early demise, it results from physical weakness and diminished energy, causing a thin frame and delicate skin.

Disharmony among the five organs leads to blocking within the six hollow organs. Symptoms like headaches and tinnitus arise from the obstruction of the nine orifices, which in turn is produced by issues in the stomach and intestines. The commentary clarifies: when the energies of the five organs are long-term reversed and thus remain unharmonized, it produces blockages in the six hollow organs. When the six hollow organs are not harmonious, the nine orifices will not function properly. The interrelatedness of Yin and Yang within the organs is such that external symptoms reflect internal troubles; thus, blockages within give rise to obstructions in the orifices.[4p]

Hot Discussions

For three days of the cold damage, the lesser yang is affected. The lesser yang governs the gallbladder, and its pulse runs along the side and connects at the ear; hence, there is chest and side pain along with deafness. After nine days, the lesser yang illness weakens, and the deafness is faintly discernible.

Note: The energy of the lesser yang governs the pivot and the gallbladder; when the gallbladder's energy rises, all the yang energies rise correspondingly, as if prompted by cold that seeks to move the pivot. All yang energies emerge from the pivot and sides to the skin surface. The greater yang governs the exterior, the yangming governs the muscles, and the lesser yang governs the chest and flanks. Chest and flank pain combined with deafness indicates a disease in the energy manifesting as tangible symptoms.

When the disease is affected by cold in both aspects, after three days, both the lesser yang and the jueyin become ill, leading to deafness, retraction of the pouch and cold extremities, inability to ingest liquids, and unconsciousness, resulting in death on the sixth day.

Note: The lesser yang and jueyin are interrelated; thus, the manifestation of deafness in the lesser yang corresponds with the retraction and cold extremities in the jueyin. Inability to ingest liquids indicates a complete loss of digestive energy. Unconsciousness suggests damage to the spirit energy. When all organs and viscera are afflicted and the protective and nutritive energies fail to circulate, the exhaustion of energy leads to death.[5p]
The reverse of the hand Taiyang leads to deafness, tears flow, and the neck cannot turn while the waist cannot bend or straighten; this treats the diseases of the master.

(Note: The diseases born from the hand Taiyang involve deafness. The small intestine governs fluids, hence the reversal leads to tears. The heart governs blood vessels, while the small intestine governs fluids and represents the heart externally. If the qi of the small intestine reverses, then the fluids cannot nourish the meridians, which is why the neck cannot turn and the waist cannot bend or straighten. The area between the waist and neck is where the major pathways of the meridians converge.)

The reversal of Shaoyang leads to sudden deafness, swelling and heat in the cheeks, side pain, and the ankle cannot move.

(Note: The meridian of the foot Shaoyang begins at the corner of the eye, travels behind the ear into the ear canal, descends to the jaw, runs through the chest and sides, exits at the outer knee, and follows along the foot. Therefore, the reversal leads to sudden deafness, cheek swelling, side pain, and the foot ankle cannot move.)

The so-called tinnitus of Taiyang arises from the exuberance of yang energy, which makes everything thrive and leap, hence the ringing in the ears.

(Note: This refers to the increased vitality of yang energy. In spring, during the third month, what is referred to as spring emergence occurs when heaven and earth give birth, and all things flourish. Thus, the energy of heaven and earth thrives and leaps upwards. Likewise, the yang energy in humans also flourishes upwards, leading to congestion in the meridians and causing tinnitus.)

The so-called floating deafness of Taiyang is entirely due to qi.

(Note: This clarifies the differentiations of meridian qi. The ringing, where yang energy is exuberant and leads to tinnitus, is due to qi affecting the meridians. However, the so-called floating deafness is entirely due to qi.)[6p]

Commentary on the Prohibition of Assassins

The assassin's master improperly collapses the central meridian, causing internal leakage and deafness.
[Note: This suggests that if the assassin's master over-indulges, he mistakenly affects the internal collapse of the meridian, resulting in leakage and deafness in the ears.]

Needle Release Chapter

The five senses of hair, teeth, ears, and eyes respond to the five sounds, corresponding to the five notes and six scales.
[Note: Hair, teeth, ears, and eyes total six, while teeth alone count for six, and the number of hairs cannot be counted. The mathematical system of rhythms can extend infinitely; hence, its number surpasses even ten thousand, illustrating the endless interconnections between heaven, earth, and humanity.]

Great Discussion on Qi Transformation

In a year with excessive fire, intense heat circulates, afflicting the lungs (metal) with malevolent influences, causing the people to suffer from malaria with low energy, coughs and wheezing, blood overflow and profuse bleeding, dry throat and deafness.
[Note: In a year where fire is overly dominant, it overwhelms metal, hence the lungs are afflicted. The lungs are the origin of water; excessive heat damages metal and depletes this source. The kidneys open to the ears, thus kidney deficiency leads to deafness.]

In a year with excessive metal, dry air circulates, affecting the liver (wood). The people suffer from pain in the sides and lower abdomen, eye redness and painful sores, and are unable to hear.
[Note: In years dominated by metal, the prevalence of dry air causes liver ailments, resulting in deafness due to liver deficiency.][7p]
Discussion on the Five Constant Virtues

The Yin aspect governs heaven; the wind and air descend, the spleen's energy rises. The body feels heavy, muscles weaken, appetite decreases, and the mouth feels dry; the eyes shift, and there is ringing in the ears. 【Note: The shifting of the eyes and ringing in the ears is due to the influence of wind above.】

Discussion on the Six Fundamentals

The Shao Yang governs heaven; people suffer from deafness and dimness of vision. 【Note: Deafness and dimness are due to the internal influence of wind and heat.】 The Yin aspect governs heaven; the energy of the Three causes ringing in the ears and dizziness. 【Note: Ringing in the ears and dizziness arise from wind-related illness above.】 When wood is obstructed, it becomes severe; thus, ears ring and dizziness occurs. 【Note: Ringing in the ears and dizziness are the result of wind energy causing illness.】 For the Shao Yang, this leads to throat blockage, ear ringing, and vomiting. 【Note: This is a common illness in autumn.】 When wood is obstructed, people suffer from pain in the stomach and pericardium, discomfort in the upper sides, blockage in the diaphragm and throat, inability to ingest food and drink; in severe cases, there is ringing in the ears and dizziness, and one cannot recognize others, often collapsing. 【Note: This results from the influence of the heavenly principle at the spring, leading to extreme obstruction, retaliating against its seasonal energy. For example, in the Ding Mao and Ding You years, the minor wood energy rises to meet the Yang Ming; in the Ren Zi and Ren Wu years, the major wood energy rises while the Yang Ming is at the spring, leading to extreme wood energy. This causes blockage in the stomach, diaphragm, and throat, preventing food and drink intake, with wood overwhelming and harming earth. Discomfort in the upper sides and ringing and dizziness in the ears follow. The inability to recognize people indicates a wind-related illness.】[8p]
Discussion on the Primordial Truth

When the Liver (Taiyin) excels, it causes ringing in the ears and dizziness.
[Note: The influence of the external wind and wood elements surpasses above, hence the ear ringing and dizziness.] When the Liver excels, it leads to ear ringing, head dizziness, nausea, and a sensation of cold in the stomach.
[Note: Ear ringing and head dizziness arise because the wood element is excessive above. Nausea and a cold sensation in the stomach indicate a stomach disorder.] When the Gallbladder (Shaoyang) excels, it brings heat to the stomach, causing restlessness, heart pain, reddened eyes, nausea, sour vomiting, a good appetite, ear pain, red urine, fright, delirium, and lower abdominal pain with darkened or light-colored discharge. The treatment involves using warming and cold herbs, complemented by sweet and salty flavors to facilitate drainage.
[Note: The influence of the Gallbladder excels in the Triple Warmer, hence the heat affecting the stomach. The essence of the Triple Warmer originates from the stomach. The Triple Warmer and the heart are closely connected, causing restlessness and heart pain. The channels of the Triple Warmer ascend to the ears and connect to the eyes, which is why excessive influence manifests as ear pain.][9p]
The Lesser Yin governs the heavens; when it is afflicted, symptoms include sneezing, stiffness in the neck, heat in the shoulders and back, headaches, shortness of breath, fever, deafness, and closed eyes.

(Note: The Lesser Yin governing the heavens corresponds to the energy associated with the Jueyin wood of wind, where deafness indicates an excess of Jueyin energy.)

The Lesser Yang governs the heavens; when it is afflicted, it results in external rashes and sores, vomiting, throat obstruction, headaches and throat swelling, deafness, bleeding, and internal conditions of convulsions. When there is excess, it leads to fullness in the chest, cough, and possibly blood.

(Note: The Lesser Yang governing the heavens corresponds to the initial phase of the three energies, being the dual fires of the monarch and minister. Symptoms like deafness are indicative of diseases caused by wind and fire.)

In years of the Greater Yin, people suffer from deafness, disorientation, and throat swelling and obstruction.

(Note: The Greater Yin corresponds to the years of Chen and Xu. The afflictions of deafness are linked to diseases of the Sanjiao meridian.)[10p]
Lingshu Classic

Chapter on Pathological Symptoms of Organs from Evils

When the heart meridian is slightly obstructed, it causes tinnitus.
[Note: The red color associated with the southern region enters the heart and opens the orifice to the ears. A slight obstruction in the heart meridian indicates a deficiency in heart qi, leading to tinnitus.] The twelve meridians and three hundred sixty-five collaterals all have blood and qi that rise to the face and traverse the hollow orifices; their associated qi travels to the ears to facilitate hearing.
[Note: The associated qi refers to the heart and kidney qi that go to the ears and enable hearing.]

Chapter on Meridians

The small intestine hand taiyang is responsible for diseases arising from bodily fluids, leading to hearing loss, jaundice, and facial swelling. The triple burner hand shaoyang, when activated, causes hearing loss, dizziness, swelling of the throat, and throat obstruction.
[Note: All of these are ailments corresponding to the pathways of the meridians.] The hand yangming collaterals connect to the ears, resulting in deafness.
[Note: This is due to qi stagnation causing the deafness.]

Chapter on Tendons

The tendon of the hand taiyang has branches that enter the ear and a straight pathway that extends above and below the ear; the corresponding ailment results in ringing in the ears and pain that radiates to the jaw.
[Note: This illness arises from the path traversed by the taiyang tendon.]

Chapter on Pulse Measurement[11p]
The kidney's vitality is connected to the ears; when the kidneys are harmonious, the ears can perceive the five sounds. If the five organs are not in harmony, then the seven orifices are not open.

In the section on heat illnesses, when one does not know the source of pain, and experiences deafness and cannot hear oneself, along with dryness of the mouth and excessive yang heat—if there is also considerable cold from yin, then the heat is within the marrow, leading to death if not treated.

In the section of inquiries, the Yellow Emperor asked: "What energy causes ringing in the ears?" Qi Bo replied: "In the ears, there is a concentration of the ancestral vessels. When the stomach is empty, the ancestral vessels become deficient; when they are deficient, energy flows downwards, leading to a depletion of the pulse, and hence the ringing in the ears."

The lungs are related to the hundred pulses, and the ancestral vessels are the root of these hundred pulses, governed by the lungs. The ears are where the ancestral vessels gather. The blood and energy of the hundred pulses are produced by food and water. Therefore, when the stomach is empty, the ancestral vessels are deficient, causing the energy of the pulses to flow downwards. When the blood and energy within the pulse are depleted, it leads to ringing in the ears. Additionally, if the upper qi is insufficient, the ears suffer from painful ringing.

This indicates that the bladder lacks sufficient fluids and cannot moisten the empty orifices, resulting in insufficient righteous qi and the emergence of strange and evil diseases.[12p]
Teacher's Transmission Chapter

The kidneys govern the external, enabling distant hearing. Observe the qualities of the ears to understand their nature.

If essence is depleted, hearing loss occurs; if fluid is deficient, bones are unable to bend or extend properly, complexion fades, brain marrow diminishes, shins ache, and the ears ring frequently.

Sea Discussion

If the sea of marrow is insufficient, there will be dizziness and ringing in the ears.

Organs Chapter

Small and dark ears indicate weak kidneys, coarse ears imply strong kidneys; high ears suggest high kidneys, while sunken ears indicate lower kidney function; firm ears show strong kidneys, whereas thin and soft ears suggest weak kidneys; ears that sit forward show correct kidney alignment, while ears that are placed high indicate a tilt in kidney position.[13p]

The Difficulties of Bian Que’s Classic

The Reason Ears Can Hear Sounds

In the fortieth difficulty, it is said: the lung governs sound, the ear is the opening of the kidney and is able to hear sounds; what does this signify? Indeed. The kidney corresponds to the water of the northern direction. Water is born in Shen, and Shen corresponds to the western metal; metal corresponds to the lung, which governs sound, thus allowing the ear to hear sounds. The lung is metal, and sounds arise from metal; hence, the lung governs sound. Although the nose belongs to the lung and cannot hear sounds, the ear belongs to the kidney and is able to hear. How is this possible? The kidney corresponds to the northern water and the branches of Shen, You, and Xu. Shen is the place where metal is exalted. Metal in the viscera is the lung, which governs sound. Although the ear belongs to the kidney—water—it is derived from the position of the lung, which is metal, thus enabling the ear to hear sounds.[14p]
The Classic of the Hidden Writings by Hua Tuo

The Connection of the Kidney and the Ear

The kidney is the residence of the spirit and the root of life, externally connected to the ears.

Deafness

If liver qi is counterflowing, it causes headaches and deafness with a flushed face. The pulse is deep and rapid, or floating and rapid. If the ears are unable to hear and the pulse is floating, large, and slack, it indicates impending death.

Ominous Signs of Ear Conditions

If black color appears in the ears and eyes, gradually entering the mouth, it signifies death. If red color is seen in the ears, eyes, and forehead, death occurs within five days. If there is dryness in the ears due to kidney deficiency, death follows in six days.

The Classic of the Primordial Yin by Huangfu Mi

The Connection of the Kidney and the Ear

The kidney qi connects to the ears; when the ears are harmonious, one can hear the five sounds. The classic states, "The kidney manifests in the orifices as the ear." Thus, kidney qi ascends to the ears and descends to the yin.

Ear Burning and Dryness

If the ears are burnt and dry due to dust and filth, the illness resides in the bones.

Direct Instruction of the Ren Zhai by Yang Shiying

Deafness[15p]
The kidneys connect to the ears, and they govern essence. When essence and vital energy are balanced and kidney energy is abundant, the ears are able to hear clearly. However, if excessive labor injures the blood and vital energy, or if wind pathogens attack a weakened state, causing the essence to dissipate and the kidneys to weaken, then hearing may turn to deafness. There are also cases of deafness caused by qi obstruction, by wind invasion, or by labor damage. The twelve meridians converge at the ears; when the yin and yang channels intersect appropriately, the organ energy may reverse and lead to obstruction, which then affects the ears—this is known as obstructive deafness, and dizziness may accompany it at times.

The ears are connected to the governing vessel; if the vessel is vacuous and wind pathogens invade, wind enters the channels of the ears, obstructing the normal flow of energy—this is referred to as wind deafness, often accompanied by headaches. If excessive labor damages blood and energy, and indulgent desires deplete essence, resulting in emaciation and fatigue, this is called labor deafness. If one can properly maintain balance, with blood and energy harmonized, the deafness may temporarily lessen. If labor injury and wind stagnation persist, this leads to chronic deafness.

Moreover, if the ear is assaulted by wind pathogens and collides with qi, the resulting sound may be noisy, and one might perceive flashes before the eyes, indicating phantom sounds. If heat energy accumulates in a vacuous state and follows the channels into the ears without dispersing, resulting in pus discharge, it is known as ear pus. There is fluid between the ears; if light, it poses no harm, but if attacked by wind-heat, the fluids can coagulate, creating a blockage in the ear, leading to sudden deafness known as cerumen impaction.

The aforementioned conditions can be inferred from the kidney channels: wind can be superficial and abundant, heat can be surging and substantial, while a vacuous state can be thin and moist. Wind disperses, heat clears and facilitates, and a vacuous state requires nourishment. When the pathogenic qi retreats, one can then use remedies to open the ears, adjust the qi, and soothe the kidneys.[16p]
Complete Book of Sores and Ulcers
By Jin Dou Hanqing

Ear Wind Poison

Ear wind poison affects the heart meridian, caused by kidney energy not circulating, stagnating in the heart meridian, resulting in damage to the ear. The five types of ear ailments—ear abscess, ear fungus, ear boil, ear dampness, and ear rot—can be treated with a liver-clearing flow drink, followed by a pain-relieving descending qi decoction. If encountering ear abscess or ear fungus, first prick and rupture with a needle, then apply red jade ointment. For ear swelling and pain, drip tiger ear grass juice into the ear, and the pain will cease. For ear boils, drip strong liquor on the boil’s root to relieve it, then wash with bitter tea to counteract the alcohol poison.

Ear Gate Boil

Ear gate boil affects the liver meridian, with toxic energy causing blood stagnation. This is a malevolent condition and should be treated with boiled medicines.[17p]
Ear Root Abscess

The ear root abscess affects the kidney meridian, caused by anger harming the heart, stagnating the liver meridian, and the accumulation of wind-heat leading to toxicity. It should be treated with eyebrow wind medicine, or with the Clear Liver Qi Flowing Decoction for relief.

Ear Carbuncle

The sore arises near the ear and is also called a hot toxin abscess. Within five or six days, it grows resembling a beehive, and if the skin appears purple, it is hot, with sensations like being burned, causing unbearable pain, and can be punctured after ten days. If no pus is present, death may occur after eleven days. If the sore is soft and white pus is seen, it will not be fatal; if yellow pus emerges, it will not result in death. Continuous fresh blood or red pus signifies mortality. Those who cannot taste food or tell lies may also die. Between twenty days, signs of fortune or misfortune will appear. When preparing medicine, use the Qianjin Neituo Powder, adjusting as needed.

Stone Abscess

Although similar to stone boils, stone abscesses show deep cold residing in the meridian, with blood and qi accumulating and not dispersing, hidden under the skin, and swollen to the touch like stone. This poison connects to the neck, internal decay occurs first, before breaking through the skin. If the marrow appears at the neck, it results in death. Use methods to drain pus and internally replenish with the Ten Xuan Powder, waiting until the pus is fully expelled, then supplement internally; for persistent heat, use Frankincense Heart Protection Powder, applying golden silk ointment, adding five flavors, tianhua fen, dry kudzu, maidenhair, and black plum if there is extreme thirst. At the onset, moxibustion on the affected area with moxa fire for thirty or forty times is necessary. If occurring on the forehead or face, it is untreatable.

Jisheng Formula (Song Dynasty, Yan Yonghe)[18p]
Discussion on the Ear

The ear is the organ of the kidneys; the kidneys are where essence is stored. When kidney energy is sufficient, the vital essence rises and one can hear the five tones clearly. However, if one becomes overly fatigued and the vital essence is deficient, then external influences such as wind, cold, heat, and dampness can invade, and emotional disturbances like joy, anger, worry, and thought can cause internal injury, leading to deafness. Tinnitus, heat accumulation, along with bleeding or pus formation, can result in problems deep within the ear. If the complexion of the cheeks and temples is dark, it indicates deafness. There are cases where the lesser yang meridian is blocked and causes deafness, manifesting as a fiery sensation inside the ear. Conversely, if the greater yang meridian is blocked and causes deafness, there is fullness of energy in the ear. Generally, deafness due to energy blockage is relatively easier to treat, while deafness due to the loss of vital essence is harder to remedy with medicine. Different symptoms correspond to various treatment methods.

The ear reflects the state of the kidneys. The kidneys gather the essence, which flows to the ear. When kidney energy is balanced, one can hear the five tones clearly. When kidney energy is unbalanced, the ear suffers illness. Medical texts state that kidney energy connects to the ears. The heart resides in the ear; external factors like wind, cold, heat, dampness, dryness, and heat impact the kidneys, while internal sources of distress such as worry and contemplation can create sores, resulting in deafness or swelling.

The six climatic factors harm the kidneys, and the seven emotions affect the heart. The method of treatment involves calming the heart and regulating energy. To ensure the energy flows smoothly and the heart is tranquil, the ear will respond with clarity. One should use a formula called "Miao Xiang San," preparing it with calamus to brew a decoction to harmonize the heart's energy. Herbs like ginseng, dan, honey, and sand should be used to calm the heart. Additionally, medicines for regulating the kidneys, such as Cistanche, should be incorporated.[19p]
The Six Books of Hejian (by Liu Wansuo)

Deafness

Deafness is considered a disease, and common physicians often treat it with harsh and aggressive remedies, claiming it is due to the deficiency of kidney water and coldness. But do they not understand the balance of yin and yang between water and fire, the cold and heat of the heart and kidneys, the flourishing and declining of nourishment and defense? It is a matter of balance: when one side rises, the other must fall. This is the principle of harmonious regulation.

The heart fire is inherently hot; if it is deficient, it turns cold. The kidney water is inherently cold; if it diminishes, it turns hot. If the kidney water is already low, how can it result in cold illness? The classic texts state: "When the kidney water of the lesser yin is deficient, it leads to fullness in the abdomen, heaviness in the body, watery diarrhea, ulcers that ooze, pain in the lower back and hips, stiffness in the joints and knees, anxiety, weakness in the legs, lack of joy, difficulty in bowel movements, a sense of fear as if being pursued, a bitter mouth, dry tongue, swelling in the throat, dry throat and pain, heart trouble and chest pain, jaundice, bowel discomfort with blood, pain in the spine, buttocks, and back of the thighs, weakness and desire to lie down, and heat and pain in the feet." From this, it is evident that the symptoms of kidney deficiency are all signs of heat.

The texts further state: "If one travels far and is exhausted, and encounters extreme heat and thirst, thirst will lead to the inner consumption of yang energy, which refers to the consumption of the yin energy within the stomach; water cannot withstand fire, leading to heat remaining in the kidneys." The texts also mention: "Bone weakness arises from extreme heat." Moreover, it states: "Kidney heat causes dark complexion and brittle teeth." Generally, individuals with a dark complexion and brittle teeth will also be thin and have overheated ears.[20p]
The principle is this: when water is deficient, fire is abundant and hot. Excess leads to harm; thus, one must regulate it. Therefore, one counteracts the blackness of water. When kidney water is weak and scarce, it cannot moisten, resulting in dryness and withering. The teeth and ears are associated with the kidneys, hence their severity. If sores or ulcers become extremely hot with no moisture, the flesh becomes dry and blackened. Thus, when water is weak, heat clearly arises; how can one then claim it is cold?

Hence, the "Immortal Classic" states that the breath corresponds to the six-character qi, which corresponds to the six energies of the three yin and three yang organs. In reality, it manifests as the fundamental transformations leading to expulsion; when weakened, it follows the path of dominance consistent with expulsion to eliminate its obstructions. The so-called six-character qi includes liver hissing, heart exhaling, fire’s sighing, spleen calling, lung's breathing, and kidney’s blowing. Thus, by blowing away the cold from the kidneys, heat is generated; and by exhaling away the heart’s heat, cold is produced.

It is said that in spring, one does not blow; in summer, one does not exhale; in autumn, one does not hiss; in winter, one does not breathe out; throughout the four seasons, there are constant sighs, indicating the three burners are never insufficient; if the eight seasons cannot be blown, it means the kidneys find it hard to be robust. Observing through blowing, when the cold emotions of kidney water are expelled, the yang heat surges, and one experiences blurring of vision and dizziness. Weakness gives proof of heat. How can one then reverse this and use heating medicines to nourish water? Moreover, if water is scarce, it cannot overcome fire, and taking hot medicine, would it not be damaging? The classics state to treat heat with cold—this means cooling to curb fire and to treat cold with heat—this means heating to help fire and exhaust water.[21p]
The text discusses the relationship between heat and cold in medical treatment. It states that although some may argue that heat can be treated by heat, the idea is derived from the notion that a patient's heat condition is severe and cold medicine is hard to administer; therefore, one may take heat-inducing remedies to follow the nature of the illness. Once the heat dissipates, the cold nature will emerge, leading to recovery from the heat illness.

It further explains that similar principles apply in the treatment of cold diseases. The text refers to the principle that cold is used to treat heat and heat to treat cold, emphasizing that these are still methods for treating heat-related conditions. The essence of treatment lies in reducing excess and nourishing deficiencies, achieving balance.

There is a caution against mistakenly categorizing heat as a manifestation of fire and cold as a manifestation of water, particularly in the context of kidney deficiency viewed as cold. The author warns against using cold medicine out of fear; instead, mistakenly opting for warming tonics before meals to counteract an overwhelming heat from the heart, only to take slightly cooling medicines post-meal to reduce heat. However, one might not realize that such approaches do more harm than good.

Moreover, if a disease essentially originates from heat and one consumes heating medicines, the condition can worsen despite later attempts to consume cold medicines. The wrong approach can lead to further complications. It highlights that the proper method does not support the idea of nurturing water to dampen fire.

In conclusion, it emphasizes that the balance of the five internal organs is the goal. This principle stands irrespective of the specific dynamics of each organ's functions and imbalances. Ultimately, the discussion revolves around the fluctuations in yang energy and the idea that if the lower body is cold, it indicates a deficiency of fire energy in the lower region; thus, heating remedies are used not to support kidney water, as deficient water cannot turn into cold.[22p]
Diseases arise not solely from the decline or changes in the internal organs but rather from the harm inflicted by internal and external evils. Hence, they lead to illness. Generally, when treating diseases, one must identify the source. If the illness is in the upper part, treat the upper; if in the lower, treat the lower; this applies to all internal organs, channels, and collaterals. If the pathogenic energy is heat, then eliminate the heat; if it is cold, then dispel the cold; the same principle applies to the six qi. Differentiate between excess and deficiency, expel evils and nourish the right, maintain balance, and this is the way of medicine. It is unwise to see a condition characterized by heat and then apply heat remedies while claiming to nourish water to overcome heart fire. This can be seen as seeking the path nearby while looking far away, pursuing ease while seeking difficulty, and it should be cautioned against! Thus, when it is said that kidney deficiency results in cold in the lower part, it does not imply that kidney water is deficient. It is said that there are two kidneys; the classics state that beside the seventh vertebra, there is a small heart located within. Yang Shangshan annotates "Tai Su" stating: the human spine has twenty-one segments, with the left side of the seventh segment being the kidney and the right being the Mingmen, which refers to the small heart. The "Nanjing" mentions that the origin of the heart emerges from the Tai Ling, and the Tai Ling point belongs to the Hand Jueyin and is associated with the fire of the small heart. The "Yuan Zhu" states that needling the Tai Ling point is to drain the fire originating from the small heart. Therefore, the right kidney and Mingmen correspond to the small heart, which is connected to the Hand Jueyin’s fire. The "Xian Jing" states: the right kidney represents the male, and the left kidney represents the female. This is because the male is associated with Yang fire and the female with Yin water. To claim that a woman's left kidney is the Mingmen is a mistake.[23p]
The "Nanjing" states that the right kidney is the gate of life; for men, it stores essence, whereas for women, it connects to the womb. Can these be contrary? However, the right kidney, as the gate of life, is closely associated with the hand's Jueyin organ, thus forming a relationship with the hand's Shaoyang Sanjiao in terms of interior and exterior, sharing the same divine pulse, as seen in the right wrist. Both channels represent the fire of the sovereign and minister, hence it is called the gate of life. Therefore, the "Xianjing" states: the heart is the sovereign fire, and the kidney is the minister fire. This indicates that the right kidney belongs to fire and not to water; thus, a deficiency of fire in the right kidney leads to cold illness. Although the sovereign and minister are two types of fire, in terms of the theory of the five elements, they are one in heat.

In the theory of the five elements, there is yin within yang and yang within yin; lonely yin does not thrive and alone yang does not persist. Only when a being fully encompasses the five elements and mutually nourishes one another can there be peace. Interactions leading to overcoming and destruction signify rise and fall. Disruption and deviation from the norm give rise to disasters. Thus, when water is scarce and fire abundant, there is yang excess and yin deficiency, causing illness from heat; when there is an abundance of water and scarcity of fire, there is yin excess and yang deficiency, causing illness from cold. Hence, using heat-inducing medicines to nourish the kidney and overpower the heart fire is misguided.

Whether due to indulgence leading to illness or prolonged conditions resulting in sickness, it is mistakenly considered that it is due to a deficiency of the original qi causing cold illness. However, the disturbances and strains are largely transformations of yang fire, with numerous cases of over-excitement and chaotic qi resulting in heat illness. Thus, the classics mention the ailments of heat and those related to the transformations of yin and yang and the exhausting of sexual energy.[24p]
Therefore, when fever has not yet receded, and in cases of excessive drunkenness leading to rapid calamity, it is because yang heat can easily become violent. The essence of Taiyi, the true original qi, is neither yin nor yang, neither cold nor hot. Hence, the essence produces qi, and qi gives rise to spirit, with the spirit able to control its form. Thus, essence is the root of spirit and qi, and provides substance to the body. When strong, it is difficult for various pathogens to harm, but when weak, numerous diseases can easily invade. Why then does one say that original qi is deficient and becomes cold? Thus, in the elderly, qi declines, leading to many ailments such as dizziness, tinnitus, or deafness, shortness of breath, coughing, thick and sticky saliva, bitter mouth and dry tongue, difficulty in the throat, weakness in limbs, muscular atrophy, and dryness inside and outside, with constipation or urinary issues. These are all symptoms of heat due to yin deficiency and yang excess. Commonly, it is said that the elderly and weak are deficient in cold and lack heat.[25p]
Even though it is said that the manifestation of heat becomes less effective with a deficiency of water, and that the deficiency of kidney water is regarded as cold, this misunderstanding is prevalent worldwide. One must discern the interplay of yin and yang, of deficiency and excess, at the right time to avoid unwarranted suffering. One must be cautious not to recklessly use heating medicines to nourish one's true energy, for how can true energy be generated then? Thus, the "Western Mountain Records" states: if one consumes golden stones, there will be the danger of swift demise. The "Inner Canon" says that stone medicines cause madness, as they are born of excessive heat. If one wishes to use warming medicines for supplementation, the texts indicate that accumulated warmth leads to heat diseases; therefore, medications should not be taken recklessly. The method of nourishing true energy relies on a balanced diet, regular living habits, and avoiding undue labor to prevent harm, with a harmonious balance of yin and yang. This alone is beneficial. Although the "Immortal Classics" mention the consumption of elixirs, they are not suitable for everyone. Moreover, it is crucial to harmonize with substances that are neutral and non-toxic, simply to regulate one's energy.[26p]
A true practitioner of the Dao regards internal affairs as the essence of achievement and external affairs as the means of conduct; they do not rely on elixirs while hoping to attain the Dao. Therefore, the "Immortal Classics" further states that if one takes elixirs without preparing the five flavors and four energies and instead focuses on a single type, over time, the internal organs will be misaligned, leading to illness. How could one mistakenly take a hot remedy and expect benefits? It is said that deafness arises from the decline of water and the fullness of fire, with heat blocking the pathways, thus obstructing the entrance to the audible. What is observed is that when one closes their ears with both hands, it resembles the sound of a drum; this is called the celestial drum. The vital energy circulates and is blocked in the ears, leading to sound within, hence the ability to hear. If there is obstruction, the celestial drum is faintly heard. If the celestial drum is inaudible, then the entrance to hearing is completely closed, resulting in deafness where nothing is heard. Thus, one method involves soaking needle, sand, and wine, applying a magnet to the ear, intending to guide the energy to unblock it.

If someone asks: Since deafness relates to heat, why is it that taking spicy hot things like dried scorpion, ginger, aconite, and strong liquor sometimes leads to recovery? The answer is: They aim to open the entrance and allow the stagnant energy within the ears to flow out. Therefore, in the practice of preserving health, using medicinals with effective results can be likened to hearing a symphony of joyous sounds, as yang energy opens the pathways. In treating deafness, one must tailor their approach; if the heat condition has subsided yet deafness remains, then spicy and warming remedies should be used to stimulate. If a few doses do not yield results, it should not be continued for long, as excessive heat may lead to other ailments. If deafness is associated with a hot condition, it is advisable to use cooling remedies that dispel wind and clear heat to achieve recovery. However, if the deafness is severely blocked, it becomes quite difficult to treat.[27p]
One must be cautious not to attack too aggressively, as it may harm the vital energy. If it is not the correct illness, do not administer the remedy. Dietary principles should be followed: what is appropriate must not be taken to excess, or it will backfire against the vital energy. When the illness is gone, cease the medications. To seek health without harm is all that is needed. Therefore, regarding the treatment of serious poisons, ten methods eliminate six; for minor poisons, ten methods eliminate seven; for chronic poisons, ten methods eliminate eight; for non-poisons, ten methods eliminate nine. Nourish with grains, meat, fruits, and vegetables, and do not exceed, lest the vital energy be harmed. Practices should not be continued indefinitely, returning to the appropriate methods. Thus it is said: one must first account for seasonal influences, avoiding disturbance to the heavenly harmony. Do not have substance without emptiness, nor emptiness without substance, to prevent calamity for humankind. Do not invite evil, nor lose the proper way, which would cut off longevity.

Exhaustion of the Yang energy accumulates in summer, causing heat syncope, resulting in blindness and deafness. Ginseng powder serves as its remedy.

The ears are not singular. In terms of perception, they are associated with water; in terms of sound, with metal. In terms of channels, both the lesser Yang of the hands and feet converge here. If there are sounds from within that cannot be heard, it relates to the master; if there are sounds from outside that cannot be perceived, it relates to the channels. There are sounds like cicadas, like chiming bells, or like roaring flames, each corresponding to the channels, and one must discern between the virtual and the actual. If one assumes that deafness relates to the kidneys, what then is the treatment for the lungs? The lungs govern sound; nasal congestion pertains to the lungs. What then is the treatment for the heart? The heart governs smell. By applying this method, all begins with the reception of energy. The kidneys receive energy at the hour of Si, the heart at the hour of Hai, the liver at the hour of Shen, the lungs at the hour of Yin, and the spleen governs all four seasons. This method is the way to longevity.[28p]
Tinnitus

Tinnitus involves sound, and it is not mere imagination. The ear is the orifice of the kidneys and connects with the channels of the hand's yang, the lesser yang, and the foot's lesser yin and lesser yang. When the water is deficient and the fire is excessive, with heat rising significantly and invading its channels, it strikes the auditory organs, producing sounds corresponding to the subtle variations in the pulse. The classics say that yang rises, causing things to flourish, hence the tinnitus.

Sound of the Ear Pipe

When the heart is deficient and evil winds combine, one hears false sounds like the sound of an ear pipe. The gallbladder and the channels of the triple warmer emerge from the ear. The "Copper Man" states: needling the Guanchong point produces blood and drains the Zhigou point. The pulse is floating, large, and string-like; start with a small dose of Chaihu Decoction followed by a larger dose of Chaihu Decoction. This condition indicates an illness involving the greater yang and lesser yang, with the pre-existing condition acting as the host and the later condition as the guest.[29p]
Tinnitus and Deafness

The classics say: Headache and tinnitus arise when the nine orifices are not functioning properly; this is generated by the intestines and stomach. When the stomach qi is deficient, the ears, eyes, mouth, and nose will all suffer. The classics further state: Yang qi, when overworked, expands; if it exhausts in summer, it leads to extreme weakness, resulting in blindness and deafness, as if the body is collapsing. Therefore, the essence of Heaven values clarity and purity, while Yang qi despises overwork. Diseases arising from the spleen and stomach are one such issue.

The pulse is taut, rapid, and deep. When one presses down, if there is a significant change, the symptom of tinnitus and deafness indicates the use of the "Regulate Middle and Nourish Qi Decoction." The classics say: Headache and tinnitus arise when the nine orifices are not functioning properly; this is due to a weak stomach that cannot nourish the Hand-Taiyang Small Intestine and Hand-Yangming Large Intestine, leading to these symptoms. However, it results solely from the weakness of the stomach. Thus, the sages speak broadly of the generation from the intestines and stomach.

Some say: Is there evidence for what you claim regarding the generation from the intestines and stomach? I respond: The classics state that when the spleen is insufficient, it causes the nine orifices to be blocked, suggesting the spleen is a dead yin that receives the Yang qi of the stomach. It is able to elevate the qi of food and fluids to the lungs, filling the skin and dispersing into the four organs. Now, if the spleen cannot receive and transport qi to the organs, this leads to the mentioned symptoms. This is called the spleen deficiency causing the nine orifices to be closed. Although it is said to be a spleen deficiency, it is also caused by the inadequacy of the stomach.[30p]
The ears are associated with the kidneys and serve the function of the lungs.

The ears connect to the upper airflow and are the orifice of the kidneys, serving the function of the lungs. The lungs are said to thrive within the offspring, which is the abode of the kidneys, thus enabling hearing sounds. Therefore, when essence is depleted, deafness occurs. This indicates that clear energy is received from the heavens, while exhaustion of the heart and depletion of the kidneys allow pathogens to enter.

Deafness is primarily attributed to heat. In cases of greater heat in the Shaoyang and Jueyin, one should use remedies like the opening phlegm dispersant, the Wind-Heat Tongsheng Powder, and the Rolling Phlegm Pills. For deafness following a severe illness, one should use the Four Substance Decoction to lower fire.

Deafness caused by Yin deficiency and active fire should also be treated with the Four Substance Decoction.

If deafness is due to stagnation, use the Tongsheng Powder refined with Da Huang wine, then stir-fry with wine three times before adding other herbs to be stir-fried with wine. For deafness, the use of Longhui Pills is essential, along with the Four Substance Decoction to nourish Yin.

For damp phlegm, one may use Shenxiong Pills or Betel Nut Pills.

Tinnitus

Tinnitus caused by alcohol repression requires a large dose of Tongsheng Powder, supplemented with Zhiqiao, Chaihu, Da Huang, Gancao, Nanzheng, Jiegeng, Qingpi, and Jingjie; if it does not resolve, the wonderful Four Substance Decoction should be applied.

For tinnitus, the use of Longhui Pills is essential and should be taken after meals.[31p]
To treat a solidified condition in the body, use betel nut and Shenxiong pills. A roaring sound in the ears indicates a deficiency in Yin or may also suggest a blockage of Qi; this is often due to heat causing the disturbance, leading to ringing in the ears.

For swelling and pain in the ears, a mixture of Qianghuo, Jingjie, and Fangfeng with wine-processed Dahuang and Huangqin, combined with a little musk, should be taken. If there is dampness, use dried alum for blowing.

According to the "Huangdi Acupuncture Classic," if the essence is depleted, it results in deafness. The kidneys are the root of the foot's Lesser Yin channel and store essence. They connect to the ears, which are where the main channels accumulate. When essence and Qi harmonize, the kidneys are robust, allowing one to hear the five tones. However, fatigue can injure Qi and blood, and together with wind and cold, can damage the kidneys, leading to essence depletion and subsequent deafness. The five organs, six viscera, and twelve meridians connect to the ears. When the Yin-Yang energies are disturbed, it leads to a condition known as "Jue Qi" that causes disturbances in the ear channels, resulting in deafness. If the deafness is due to kidney essence depletion, the complexion around the cheeks and cheekbones will appear dark. If the pulse of the Lesser Yang pathway is reversed, leading to deafness, you will observe a bright, shining sensation within the ears. If it’s the Taiyang pathway causing deafness, there will be fullness in the ear; in such cases, treatment with Shujing Powder is appropriate.[32p]
Sudden Deafness

Sudden deafness is caused by a deficiency of kidney qi, which allows wind evil to invade and strike the meridians. It rises through the blood vessels to the ears, where the righteous qi clashes with the evil qi, resulting in sudden deafness. It should be treated with cattail pollen ointment.

Ear Inflammation

The ear is where the meridians converge and is connected to the kidney qi, belonging to the foot's lesser yin channel. If labor exhausts the qi and blood, and the heat qi enters through the deficiency in the meridian, the evil follows the blood and qi to the ear. When heat accumulates, it generates pus, which is termed ear inflammation.

Ear Sores

Ear sores arise because the foot's lesser yin channel connects to the ear. If this channel is deficient, wind and heat can invade, following the pulse into the ear. The clash between qi and blood causes sores to form within the ear.

Treated Successfully by Contemporary Physicians

Tinnitus

Tinnitus is primarily due to insufficient kidney essence and the movement of fire from yin deficiency. In cases of phlegm and fire, the ringing is pronounced; in cases of kidney deficiency, it is faint. Treatment should include kidney tonifying pills, astragalus pills, restorative pills, kidney nourishing and qi promoting decoction, or six-ingredient pill with rehmannia.[33p]
Remarkable Efficacy of Excellent Formulas
[Ming Dynasty - Fang Xian]

On Tinnitus and Deafness

Deafness is associated with the Lesser Yin of the foot; the kidneys reside in the ears. The essence, governed by the kidneys, is essential; when the essence and vitality are harmonized and the kidney energy is sufficient, the ears will naturally be clear. Moreover, the causes of deafness are varied. There are those who suffer from exhaustion of vital energy and blood, where wind becomes combined with heat, leading to the essence’s depletion and resulting in fatigue and deafness; those who suffer from wind-induced deafness; and those whose labor has led to damage and deafness. The twelve meridians connect to the ears, and when these channels intersect adequately, the organ energies may rise in reverse, causing blockage that enters the ears, resulting in a condition known as wind deafness.

The ears are attached to the primary vessels; when the pulse is weak and wind evil invades, the wind enters the ears, obstructing the channel energies, causing wind deafness. Labor exhausts the blood and energies, and unrestrained desires consume the vital essence, leading to weakness and fatigue, producing symptoms of labor-induced deafness. Some individuals are adept at maintaining their health; their energies and blood remain balanced, and without excessive exertion, their condition gradually improves. Others fail to avoid exertion, and damage to their essence and spirit from labor and wind stagnation leads to persistent deafness.

Additionally, there are cases where wind evil comes into contact with the ears, clashing with the energies, resulting in a clamor of sounds, with the eyes possibly seeing flashes as a manifestation of phantom sounds. When there is hot energy invading through a weakness, entering the ears with the pulse, if heat accumulates without dispersing, it leads to a condition termed “ear pus.” Common practitioners often use harsh, drying, and heating medicines to address this issue, but this may frequently result from the deficiency of kidney water and the presence of cold. The heart fire is inherently hot; when deficient, it turns cold; the kidney water is inherently cold; when weakened, it can become hot.[34p]
When kidney qi is insufficient, how can it lead to illness? Therefore, one method involves soaking needle sand in wine for a day until evening, then taking out the needle sand and holding the wine in the mouth. Use a piece of magnet wrapped in cotton to block the ears, placing it on the left ear for the left side and the right ear for the right side, to guide the qi and promote its flow.

Someone asked, since deafness is caused by heat, how can taking hot substances like dry scorpion, ginger, prepared aconite, or strong wine sometimes lead to improvement? The answer is that these are used to open the source and relieve the obstruction in the ears.

In treating deafness, one must adapt to the appropriate methods. If the heat signs have diminished but the deafness persists, one should use spicy and warming medicinals to disperse it, stopping immediately when improvement occurs and avoiding prolonged use, lest excessive heat lead to other illnesses. If deafness is accompanied by heat signs, it is advisable to use methods to dispel wind and clear heat, thus resolving the blockage and achieving recovery.

However, if deafness is extremely severe, it can be very difficult to treat. Care must be taken not to attack it too aggressively, as it may harm the vital qi. If it is not the appropriate condition, do not take the medicine. The same principle applies to diet; moderation is crucial, as excess can damage the vital qi. Once the illness is resolved, discontinue the medicine. To seek health is merely to avoid harm.

Furthermore, it is said that the elderly tend to be weak and often sick, experiencing symptoms like dizziness, tinnitus, or respiratory difficulties. These are all signs of excess yang and deficiency of yin. The common saying is that the old and weak are deficient, cold, and without heat. Even if heat signs are present, it is often said that insufficient kidney water cannot withstand excessive fire, implying that deficient kidney water leads to coldness. This reflects the misunderstanding prevalent in society.[35p]
Medical Treatise: Ear Disease

The "Inner Classic" states: The kidneys are the organs of strength, and skills emanate from them. It also says: The ears are the external manifestation of the kidneys. Furthermore, it says: The kidneys are connected to the ears. It is well known that the kidneys are a water organ. The heavens produce water, thus at the beginning of life, there are two kidneys formed, with one hidden yin within, and there is also the fire of vitality residing in the gate of life. This vital fire often carries the momentum of the sovereign fire, thereby overpowering what cannot be defeated, as the text states, "one water cannot overcome two fires." This condition may arise from excessive desires, overexertion, or after middle age, following a severe illness; when kidney water depletes, the yin fire flares up, resulting in constant ear itch and ringing. Sometimes it resembles the noise of cicadas, at other times like the sound of bells and drums, which can be extremely annoying. If untreated, it may gradually lead to senility, which is indeed lamentable! The treatment method should focus on draining the fire from the south and replenishing the water from the north; there is no one who is not unsettled by this. Qian Zhongyang said: "The kidneys have nourishing but no draining; is this not profound?"[36p]
Diagnosis Method

The left pulse is strong, indicating fire rising; when both pulses are strong, it suggests phasic fire. Such a person is likely to experience nocturnal emissions and may have tinnitus or hearing loss.

Key Points for Diagnosis and Treatment
(Ming Dynasty, Dai Sigong)

Ear Diseases

The ears are the orifices of the kidneys, and all ear diseases pertain to the kidneys. Due to kidney deficiency, there may be sounds like waves or cicadas in the ears, or rapid deafness. One should use Minglong San, or chew beeswax with wine, and consume yellow wax porridge. If kidney deficiency persists and there are continuous sounds like waves or cicadas, leading to impaired hearing, it is advised to tonify the kidneys with Zhangqi and take Zhengyuan Decoction, along with Heixidan and An Shen Wan. If ear pus arises due to wind and toxins, it is called “Teng Ear.”

Medical Summary
(Ming Dynasty, Lou Ying)

Eyes and Ears Receive Yang Qi for Clarity

The human ears and eyes, like the essence of the moon, can only gain brightness with sunlight. Similarly, the ears and eyes must receive yang energy to achieve clarity. Therefore, when the yin blood of the ears and eyes is deficient, they cannot absorb yang energy, resulting in impaired sight and hearing. When the yang energy of the ears and eyes is deficient, the yin blood cannot sustain its function, leading to a loss of clarity as well. Thus, the clarity of the ears and eyes necessitates the mutual support of blood and qi to enable vision and hearing.[37p]
Ear Diseases are Related to the Kidney and Liver

The ear, in terms of orifices, is associated with the kidney’s water. The classic text states: the kidney governs the ears; within the organs, it is the kidney, and in terms of orifices, it is the ear. It also states: the kidney's energy connects to the ear. When the kidney is harmonious, the ear is able to hear the five tones. Furthermore, it is said that if essence is depleted, deafness occurs. Therefore, Luo Qianfu suggested that with essence depletion leading to deafness, the complexion should be dark around the cheekbones. The classic text states: if the liver is deficient, the eyes cannot see and the ears cannot hear, leading to great fear. Treatment uses the Four Substance Decoction, adding additional ingredients such as Fangfeng, Qianghuo, Chaihu, Changpu, and Fushen in equal portions, boiled and taken for over twenty doses. Then use a remedy of Duorenjiang and Xie powder. If the liver is deficient, ginger is used to replenish it.

There are Four Causes of Deafness

  1. The first is: dampness evil injures the kidneys leading to deafness in the Sanjiao. The classic text states, "the greater yin resides in the springs; dampness overcomes it, leading to the people's illness of deafness where the sound is unclear." Treatment for this is with bitter and warming remedies.

  2. The second is: dryness evil injures the liver leading to deafness. The classic text states, "the yearly metal is excessive; as dry air circulates, the liver wood is affected, leading to the people's illness of deafness where nothing can be heard."

  3. The third is: fire evil injures the lungs leading to deafness. The classic text states, "the yearly fire is excessive; as summer heat circulates, the lung metal is affected, leading to the people's illness of deafness."

  4. The fourth is: wind heat disturbance above leads to deafness. The classic text states, "the lesser yang governs heavenly affairs; wind and heat intermix, causing chaos and boiling clouds, leading to the people's illness of deafness and disturbance; with the arrival of the three energies, summer heat leads to inner heat deafness, which is treated with cold remedies."[38p]
    Tinnitus and Ear Pain are Related to Wind and Heat

The classic text states: The liver governs heaven; the wind moves through the void, causing clouds and objects to sway, leading to eye movements and ear ringing. When the three energies align, the heavens distribute their governance, and the energy rises at the right time, resulting in the people suffering from ear ringing. It also states that when the liver's energy is strong, ear ringing and dizziness occur. Furthermore, the lesser yang's influence causes ear ringing and is treated with warming herbs.

Ear Pain is Related to Heat

The classic text states: When the lesser yang's energy is strong, ear pain arises, which should be treated with warming herbs.

The Distinction Between New and Old Deafness

Deafness must be categorized as new or old. New deafness is often due to heat, arising from an abundance of lesser yang and yangming fire, so it is advisable to disperse wind-heat and administer remedies to resolve phlegm obstructing the channels. Old deafness is often due to deficiency, as the kidney is commonly weak, so it is advisable to nourish and simultaneously open the channels. The pulse patterns indicate that the kidney is predominant; a slow, thin pulse indicates deficiency, a floating pulse indicates heat, a large floating pulse indicates wind, a deep and thick pulse indicates air, and a rapid, solid pulse indicates heat.[39p]
There are three types of deafness.

When rich flavors stimulate the stomach fire, both ears become deaf; when anger stirs the gall bladder fire, the left ear becomes deaf; when lust stimulates the heart fire, the right ear becomes deaf. Among these, anger is the most prevalent.

Deafness can vary due to phlegm fire, wind, dampness, Qi blockage, exhaustion, or loss of essence and Qi.

Phlegm fire: Caused by rich foods heating the stomach, resulting in ringing in the ears; it can progress to Qi blockage and gradual deafness with fiery tears. For this, use Er Chen Tang with Huangbo, Mutong, Bianxu, and Qumai; if caused by alcohol, employ Tongsheng San with Nnoxing, Zhikua, and Dahuang, or consider Guo Phlegm Wan.

Wind deafness: Elicited by wind evils entering the ear, leading to itchiness, often accompanied by headaches due to wind heat, or can be due to stagnation. Use Fangfeng Tongsheng San, first stew Dahuang with wine, then stir-fry with other herbs in wine three times before decoction. For those with wind blockage affecting clarity, use Qingshen San; for those with wind deficiency, consider Paifeng Tang, Guixiang Yin, or Qiuzhi San.

Damp deafness: Resulting from exposure to rain, which leads to internal swelling and pain; use Liangge San with Qianghuo and Fangfeng, prepared with wine; or apply Wuling San with Chenpi, Zhikua, Zisuan, and Shengjiang. For damp phlegm, use Shenqiung Wan. If there is blockage accompanied by dizziness, the treatment for those with excess from anger is Danggui Longhui Wan; for those weak from worry, use Miaoxiang San; for stagnation due to sadness, consider Liuqi Yinzi with Changpu; and for those with excess above and deficiency below, utilize Mijuan Jiangqi Tang with Changpu.[40p]
Deafness from Deficiency: This occurs after prolonged diarrhea or severe illness, where wind pathogens enter the ear through a weakened state and clash with the vital energy, resulting in a noisy ringing. If there are also symptoms of visual disturbances, such as seeing dark flowers, the prescription may include Siwu Decoction with additions of Rhizoma Acori and Polygala, or Shenqi Pill with additions of magnetite, medicated leaven, Cuscuta seed, and Huangbo. For those with Yang deficiency, Bamei Pill, Yishen Powder, or Magnetite Decoction are recommended.

Deafness from Overuse: Characterized by a dull and heavy sensation, along with emaciation and weakness. This results from overexertion depleting vital energy, requiring Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction with Rhizoma Acori; if there is heat, add Rhizoma Zhi, Huangbo, and Poria; in cases of sexual exhaustion, Ren Shen Yang Rong Decoction with Rhizoma Zhi, Huangbo or Bugu Zhi Pill should be used. If there is prolonged deafness due to a weak kidney and absolute qi deficiency leading to complete inability to hear, treatment is difficult.

Main Points: Harmonizing qi and opening the auditory orifices are essential. The kidney's water pathways influence the ears’ ability to hear, as water generates from metal. The lungs control the qi, which flows throughout the body to the ears, thereby enabling sound perception. In all cases of deafness, one should first harmonize qi and alleviate stagnation, intermittently using magnetism and Yang Kidney Pill to open the orifices. Generally, deafness is due to phlegm and fire stagnation; unless magnetism weighs down and disperses the phlegm and fire, with the use of spices like cinnamon and pepper, along with Rhizoma Acori, it remains difficult to clear the old phlegm and heat. However, this approach can also be overpowering, so after treatment, using Tong Sheng Powder for harmonization is advisable.[41p]
Tinnitus

Tinnitus is the gradual onset of deafness; when the energy is blocked, there is often no sound leading to deafness. For tinnitus caused by wind-heat, one can use Detox Decoction with raw Rehmannia and Anemarrhena, or Tong Sheng Powder. If phlegm-heat is severe, use Dang Gui Long Hui Pills. If accompanied by dampness, use Shen Xiong Pills or Qing Mu Xiang Pills. For slight ringing due to kidney deficiency, use Zi Shen Pills; for qi deficiency, take Si Jun Zi Decoction; for blood deficiency, Si Wu Decoction; for yin deficiency, use Hu Qian Pills.

Ear Inflammation, Purulent Ear, Ear Pain

Ear inflammation and pain are typically due to wind-heat. The ear contains oil and liquid, which can become bound by wind-heat into a mass, causing ringing or deafness. For treatment, externally apply a mixture of pig fat, earthworm, and pot coal, forming them into balls with ginger juice, the size of jujube pits, wrapped in cotton and inserted into the ear to moisten and remove impurities. In severe cases, take Chai Hu Cong Er Decoction internally. For purulent ear infection with wind-heat obstructing upward, externally use five parts dried alum, two parts each of burnt tangerine peel and rouge, and half a part of musk, ground into powder to blow into the ear; for severe cases, take Xi Jiao Yin Zi internally. For pain that feels like insects crawling, it is due to excessive wind; if it is dry pain, this may indicate wind-heat or deficiency fire; if there is blood and water, it indicates wind-dampness. Externally, use burnt snake skin powder, or blowing in dried alum powder can also work; for severe pain, use Wu Yu, Aconite tips, and rhubarb to grind into powder to apply to the feet; in severe cases, take Dong Yuan Shu Nian Zi Decoction internally.[42p]
Discussion on Ear Diseases

The ear is the orifice of the kidneys, and its diseases can be classified into several types: there are those who are deaf due to wind obstruction, those who suffer deafness from laborious exertion, those who are deaf from heat and pathogens entering the ear, and those who have purulent ear conditions resulting from wind and heat obstructing bodily fluids, causing sudden deafness and a buzzing sensation. Additionally, there are people who are deaf in the left ear, those deaf in the right ear, and those deaf in both ears; it is essential to distinguish these for treatment.

Treatment Methods
For those deaf in the left ear, excessive anger stirs the lesser yang gallbladder fire, so treatment begins on the left side using Longhui Pills. For those deaf in the right ear, excessive desire stimulates the greater yang bladder fire, thus treatment begins on the right side using Liuwei Dihuang Pills. For those deaf in both ears, excessive consumption of rich foods and alcohol incites the stomach fire of the foot yangming, so treatment is approached from the center using Tongsheng Powder and Guo Phlegm Pills. Notably, left ear deafness is more common among women due to their propensity for anger, while right ear deafness is more prevalent in men due to excessive desire. Those deaf in both ears often come from affluent households because of their indulgence in rich flavors. Overall, among these three, anger is the most common cause of deafness.

When phlegm and fire rise, causing both ears to buzz and gradually lead to deafness, it is advisable to modify the Longhui Pills, along with needles, sand wine, and Tongyong Liqi Decoction and FucHong Decoction.[43p]
Return of Health from Ten Thousand Diseases
[Ming Dynasty - Gong Tingxian]

Deafness and Pulse Diagnosis

For left ear deafness, use Longdan Decoction. For right ear deafness, use Nourishing Yin and Rehmannia Decoction. For deafness in both ears, use Jiu Zhi Tong Sheng San and Qing Cong Hua Tan Wan. For kidney deficiency causing deafness, use Six-Flavor Rehmannia Pills, adding Yuan Zhi, Chao Pu, Huang Bo, and Zhi Mu, stir-fried with saltwater, which also treats deafness caused by Yin deficiency and rising fire. In cases of ear disease with kidney deficiency, the pulse is slow and wet. A floating pulse indicates wind, while a surging pulse suggests fire excess. A sinking and thick pulse indicates phlegm obstruction with heat accumulation. In cases of prolonged deafness, the focus is on kidney responsibility. In acute conditions, a floating and surging pulse should feel the same at both wrists. If both wrists pulse strongly, it indicates Yin fire surging upwards.[44p]
Ear Disorders

Medical Standards Synopsis Six Essentials
(Ming Dynasty, Zhang Sanxi)
General Discourse on Tinnitus and Hearing Loss

Tinnitus and hearing loss must be classified by their onset—whether sudden or chronic, and their nature—whether due to deficiency or excess. Sudden deafness or ringing resulting from intense anger or drunkenness is attributed to phlegm and fire, distinguishable by their severity.

For middle-aged individuals or those with a deficiency, or for those who experience this after illness, all are deemed deficient. It is vital to differentiate between qi (vital energy) and blood in relation to the ear.

Ancient prescriptions include using mouse bile, cat urine, and vine flowers to make drops for the ear; skinning almonds, adding salt, steaming, and then applying oil drops; skinning castor seeds, mixing with a jujube, mashing, and wrapping with cotton to seal the ear; hollowing garlic cloves, filling them with fried and cooked medicinal beans, and wrapping with cotton to seal; mixing realgar and medicinal beans with scallion juice and rolling in paper to seal the ear; and using Sichuan pepper, medicinal beans, calamus, and resin, formed into a tube to seal the ear.

Moreover, incorporating xixin (wild ginger), puhuang (cattail pollen), curcuma, and almonds into a pellet to block the ear is also noted. When adding dragon's brain and peppercorn, these are primarily warming and dispersing methods, intended for promoting and unblocking the orifices, which may yield results if the condition arises abruptly.

However, if the original qi is insufficient, and kidney yin is depleted, with deficient fire carrying phlegm rising and blocking the orifices leading to deafness and ringing, then even repeated applications or insertions will be powerless—as futile as ants shaking a rock.[45p]
It is necessary to greatly replenish Qi and blood, nourish Yin and control fire, so that the great Qi rises and fills the head, ensuring that the nine orifices are unobstructed and hearing issues are eliminated. The "Nanjing" states: "Kidney Qi is connected to the ears; when the ears are harmonious, one can discern the five tones." If the Kidney Qi does not flow to the ears, then the ears are disharmonious and one becomes deaf. If it can connect upward to the ears, then the ears will be harmonious and hearing will be acute. Observing this, the distinction between deficiency and excess is evident.

In cases of Kidney deficiency, when there is a constant sound of water or cicadas in the ears, hindering hearing, one should replenish Qi and nourish the Kidneys with Zhengyuan Decoction and Black Lead Pill, intermittently taking Anshen Pills. If there is heat, Longchi San should be used. For wind in the Kidneys causing ear ringing and a drum-like sound at night, with aching in the limbs, and a strange itching sensation in the ears as if blown by wind, Huangqi Pills are advisable.

The ears are known to belong to the Kidneys. However, the Shaoyang Gallbladder meridian connects to the ears; thus, when cold evil transmits to the Shaoyang, ear deafness and lateral pain occur. If women experience prolonged depression, lumps may form in front of and behind the ears; if they are overtaken by sudden anger, they may suddenly go deaf—this is due to fire invading the primary channels, not solely the Kidneys.

For ear deafness and ringing, there may be phlegm and heat, Qi deficiency, Yin deficiency, or Liver fire. In youth, it is mostly due to phlegm and heat, while in middle age, it is primarily Yin deficiency.[46p]
Yin Deficiency and Hearing Loss

A pulse of two inches, either the left pulse is strong or the left pulse is weak and large, with a thin body and dark complexion. If accompanied by dry mouth, dry intestines, and tinnitus or deafness, the palms and soles will be warm, indicating yin deficiency. Six-Flavor Pill and Kanli Pill are indicated for treatment.

Qi Obstruction and Hearing Loss

Hearing loss that arises from irritation requires methods to unblock and disperse. One should take equal amounts of fennel, costus root, ginseng, Corydalis yanhusuo, dried tangerine peel, and sweet flag, each a penny; and five parts each of Notopterygium, silkworm, Sichuan lovage, and cicada slough, with two pennies of pangolin and half a penny of licorice ground into fine powder. Each dose is three pennies, taken with warm wine.

Liver Fire and Hearing Loss[47p]
The left pulse is tense, rapid, and belongs to liver fire. Such a person is likely to be easily angered, and may experience tinnitus or deafness. It is advisable to calm the liver and reduce wood; take Longdan Porridge to purge the liver. If it does not improve, use Longhui Pills.
Phlegm-fire deafness

The right pulse is slippery and rapid, indicating phlegm-fire stagnating in the upper jiao. It is advisable to clear phlegm and reduce fire, using Erchen Decoction, Jiuqin Lian, Chaihu, Zhuhuang, or Bamboo Juice and Ginger Juice with Rolling Phlegm Pills.
Qi deficiency deafness
