Chai Hu Zhi Zi San treats wind-heat in the three jiaos and the foot Shaoyang channel, presenting symptoms like itching in the ears, sores or discharge with pain, chest or breast pain, or alternating chills and fever. The ingredients include: Chai Hu, Zhi Zi (stir-fried), Mu Dan Pi, each 1 qian; Fu Ling, Shao Yao, Dang Gui, Niu Bang Zi (stir-fried), each 7 fen; and Gan Cao 5 fen. These are simmered in water for administration. It is also known as Zhi Zi Qing Gan San.

Dang Gui Chuan Xiong San treats blood deficiency sores in the hand and foot Shaoyang channels; symptoms may include itching and pain in the ears due to wind-heat, sores and discharge; or unclear head and eyes, chills and fever, reduced appetite; or irregular menstruation in women, insufficient chest and diaphragmatic function, and abdominal or flank distension and pain. The ingredients include: Dang Gui, Chuan Xiong, Chai Hu, Bai Zhu, Bai Shao, each 1 qian; Shan Zhi (stir-fried), 1 qian 2 fen; Mu Dan Pi and Bai Fu Ling, each 8 fen; Man Jing Zi and Gan Cao, each 5 fen. These are simmered in water for administration. If liver Qi is unbalanced, add Di Gu Pi. For excessive liver Qi, add Chai Hu and Huang Qin. If Qi and blood are deficient, add Ren Shen, Huang Qi, Dang Gui, and Di Huang. For spleen deficiency, with reduced appetite, add Ling and Zhu. If there is spleen deficiency with insufficient chest and diaphragmatic function, add Ren Shen and Huang Qi. For phlegm stagnation resulting in chest and diaphragmatic blockage, add Zhu and Ban. If liver Qi is not smooth causing chest and diaphragmatic obstruction, or if there is distension and pain in the lower abdomen, add Qing Pi. For liver blood deficiency causing chest and diaphragmatic obstruction, or distension and pain in the lower abdomen occurring intermittently, add Shu Di. For cold due to liver blood deficiency with pain in the lower abdomen, add Rou Gui. If there is fever in the late afternoon, add Dang Gui and Di Huang.[116p]
Jiawei Dihuang Pill treats liver and kidney yin deficiency causing sores, or itchiness and pain in the ear with discharge; or blurriness in the eyes, phlegm, breathlessness, or thirst with fever, and red, painful urination. Take one hundred pills with warm water on an empty stomach. If there are side effects, use the modified Eight Flavor Pill.

Liyansan treats insects entering the ear. The ingredients are: Sichuan lovage, white angelica, night-shining sand (stir-fried), pig's tooth soapberry (roasted), and southern star (prepared), each 7.5 grams; hundred parts, white clove, and rhizoma phragmitis, each 4 grams; black cocoon 5 grams; arsenic prepared separately; and pipul, each 2 grams; sea gold silk 2.5 grams. Grind all into a fine powder, mix thoroughly, and if needed, adjust color with lead cinnabar in a porcelain container.

If an insect enters the ear, take a small amount of vinegar to mix, dip a fine feather in the medicine, place it in the ear, and blow lightly to allow the medicinal vapor to circulate, prompting immediate expulsion. Do not use too much medicine, as too much will turn the insect into liquid and not come out. For scorpion stings, first apply a small amount of vinegar to the sting site and then sprinkle some medicine to rub in until warm, which will have an immediate effect.[117p]
Jia Jian Long Hui Wan
Treats phlegm and fire rising, causing tinnitus.

  • 0.5 grams of musk
  • 1 tael each of herbal dragon gall, angelica root (washed with wine), fried gardenia fruit, and yellow qin
  • 2.5 qian of wood fragrance
  • 0.5 tael each of rhubarb (steamed with wine), green indigo, and bupleurum
  • 0.3 tael each of aloe vera and southern stargrass
    Grind the above into powder, mix with fermented sorghum dough to form pills the size of a mung bean. Take twenty pills with ginger soup three times a day. After seven days, use needle sand wine to facilitate the movement of qi. One version does not include southern stargrass.

Needle Sand Wine
Treats the conditions mentioned above.

  • 1 tael of needle sand
  • 0.1 tael of ground pangolin
    Mix the pangolin with needle sand, let it rest for one day and night, then remove the pangolin. Soak the needle sand in a bowl of wine for three to four days, hold the wine in the mouth, and externally use a piece of magnet wrapped in cotton to block the ear. Avoid anger.

Tong Ming Li Qi Decoction
Treats deficiency fire and phlegm-qi accumulation in the ear, which may be blocked or ringing, with excessive phlegm fire causing fullness and restlessness.

  • 1.5 qian of fritillaria
  • 1.25 qian of aged tangerine peel
  • Yellow liand and yellow qin, soak in wine, then mix with fried pig bile juice, 0.75 qian
  • Fried berberine wine

  • 1 qian of original ginseng washed with wine

  • 0.5 qian each of raw dry rehmannia and ginger juice fried
  • 0.25 qian of betel nut
  • 0.4 qian of chuanxiong
  • 0.25 qian of wood fragrance
  • 0.2 qian of licorice
    Grind the above ingredients, prepare one dose, add three slices of ginger, and decoct in water. Add five spoonfuls of bamboo juice before taking.[118p]
    Fu Cong Decoction [Danxi]
    Treats phlegm fire surging upwards, causing tinnitus and deafness.
    Ingredients: Banxia, red poria, aged tangerine peel, licorice, beebalm, mu tong, qu mai, and salt-fried Huangbo, each 3 grams. Grind together to make a paste, add three slices of ginger, and boil in water.

Da Bu Pill [From "Yi Jian"]
Treats tinnitus with a desire for deafness.
Ingredients: Eight taels of Huangbo, grated, mixed with human milk, dried, and then stir-fried in salt water until brown. Mash into a fine powder, form into water pills the size of a wax gourd, and take one hundred pills with hollow salt water. Also known as Du Sheng Wan.

Zi Shen Tong Qi Decoction [From "Hui Chun", same below]
Treats kidney deficiency with tinnitus and a desire for deafness.

Long Dan Decoction
Treats anger stirring gallbladder fire, causing left ear deafness.
Ingredients: Huanglian and Huangqin stir-fried, zhizi stir-fried, dang gui, aged tangerine peel, niu dan, and south star anise, each 3 grams; long dan and xiang fu, each 2.5 grams; yuanshen 1.5 grams; qing dai and mu xiang, each 1.5 grams; dry ginger stir-fried black, 1 gram. Grind together to make a paste, add three slices of ginger, boil in water, and add 1.5 grams of Yuan Ming powder before consumption.[119p]
Zi Yin Di Huang Decoction: Treats sexual desire-driven fire, leading to deafness in the right ear. Qing Cong Hua Tan Pill: Treats ear deafness and ringing caused by excessive eating and anger stirring liver and stomach fire, leading to blockage and inability to hear sounds. Grind together, first use paper to wipe away pus and water, then dip cotton in the medicine and place in the ear, changing daily.[120p]

Chai Hu Clear Liver Powder
Used to treat wind-heat sores or ulcers in the liver, gallbladder, and triple burner, or when anger and aversion to cold cause fever, or when sores or toxins are located around both ears, or on the outer body down to the feet, or in the chest, lower abdomen, or inner thighs down to the feet.

Musk Finger Citron Powder
Used to treat five types of ear bleeding.[123p]
A small amount of musk, human bone calcined to preserve its potency, is toxic when heated. Grind it into a fine powder, and use a small amount to blow into the ear until dry. For treating smallpox in children where facial marks appear, mix a character with wine and take it.

Mercury ointment treats moon-eclipsed sores located on both ears and around the openings, following the waxing and waning of the moon for healing. Use 2.5 taels of mercury, five taels each of ground hu powder, pine resin, and yellow lily, with the hairs removed. First, boil pig fat until boiling, then add the pine resin and other powders along with mercury, mixing evenly and storing in a ceramic container. First cleanse the sores with saltwater, then apply three to five times a day.

Hu powder powder treats moon-eclipsed sores.

Slightly roasted hu powder, white alum, calcined realgar, purified yellow lily, and light powder each 2 taels; one tael of rouge and a small amount of musk, ground into a powder. First, wash with warm rice water and salt, then blend with the medicine; if the sores are dry, apply with sesame oil.

Huangqi mixed internal powder treats swollen and painful ears.

Chuanxiong, angelica, and Huangqi each 2 taels; white attractor, honeysuckle, tianhuafen, and soap pod spines each 1 tael; licorice and poria cocos each 0.5 tael. Boil with three bowls of water until reduced to two bowls, and take before meals.

Xianfang Huoming Decoction treats the previous symptoms.

Roasted pangolin shell powder, white angelica, protective wind, red peony, flower pollen, angelica root, frankincense, myrrh, chuan bei mu, soap pod thorn, and licorice each 1 tael; honeysuckle and dried tangerine peel each 3 taels. Boil in a bowl of wine until boiling and take warm.[124p]
Tori Disinfection Powder - Treats the previous symptoms.
Add or subtract ginseng according to the symptoms, stir-fried astragalus with saltwater, one qian each of angelica, chuanxiong, fried white peony, fried white atractylodes, and fried white poria; seven fen each of honeysuckle and white vector; five fen each of licorice and forsythia. Decoction and take.

Ginseng and Astragalus Inner Disinfection Powder - Treats the previous symptoms.

Ten Dissemination Powder - Treats the previous symptoms.
Ginseng, honey-prepared astragalus, and angelica, each two qian; chuanxiong, fried licorice, platycodon, white vector, fangfeng, and magnolia bark, each one qian; three fen of cinnamon. Grind into a fine powder; take one or two qian with wood incense decoction.

Coptis Disinfection Powder - Treats the previous symptoms.
Fried coptis and qinghao, each one fen; yellow sheng, huangbo, platycodon, dried root, and fangji, each five fen; four fen each of angelica tail, forsythia, fangfeng, duhuo, and fried anemarrhena; three fen each of ginseng and licorice; two fen each of astragalus, red sandalwood, dried orange peel, and water plantain. Grind into coarse powder and decoct for use.[125p]
Yuan Zhi Wine can dispel various toxins.
Yuan Zhi is not limited by quantity; soak and wash it with rice water, pound out the heart, and fine grind it into powder. Each dose is three qian, mixed with a cup of good wine. After a little while, let it settle, drink the clear liquid, and apply the sediment to the affected area.

This treats ear hemorrhoids, ear fungi, ear carbuncles, ear dampness, and ear ulcers.

Pain-Relieving and Qi-Regulating Decoction

Refined Stone Powder
Treats ear stones that are hard as stone and unchanged in color.
Burned Deer Antler Ash: eight liang; White Licorice: three liang; Coarse Yellow Stone: two jin.
Mix these with five sheng of good vinegar, first burn the stones until red, then quench in vinegar, burn again and quench until the vinegar is used up. Grind to powder and mix with the remaining vinegar to form a paste for application, which will soften the hardened area. Apply it to the roasted area as well.

Collection of Medical Works from Ancient and Modern Times, Volume 137

Ear Section[126p]
Single Prescriptions

Swelling and inflammation of the ear with bleeding: Take the droppings of willow insects, mix with water, extract the clear juice, and add a small amount of powdered alum, then drip it in. [“Zhou Hou”]

Ear discharge with fluid: Mix equal parts of bamboo wormwood, wolf tooth, and white vine into a powder, and apply frequently. [“Sheng Hui”]

Painful ear pus due to water entering the ear: Use a mix of one penny of worm-eaten arrow shaft powder and greasy powder, and five cents of musk, grind together into a powder, use cotton to pack tightly, insert the medicine into the ear, and plug with cotton to secure. Let any foul material flow out. In severe cases, it will heal after three times. [“Pu Ji Fang,” same applies below]

Ear discharge with pus: Grind the droppings of jujube borers, and blow in with a little musk.

Centipede in the ear: Cover the ear with roasted lard, and it will come out by itself.

Various insects in the ear: Use one penny of pepper powder, half a cup of vinegar, soak for a long time, and drip in small amounts to expel. [“Xu Qian Jin Fang”]

Elderly person with deafness: Take a pair of pig kidneys, remove the membrane, slice, and combine with two cups of glutinous rice, two green onions, seven garlic chives, two parts ginseng, and one part fangfeng, grind together, and cook into porridge for consumption. [“Feng Qin Yang Lao Fang”]

Gecko in the ear: Grind moist growth insect into a paste, apply to the ear side, and it will come out; or twist it into a roll on paper, and place it in the ear to also extract. [“Wei Sheng Bao Jian”]

Deafness from kidney deficiency: Use a pair of deer kidneys, remove the fatty membrane, slice, and with fermented soy sauce, mix with two cups of glutinous rice to cook porridge, which can also be made into soup. [“Sheng Hui Fang”][127p]
Deafness: For deafness, take half a spoonful of goose oil, a small quantity of magnetite, and a little musk. Mix thoroughly, form into a pellet using cotton, and place it in the ear. Hold a small piece of raw iron in the mouth, using three to five pieces for effectiveness.

Ear with pus from malnutrition: Mix swan oil with powdered aconite, add a small amount of dragon brain, and apply to produce immediate effect. If unavailable, use goose oil instead.

Ear with pus: Blow powder of centipede into the ear.

Kidney deficiency deafness: Take one black rooster, clean it, and cook it in three liters of unslaked wine. Eat three to five while hot for effect.

Ear with discharge: Burn and grind a small quantity of aged orange peel with a little musk into a powder, and use it daily.

Ear with discharge: Burn and grind the peel of green tangerines and stuff it into the ear with cotton.

Ear with fluid or pus and blood: Take seven young leaves from a citrus tree, crush them with a few drops of water to extract the juice, and apply it for healing.

Ear with discharge: Grind walnut kernels, mix with dog's gall juice, and form into a cotton plug to insert.

Ear injury with discharge: Use a pestle to extract oil from walnuts and apply inside.

Ear with pus: Blow powdered betel nut into the ear.

Ear with pus: Grind camphor wood and insert using a cotton rod.[128p]

  • For sudden ear swelling: Mix five parts of bitter neem fruit, crush it, and wrap it in cotton to stuff the ear; change it frequently.

  • For ear pain with pus: Finely chop the root of willow, cook it, and seal it; replace when dry.

  • For sudden deafness: Take one kernel of physostigma, wrap it in wax, make a small hole with a needle for ventilation, and stuff it in for effect.

  • For tinnitus and deafness lasting one to twenty years: Use twenty jin of zhe root and five jin of sweet flag, boil with one stone of water to extract five dou of juice, heat twenty jin of iron until red, soak in five dou of water to extract clear water, combine one stone and five dou of water, use two shi of rice and two dou of flour, ferment as when brewing wine, pulverize three jin of true magnet and steep in the wine for three nights, drink day and night until drunk and sleep; stop when hearing human voices.

  • For ear discharge with pus: Burn half a liang of cicada molt to preserve its potency, grind five fen of musk into powder, wrap in cotton to stuff it in to expel bad substances.

  • For sudden deafness: Place earthworms in salt and onions, moisten with water for immediate effect.

  • For ear discharge with pus: Grind equal parts of earth dragon, lampblack, and fresh pig fat, mix with onion juice, roll into a stick, and stuff it in. The "Shenghui Fang" suggests blowing powdered earth dragon into the ear.

  • For impacted earwax that won't come out: Place white earthworms in a green onion tube, let it dissolve into liquid, drip it into the ear until full; after a few applications, it can be easily removed.[129p]

  • If a centipede enters the ear: use earthworm powder, mix it with scallions, and it will transform into water; this also makes the centipede turn to water. 【From "Shenghui Fang"】

  • For deafness and blocked ears: use equal parts of earthworm and chuanxiong, ground into powder. Take two qian each time and swallow with Mai Men Dong decoction. After taking, lower your head and sleep; one dose at night for three nights will be effective. 【From "Shengji Zonglu"】

  • For ear sores caused by lunar eclipse: take rabbit droppings at night, place them in a toad's belly, burn them, and apply the ash. 【From "Zhouhou Fang"】

  • For ringing in the ears and ear discharge: use burnt cotton to pack the ear after mixing it with ashes. 【From "Shenghui Fang"】

  • For ear discharge of pus: use a dog’s gallbladder and one qian of dry alum, mix well, and pack it into the ear with cotton. Three to four applications will heal it. One recipe adds pig lard for mixing. 【From "Qixiao Liangfang"】

  • For deafness and blockage with snail mucilage: use one liang of snails, and two qian and five fen each of stone gall and chongru powder as fine powder. Store in a porcelain box, fire-roast until red, grind into powder, then mix with a small amount of oil and drop into the ear; all will be cured. 【From "Shenghui Fang"】

  • If a centipede enters the ear: decayed snail placed near the ear will cause it to come out. 【From "Ruizhutang Fang"】

  • If there is something in the ear that cannot be removed: use a three-inch long bowstring, fray one end, coat it with glue, and gently introduce it into the ear to pull out the obstruction. 【From "Shenghui Fang"】[130p]
    For prolonged deafness: Take three taels of pine resin and one tael of croton seeds, mix and pound into pills, wrap in thin cotton and insert; administer twice daily.

For deafness: Use half a handful of mouse fat, one qian of blue salt, and one earthworm; mix and dissolve together, then soak cotton and apply drops into the ear, sealing it.

For deafness: Use half a sheng of white chicken dung, one sheng of black beans, and two sheng of ash-free wine; heat and mix, then take it to induce sweating. Do not be surprised if the ears swell like drums.

For ear sores: Grind white chicken dung and apply it.

For persistent ear problems with pus and blood from worms day and night: Use three jin of carp intestines, one carp brain, and one whole carp washed and cut, along with one sheng of fried black sesame seeds ground finely; mix all into a container, warm slightly over low heat, wrap in cloth and apply to the ear. When the white worms have all emerged, it will heal. Be cautious of drafts and cold.

For deafness: Use carps' gallbladder juice and drip into the ear.

For deafness: Take the raw brain of a carp and wrap in cotton to block the ear. Another method: Use a bamboo tube to hold the raw carp brain, steam it near the cooking rice until it melts, and then pour into the ear.

For sudden deafness: Use two taels of carp brain fat, three he of glutinous rice, and cook with salt to make porridge to eat.[131p]
For chronic deafness: Take mouse bile, have the patient lie on their side, and drip the bile into the ear until it is finished. After a moment, the bile will flow out from the other ear. Initially, this may worsen the deafness, but after half a day, it will improve. This remedy can treat deafness that has lasted for thirty years. However, mouse bile is hard to obtain; once the mouse dies, the bile quickly dissipates. It may be available around the third day of the third lunar month.

Mouse brain marrow, wrapped in cotton and stuffed in the ear, can also treat deafness.

For ear deafness: Use snake gall to plug the ear; it is remarkably effective.

If there is sudden severe pain in the ear, as if there are insects running inside, or if there is bloody fluid flowing out, causing unbearable pain: Burn shed snake skin into powder and blow it into the ear; it will cure immediately.

For ear pain with pus: Take bitter almonds, boil them until they turn red into powder, mix with the saliva of green onions, form into pills, and wrap in cotton to place in the ear, changing three times a day.

For deafness: Grind mustard seeds into powder, mix with human milk to form pills, wrap in cotton and place in the ear, changing twice a day.

For deafness: Drip male cat urine into the ear, left ear with left urine, right ear with right urine. If the cat does not urinate, rub its teeth with ginger to induce urination.

For deafness due to air blockage: Grind genuine musk into powder, blow it into the ear using a green onion stalk, then plug the ear with green onion; it will restore hearing.

For long-term deafness: Mix donkey fat with mature Sichuan pepper, pound it together, wrap in cotton, and plug the ear; it is extraordinarily effective. One variation uses ginger instead of Sichuan pepper.[132p]
Hearing loss: Take one seed of dadou (castor bean) and remove the heart and skin, take one wingless cicada and remove its wings and legs; combine these two and grind them into a paste, wrap in cotton and plug into the ear. Replace as necessary; this method is very effective.

If the ear suddenly swells and oozes pus, along with both ears and treating hearing loss with pus: Take desiccated alum and grind it finely, then blow a little into the ear with a reed tube three to four times a day; or wrap cotton around a jujube pit and plug the ear. One method involves mixing with table salt and then adding alum powder, which is particularly effective. Another method involves first wrapping a piece of paper to absorb the ear's secretions, then putting in alum powder, and finally adding salt powder; enduring this for a long time will result in healing, usually without needing to repeat. Another method does not use salt. Additionally, take the root of shanglu (a plant) and clean it, then cut it with a bamboo knife to the size of a jujube pit; plug it into the ear, which also treats internal sores.

For pus to flow from the ear: Fire-calcined white alum should be ground into powder, mix in a small amount of musk, and wrap in cotton to plug the ear. [From "Bencao"]

If pus flows from the ear, swelling and pain have subsided but pus continues to flow, use this method mixed with divine efficacy. Use three qian of calcined white alum, two qian of dried carmine, and 1.5 fen of musk, grinding them into an extremely fine powder, stored in an airtight container. When needed, first make a ball of new cotton, squeeze out the pus from the ear, then use damp cotton to roll the medicine and insert it deep into the ear, doing this two to three times daily will lead to self-healing. [From "Wai Ke Zheng Zong"]

Another method: finely grind magnetic stone and wrap it to insert into the deaf ear, separately using iron sand powder to insert into the hearing ear; this will naturally allow hearing. [From "Zhi Zhi"][133p]
Deafness: Take one inch of acorus, one seed of croton, crush together into a pill, wrap in cotton and plug the ear, change daily.
Earache: Use the natural juice of acorus to irrigate the ear, highly effective.
Deafness, tinnitus: Take fresh prepared rehmannia ash, warm and wrap it to plug the ear, change several times until healed.
Water in the ear: Use natural mint juice to drop in for immediate effect.
Deafness, tinnitus: Take forty-nine peeled castor beans, ten jujube flesh, mix with human milk and crush until uniform, shape into pieces the size of jujube pits, wrap in cotton and plug in the ear, warmth should be felt, change daily. This is called jujube seed pill.
Long-term deafness: Half an inch of gan sui, wrap in cotton and plug in the ear, half an inch of licorice, chew in the mouth until passage is clear. Another method: Blow powdered gan sui into the left ear, powdered licorice into the right ear; this is also effective. Two people should each administer to the respective ears for effect. Acupuncture

The "Suwen" states: When deafness occurs due to a sudden disturbance, the eyes and ears become unclear; use sky windows.

Pathogenic factors on the Yangming meridian of the hand can cause ear deafness, making one unable to hear sounds. Insert needles into the fingernail of the index finger and the thumb, removing the needle as one would with chive leaves, puncturing each once for effectiveness; if there is no immediate effect, insert into the fingernail of the middle finger where it meets the flesh for immediate effect. If there is still no response, do not insert again. If wind is generated in the ear, use the same method of puncturing several times, moving from left to right, then right to left. To alleviate ear deafness through the Yangming meridian, if not resolved, puncture the pathway leading to the front of the ear.

Pathogenic factors affecting the Taiyin and Shaoyin of the hands and feet are related to the Yangming meridian; these five meridians all converge in the ear, with connections to the left angle. When all five meridians become blocked, it causes the body’s qi to stir, leaving one in a state of unawareness, resembling a corpse, or some may say, a state of corpse-like stupor. Puncture the inner side of the toenail of the big toe, leaving it punctured as one would with chive leaves; then puncture the center of the foot; next, puncture the toenail of the middle toe, each once; then puncture the inner side of the thumb, as one would with chive leaves; finally, puncture the heart point of the Shaoyin where the sharp bone ends, each once, for immediate effect; if still unresolved, blow into both ears with a bamboo tube, take one inch of hair from the left angle, burn it, and drink a cup of fine wine. If one cannot drink, administer it forcefully for immediate effect."[143p]
Individuals with liver disease, when deficient, cannot see with their eyes or hear with their ears, are often fearful, as if someone is about to catch them. One should treat using the channels of Jueyin and Shaoyang; if the qi is rebellious, symptoms include headaches, deafness, and facial swelling, and one should draw blood.

For those with lung disease, if deficient, there is shortness of breath, an inability to exhale fully, deafness, and a dry throat; one should treat using the channels of Taiyin, on the foot of Shaoyang externally, and Jueyin internally to draw blood.

The "Lingshu" states: When there is ringing in the ears, what qi causes this? Qibo replied: The ears are where the ancestral vessels gather. Therefore, when the stomach is empty, the ancestral vessels become deficient, and if deficient, they flow downwards, leading to a deficiency in the vessels, hence the ringing in the ears. Nourish both the host and the guest; it is at the junction of the thumb's nail and flesh.

Furthermore, it is said: When there is insufficient upward qi, the ears suffer from distressing ringing; nourish it at the location below the outer ankle.[144p]
It is also said: When the marrow sea is deficient, the brain turns and the ears ring. Carefully observe the flow and regulate the deficiency and excess. It is also said: The hand's sun channel affects the shoulder, hip, and neck, causing pain and ringing in the ears. If the pain twists the muscles, treatment lies in the moxibustion and needling based on knowledge and pain. Diseases arising from the hand's sun meridian manifest as deafness, yellowing of the eyes, and swollen cheeks. Adjust for excessive heat or cold that is deficient and sinking. In cases of febrile illness with heaviness, bone pain, deafness, and desire for sleep, target the bones with the fourth needle, using fifty-nine punctures. Bone ailments that prevent eating, with enamel-like ears deepening to green, seek the bones in the kidneys, but refrain from drawing from the earth; scholars correspond to the spleen. The "Jia Yi Classic" states: Hand sun counterflow causes deafness; treat the root of the issue. If there is dryness in the ears, do not apply moxibustion.

If there is pus in the ear canal, do not apply moxibustion.

For neck pain and inability to turn, with unclear vision, the wind pool controls it. Severe shoulder and back pain leading to sudden deafness, with obstructed hearing and vision, the heavenly window regulates it. In cases of fever where sweat does not emerge, resulting in ringing in the ears and deafness, the yang valley controls it.

Deafness and ringing in the ears are managed by the lower orifice.

In sudden illness with headache and body heat, muscle twitching leads to deafness; the bound bone controls it. For a headache with pain behind the ears, the completed bone regulates it.[145p]
The condition of deafness often involves complaints of tinnitus, yet in reality, it is a form of deafness governed by the Pathway of the Fen. Tinnitus is linked to the arterial movement in front of the ear.

For deafness without pain, focus on the Lesser Yang at the foot; for deafness with pain, the Yangming at the hand is indicated. Tinnitus is governed by points like Baihui, Yanyan, Lusi, Tiankuang, Daling, Pianli, Qianggu, and Houxi. Ear pain with deafness is related to Shangguan, with the admonition to not pierce deeply.

For deafness and tinnitus, the points Xiaguan alongside Yangxi, Guanchong, Yumen, and Yanggu should be considered. If deafness and tinnitus coincide with pain in the head or jaw, the point Ermen is significant.

Should there be heaviness in the head and pain in the jaw, drawing to the ear, with sounds like chirping or buzzing, the Hejiao point is of relevance.

In cases of deafness with sounds resembling wind or frenzy in the ear, the Tinghui point should be applied. If there is an emptiness in hearing that feels as if nothing is heard, leading to a continuous noise akin to cicadas, the Tingong point should be noted, with the emphasis on the lower jaw much like a broken sound piercing through this condition.

For deafness without hearing, focus on the Tianshu point. If there is clamor without discernible hearing, Tiansheng is the place of focus.

When wind arises within the ear, leading to both tinnitus and deafness during non-hearing times, focus on the Shangyang point. For conditions of deafness and blockage within the ear, the Hegu point is to be utilized.[146p]
Deafness with pain in both temples is managed by the point Zhongzhu.

When hearing is muddled and there is no sound perception, the point Waiguan is used.

For sudden deafness, the points Sidu are applicable.

The "Thousand Gold Recipe" states: for ear pain or deafness with a buzzing sound, use the points Shangguan, Xiaguang, Sibai, Baihui, Luxi, Yifeng, Ermen, Hanyan, Tiankuang, Yangxi, Guanchong, Yumen, and Zhongzhu. Deafness with a buzzing sound like that of cicadas can be addressed with points Tianrong, Tinghui, and Tinggong.

For sudden deafness, use Tianyou and Sidu.

For pain in front of the ear, the point Shaoshang is indicated.

For ear pain, use Quqi.

When hearing is muddled and there is total deafness, apply the points Waiguan and Huizong. For tinnitus, the points Qiangu and Houxi should be considered. Additionally, apply Pieli and Daling.

For ear pain radiating to the ear, with a buzzing sound where there is no hearing, consider Wangu, Yanggu, Jianzheng, Qiaoyin, and Xiaxi.

For wind-related deafness buzzing, utilize Shangyang, inserting a needle to a depth of one portion, leaving one breath, and moxibustion three times. Alternate sides as if eating.

The "Medical Guidelines" states: for deafness and tinnitus, with either pain or itchiness, or a feeling of fullness, use the point Tinghui. The acupoint is located in the depression at the front of the ear lobe, apply eight draining and suction techniques.

For the point Yifeng, insert the needle half an inch deep with seven draining and suction techniques; you may also use Hegu or Sanli.

Another method: Yifeng is located in the depression before the ear, pressing it helps draw the sensation inward. Instruct the patient to first hold twenty-four coins in their mouth while lying on their side and use needles to pierce, asking the patient to keep their mouth closed and shake their head, releasing the anger through the ear.

For the points Tinghui, Zhongzhu, and Linqi, use the same needle technique as previously mentioned.[147p]
Ear buzzing and ringing can be treated at the points of Shen Shu and Tai Xi.

For sudden deafness, use a moxa stick on the ear with the herb Atractylodes, cut into seven parts—one end flat and the other pointed. Insert the pointed end into the ear and moxa the flat end for seven times; if the condition is severe, do it for fourteen times. When you feel heat inside the ear, it is effective. The "Complete Book of Jing Yue" says that for wind-related deafness, moxa seven times at the point Shang Xing to allow the qi to flow into the ear, which can lead to recovery.

For ear deafness and pain, use moxa seven times. For deafness, moxa at He Gu point seven times; or at Wai Guan, Ting Gong, Shen Shu, and Pian Li. The "Treasure Mirror of Eastern Medicine" states that for ear buzzing, select points such as Ye Men, Er Men, Zhong Zhu, Shang Guan, Wan Gu, Lin Qi, Yang Gu, Qian Gu, Hou Xi, Yang Xi, Pian Li, He Gu, Da Ling, Tai Xi, and Jin Men.

For ear deafness, use points Zhong Zhu, Wai Guan, He Liao, Ting Hui, Ting Gong, He Gu, Shang Yang, and Zhong Chong.

Regarding guidance, the "Book of Nurturing Life" suggests massaging the ear rim without limitation on the number of times. This is to strengthen kidney qi and prevent deafness. To maintain hearing strength, one should always feel full.[148p]
The "Secrets of Preserving Life" states: Engage in deep breathing to block distractions, clench your teeth, press your nostrils tightly with two fingers, and open your eyes wide, allowing your breath to connect your ears and clear your passages. You may feel a buzzing sound inside; practice this for two or three days until your passages are open. Regularly listen with both ears in order to return to a quiet state. You can also hold your breath, closing your mouth and nostrils, and imagine the breath coming out of your ears, then draw your focus back; your ears will naturally become sharp. For ear ailments, rub the palms of your hands together fifty times, applying heat to the ear to open it, and continue this rubbing and observing for six repetitions. Symptoms will improve, and with ongoing practice, results will be evident. Use mental focus to disperse heat; for men, gather it back between the kidneys, and for women, draw it back beneath the breasts or to the ears. You can press the ear area, and if you hear a buzzing, swallow saliva to calm the energy within.

For ear pain, visualize fire burning the kidneys, and cleanse it with kidney water; press the ear several times to stimulate sound, swallow saliva, and breathe down until you feel at ease. For ear problems, use your mind to scatter the heat, drawing it back and storing it within the kidneys, or if something is lodged in the ear, mentally remove it.

The "Complete Works of Jing Yue" states: If the ear passages are damaged, blocked, or injured, leading to sudden deafness or persistent buzzing, gently press your fingertip against the ear opening, pushing and releasing in rhythm. This should be done several times; the air will flow, and when it does, the passage will naturally open. If these conditions occur, failing to take timely action may result in gradual blockage, ultimately leading to complete ear closure.[149p]
Medical Case

According to "Danqian Xulu," Wang Wanli suffered from ear pain at that time. Wei Wenjing Gong advised him to take a potion made of blue salt and deer antler decoction. He mentioned that this medicine was not for consumption due to deficiency, and asked why one shouldn’t consider the "I Ching," where "Kan" corresponds to the ear. The Kan water resides in the kidney, opening the orifice at the ear. In terms of emotion, it relates to fear; fear injures the kidney, hence the ear pain. The movement of Qi Yang is always evident, while the flow of Blood Yin is often hidden. Blood, like water between heaven and earth, leads to Kan being the hexagram of blood, indicating disease is already documented in the classics. In the end, after taking it, he was cured.

Shen Cunzhong stated: When I was an inspection official in Hebei, I suffered from red eyes for more than forty days. The black part of my eyes was darkened and developed sores, causing pain day and night. Various treatments failed to heal me. The gentleman Qiu Ge, upon seeing my condition, asked if my ears had been itchy. If they were itchy, it would indicate kidney wind. There is a formula called Si Sheng San to treat kidney wind, and it typically takes two or three doses to heal, known locally as the "sacred powder." I transmitted the formula and took it as directed: one dose at noon and one before sleeping. My eyes began to hurt greatly, and I could only sleep at the second watch; upon waking, my eyes had slightly improved and were no longer painful. After taking three or four more doses, I returned to normal health. At that time, Scholar Sun Hefu was in charge and, upon hearing me, was overjoyed, saying: "I now know how to treat the eyes myself." Earlier, suffering from a long-term eye ailment, I once heard Lu Jifu, a political advisor, say that after a prolonged eye illness, he healed himself by taking the Tou Bing Dan (Icing Pill). Following his recommendation, I tried taking two or three dozen doses, and my eyes were cured, leading me to realize that the Tou Bing Dan also treats kidney wind in the ears.[150p]
"The Sacred Benefit" states: If someone experiences itchy ears that occur daily, it is a cause for concern. Poking at it until it bleeds may bring slight relief. This indicates kidney deficiency, leading to a floating toxin ascending, which is not easily treated by conventional methods. It is advisable to take 'Ice-Clear Pill' and avoid alcohol and damp vegetables, chicken, and pork for at least a month for the best results; if one cannot abstain, treatment will be ineffective.

"Notes from Ink Visitors": Creatures that can enter the ear are not just earwigs; such as wall lice, fireflies, head-banging bugs, and soap pods can also cause harm. I have a distant relative who had a bug enter his ear, convinced he would surely die, and thus squandered his family's resources over several years, leading to his financial ruin. When the bug came out, he discovered it was a head-banging bug. Another individual had an earwig enter his ear; in a peak moment of distress, he unconsciously banged his head against a pillar, causing him to bleed without realizing it, claiming the itch was unbearable. Earwigs often consume marrow and can breed in the winter. For any bug in the ear, the best remedy is to flush it out with raw oil.[151p]
The "Medical Cases of Xue Ji" states: The late emperor once had a bug crawl into his ear while sleeping, causing intense pain. He took ginger and rubbed it on a cat's nose, and its urine came out. He then dripped that urine into his ear, and the bug came out, resulting in a cure. Zhang Jin, a hundred households, said to me: When there is a sore in the ear that causes periodic severe pain, one may feel as though they want to die, yet when the pain subsides, it feels the same as before, and upon diagnosing the pulse, all seems calm. I deduced it was not a sore. Suddenly, the pain arose, and I suspected a bug had entered the ear. I instructed him to turn back, quickly took the cat's urine and dripped it into the ear, which caused a stinky bug to come out, and thereafter there was no more pain. Some use hemp oil to drip in, but the bug dies and is hard to remove. Others use fried sesame to treat it, and the bug also comes out, but neither method is as quick as using cat urine.

Wen Xuan’s Yao Haishan had a red swollen ear root with cold and hot pains, indicating wind heat from the sanjiao. However, with pre-existing deficiency of the central qi, I added Gardenia fruit, fried Scutellaria, and Burdock seed to tonify the middle and benefit qi, and he recovered.

A scholar, due to anger, experienced pain in the ear accompanied by fluid discharge. Using wind-dispersing medicine caused muscle spasms and pain, and limbs felt constrained. This was a result of liver fire injuring the blood. I used the Six Flavor Pill, and after several doses, he recovered.[152p]
A scholar, Mao Shifeng, at the age of twenty, experienced water discharge or pain in his ear for over a year. His pulse was rapid and strong, especially at the left wrist. This was attributed to the deficiency heat of the liver and kidney. A dose of the modified Eight-Flavor Pill cured him.

A man would feel itching or experience a discharge in his ear every time he entered a room. He often probed with a silver hairpin, finding great pleasure in the coolness. This was attributed to heat in the kidney channel. He was cured with the modified Eight-Flavor Pill.

A woman, after a fit of anger, experienced pus discharge from both ears and pain at the temples during her menstrual cycle. Pressing on it would slightly relieve the pain, but anger caused swelling and pain in the chest, sides, and breasts, along with alternating chills and fever, frequent urination, and abdominal distension. These symptoms were due to liver fire and blood deficiency. She was first treated with two doses of the Gardenia Liver-Clearing Powder, followed by several doses of the modified Free and Easy Wanderer Powder, which alleviated all symptoms; she then fully recovered with the Middle-Away Qi-Boosting Decoction enhanced with five-flavor ingredients.

A woman, after her menstrual cycle, became ill with chills and fever due to anger and labor, experiencing ear pain. I considered her blood deficiency as related to her menstrual cycle and treated her with the Eight-Treasure Decoction supplemented with Bupleurum; the anger indicated liver fire, treated with the modified Free and Easy Wanderer Powder; the labor indicated qi injury, treated with the Middle-Away Qi-Boosting Decoction enhanced with gardenia, resulting in her recovery.

A woman experienced ear pain, swelling, and alternating chills and fever. Her complexion was pale yellow, but it would turn red during her menstrual cycle. I attributed this to anger damaging the liver and stagnation injuring the spleen, treating her with the modified Return to Spleen Decoction and the modified Free and Easy Wanderer Powder, leading to her recovery.[153p]
A woman had swelling and pain in her ear, experiencing chills and fever, with a bitter taste in her mouth, ear discharge, and a hot sensation radiating to her neck, along with reduced appetite and thought. This indicated severe liver fire damaging the spleen. I prescribed Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with added San Zhi (gardenia fruit) and Mu Dan Pi (peony root), which brought slight improvement. Then I used Jia Wei Xiao Yao San and Ba Zhen Tang, with additional Chai Hu, San Zhi, and Mu Dan Pi, to regulate and nourish the liver and spleen, resulting in full recovery.

A widow had pain in her ear, or exterior ear pain, or a hard lump on the side of her neck, with internal heat characterized by afternoon fevers, irregular menstruation, little saliva and phlegm, and hindered chest. I believed that repressed anger harmed her liver and spleen. In the morning, I prescribed Gui Pi Tang to relieve spleen depression and enhance spleen energy; in the evening, I used Jia Wei Xiao Yao San to clear liver fire and nourish liver blood, leading to her recovery.

Taiqing Wei Zhuang Qu, in the winter of the year Gui Mao, had ear pain, with the left pulse being large and slippery. I said: this is due to kidney essence depletion, unable to nourish the liver wood, so it is necessary to moisten the source of transformation. He did not believe this and continued to mix other tonifying medicines. I told his son-in-law Lu Shi Ruo that if Zhuang Qu could not nourish kidney essence, he would surely not survive until spring. The following year, on the 18th day of late spring, he sought treatment again. He was lethargic and unable to speak, with pus already forming in the audiophore, and also had reduced bowel movements. Only then did he believe my words. He sought treatment but was unable to. I used Liu Wei Wan, which is a remedy, and his penis retracted, his urination decreased from ten to six or seven times, and his mind quickly regained clarity. I said: if we let the pus out, we might extend a few days for the continuation of descendants; otherwise, if the pus comes from the ear, death is imminent. Some said that if we don’t let it out, he might survive, so I excused myself and left. The next day, pus indeed came from his ear, and by the 21st day of the Jiwei Fire day, he passed away.[154p]
In the winter of the Gui-Mao year, the assistant Jiang Shichuan had a rapid pulse at the right wrist and phlegm, with the sensation of sores in the mouth. I said: This is fire from the stomach transferring to the lungs; one should eat lightly and be careful in daily activities to combat it. In the autumn of the Jia-Chen year, his pulse was strong and rapid but lacked strength. I said: This indicates that the lung's metal is unable to nourish the kidney's water—rootless fire is rising. It is advisable to calm and nurture, supporting the source of transformation to treat it. He mentioned that his throat and ears were occasionally dry and painful, and his limbs would sometimes feel hot—indeed, it was rootless fire, without a doubt leading to his demise. Later, when meeting Liu Guxia, he confirmed: Jiang's condition was as I had assessed, and I urged him to go see him. The throat was indeed swollen and ulcerated, and the pulse was increasingly vigorous. Mistakenly thinking it to be a toxic sore, he administered bitter cold remedies. He passed away on the twenty-eighth day of late spring; it was the medicine that hastened his death; otherwise, he could have lasted until mid-summer.[155p]
A man had swelling and pain behind his ear, with the flesh color unchanged and a weak, rapid pulse. I prescribed Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with the addition of Chuanxiong, Angelica, and Platycodon for four doses, and the swelling subsided. Then I used Tori Xiaodu San for several doses; the pulse became slippery and rapid, indicating that pus had formed. It was advisable to use acupuncture, but he was afraid and unwilling. Only after the pain became severe did I insert the needle, yielding about a bowl of pus, and after using the Tori medicine for over two months, he began to recover.

For sores that do not break, one must provoke them to burst; if they do not form pus, one must nourish to encourage formation, preventing internal damage. Pus that has formed must be punctured promptly; recovery can occur within a few days. Patients often fear the pain of needles and hesitate to use them, also worrying about injuring healthy flesh, yet they do not realize that although sores may occur in thin flesh, once pus has formed, the swelling can be over an inch high, and the skin of the sore is thick. The needle should not go deeper than two tenths of an inch. If the swelling is on the back, it can rise three to four inches, with needle insertion limited to about an inch, especially since the flesh at the affected site is already damaged—what pain is there to fear? What harm to anticipate?

Cowardly individuals, particularly those with bone abscesses, often wait for pus to drain naturally, leading to major rupture, and many cannot contain their vital energy and blood, ultimately leading to death.[156p]
The "Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment" states: When a person is exhausted and experiences a swelling under the ears, chills, fever, headache, and thirst, with a large and soft pulse on the right, they should take the "Buzhong Yiqi Decoction." If they mistakenly take medicines that disperse, it may lead to vomiting, which confirms the diagnosis. I used "Liu Junzi Decoction" and then administered "Buzhong Yiqi Decoction," resulting in recovery. Generally, internal injuries to the nourishments of the body lead to the failure to defend against wind and cold; without the energy to nourish the skin, one cannot withstand such external influences. If the stomach's qi sinks, yang fire will surge upwards, causing wheezing, fever, and a large pulse. This is insufficient evidence for an external condition; treating it as an external pathogen may lead to harmful consequences of deficiency. Dongyuan states: A large pulse on the right indicates internal injury, while a large pulse on the left indicates external invasion, and this distinction should be made accordingly.[157p]
A woman had swelling and pain under her ear, with chills and fever. After four doses of Jingfang Baidu San, the symptoms retreated; then, with several doses of Sanfu Guojian Tang, the swelling reduced significantly. Finally, after four doses of Shenxiao Guo Luo San, she was well.

Another person had wind-heat in the liver channel, with swelling and pain under the ear, and a rapid floating pulse. It was treated with Bohe Dan, which resolved the issue.

A woman, due to anger, experienced pain and swelling under her ear. She was treated with Jingfang Baidu San, adding Lianqiao and Huangqin. After four doses, she recovered. I had previously treated a similar case where the swelling did not subside after ten days; using tonics for qi and blood along with Yan Zhi wine was effective. If there was no pus, it would resolve on its own; if there was pus, it would rupture.

A woman, due to anger, had painful swelling under her ear, headaches, and chills and fever. After administering Jingfang Baidu San with added Huangqin, her superficial symptoms retreated. However, she experienced reduced appetite and intermittent fever. Dongyuan noted that, despite having false heat, one should not attack too vigorously; as the heat recedes, the cold may arise. Hence, I used Xiao Chai Hu Tang with a mixture of Digupi, Xiong, Gui, Ling, Su, and Chenpi, which cured her after more than ten doses. The following spring, she had recurring firm swelling that did not rupture. I prescribed Ba Zhen Tang with additional Xiangfu, Chaihu, Digupi, and Jiegeng, continuing for six or seven doses. As a result of prolonged treatment, she became increasingly weakened and was also administered Liuqi Yin. She then experienced night sweats, fever, dry mouth, and reduced appetite. By autumn, she sought further consultation, presenting severe qi and blood deficiency. I declined to treat her, and she eventually passed away.[158p]
When a person becomes angry, they may experience swelling under the ear or pain in the side. Using Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with added Qingpi, Honghua, and Taoren can bring recovery.

A woman who is quick to anger often has swelling and pain under the ear, with alternating chills and fever, and tightness in the liver pulse. Administering Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with added Qingpi, Burdock Seed, Jingjue, and Fangfeng can alleviate the chills and fever. Additionally, several doses of Xiao Chai Hu Decoction combined with Siwu Decoction will reduce the swelling. Her father wanted to eliminate the root of the illness, and I advised that the liver is responsible for storing blood internally and nourishing the tendons externally. If anger causes qi to rebel, it can damage the liver, which governs the tendons, resulting in swelling and knots. She needs to manage herself to avoid further issues. Otherwise, the rebelling liver will fail to store blood, and blood deficiency makes recovery difficult. Later, she did not take precautions and developed three lumps; despite frequent treatment, they persisted and eventually led to her demise.

A man who had traveled far, experiencing fatigue and fever, with a weak and large pulse and swelling under the ear, suffered from labor-induced damage. He should have taken the "Buzhong Yiqi Decoction" to naturally reverse the heat and reduce swelling. However, he did not listen and instead took antipyretic medicines and strong dispersants, ultimately leading to vomiting, diarrhea, and death from not eating. Fatigue depletes qi, and when qi is weak, fire becomes strong, leading to fatigue and heat; this is an injury to the original qi. Danxi stated that one should replenish the physical qi and regulate the meridians, allowing wounds to resolve on their own; one should not sweat or purge. If one does not carefully assess the pulse and symptoms related to meridian illnesses but hastily uses harsh remedies, the risk of danger is significant.[159p]
At the hairline behind the ear, there was a swelling without a head, flesh-colored with slight pain upon pressure. I believed it to be phlegm causing a soft pulse appearing intermittently. The classics state that a pulse that is rapid yet does not appear intermittently indicates a sore rather than phlegm. Zhongjing says that a weak pulse denotes a deficiency in both blood and qi, and that there is insufficient essence and form. It further states that a sinking, slow, and weak pulse should all be treated with tonics. Thus, I used ginseng, astragalus, angelica, poria, Sichuan lovage, and fried licorice to tonify, adding a little honeysuckle, white peony, and platycodon to dispel toxins. They disagreed, suggesting internal consumption to clear heat and resolve phlegm, and applying cooling medicines externally; however, they felt chilled to the bone while the affected area was very hot, leading to increasing heaviness in the head and decreasing appetite. Upon further consultation, I prescribed Four Gentlemen Decoction with added aromatic cardamom and toasted dried ginger over several doses, gradually increasing food intake. When pus formed, it was needled, and then I applied Ten Full Great Tonic Decoction minus cassia, and moxibustion with fermented soybean cake, eventually leading to recovery after over a month.

Luo Zongbo experienced painful swelling behind the ear with a rapid pulse. I treated him with Xiao Chai Hu Decoction enhanced with platycodon, burdock seeds, and honeysuckle over four doses, leading to recovery.

Another individual had a toxic infection over an inch behind the ear, with a solid pulse indicating a need for internal Huanglian Decoction; however, due to the severe winter, he refused cold medicines and ultimately did not recover.

A third individual had a toxic infection at the edge of the hair approximately an inch behind the ear, diagnosed as a sharp sore, causing burning pain and alternating chills and fevers, along with restlessness and a preference for coolness. This was due to heat stagnating in the gallbladder channel. Initially, I prescribed Shenxian Huo Ming Decoction, which reduced the intensity significantly by two-thirds. However, given the mid-winter conditions, he was wary of using cooling agents and instead took ten doses of the tonifying medicine, leading to a worsening condition; pus erupted in the ear, the throat became swollen and obstructed, and he was unable to swallow the medicine, resulting in death.[160p]
The "Meaningful Grasses" states: Wang Yu originally experienced a感证 (a sensation or feeling) many years ago, and due to poor treatment, all the bodily fluids were consumed by evil heat. After more than ten years, the heat had not dissipated, and the right ear canal was often blocked. This summer, he fell ill again, enduring for more than fifty days with swelling of the face and feet, unable to sleep peacefully. Air from the ear was in contact with the outside, indicating that new heat had combined with old heat, making the situation more troublesome, therefore difficult to eliminate from the body. The physicians did not observe the binding and entangled nature of his condition, and their treatment was ineffective. As autumn deepened, with the cold of metal and water, the illness started to recede. However, while mild symptoms may retreat, severe ones cannot quickly dissipate. The swelling of the face and feet indicates that the lung's metal energy is obstructed by heat, losing its ability to descend and clear. Inability to sleep peacefully indicates that the fluids in the stomach are dry, unable to nourish the spirit. The gas striking out from the ear suggests a long-blocked canal, with air coming without sensation. Now, with the body weak and emaciated, there is no obstruction, and the gas reverses and surges upwards, making him aware of it. Although the external illness may have improved, internal adjustments through diet and medicine still occupy half of the condition. Especially focusing on two matters, the general principle is that those who become ill must understand the methods for post-illness recovery. It is necessary to realize that after falling ill, the body's vital energy has already weakened, and the evil heat within has not cleared. Thus, to restore the deficiency, the heat cannot be eliminated; and to clear the heat, the deficiency cannot be sustained. Therefore, if one aims for half to tonify deficiency and half to clear heat, it ultimately leads to confusion, lacking clear understanding. However, apart from tonifying deficiency and clearing heat, there is no other method, and one must carefully discern this. There are two methods of tonifying deficiency: one is to tonify the spleen, and the other is to tonify the stomach.[161p]
After the weakness of the spleen and qi following malaria or dysentery, if digestion is impeded, it is advisable to tonify the spleen; after an illness like typhoid, when the stomach's fluids have been depleted for a long time and new fluids have not yet been generated, it is necessary to tonify the stomach. The differences between these two cases are as vast as the sky and the earth. There are also two methods to clear heat: in the initial stages of illness, the heat is classified as excess heat, and it is appropriate to use bitter and cold herbs to clear it; however, after a severe illness, the heat becomes deficiency heat, so sweet and cold herbs should be used to clear it. Again, the distinctions between these two are as vast as the sky and the earth. The body's vital essence resides entirely in the stomach; if the fluids are insufficient, it indicates deficiency. Generating fluids indicates tonification, so remedies that generate fluids are combined with sweet and cold herbs that drain heat, which treats the deficiency heat following an illness. Herbs such as Ophiopogon root, Rehmannia root, Moutan bark, ginseng, pear juice, and bamboo sap are all appropriate for this purpose. Zhang Zhongjing frequently used Tianshui powder to clear deficiency heat, specifically selecting talc and licorice, which embodies the principle of one sweet and one cold.[162p]
If we use herbs like Shen, Qi, Ling, and Bai Zhu, which are meant to tonify the spleen as supplements, don’t we risk supplementing while concurrently aggravating external heat? When it comes to dietary supplements, we should focus on their essence rather than their flavor. For instance, the essence of the five grains nourishes the body, while the essence of the five vegetables enhances it. After each meal, one would feel refreshed, and the accumulated internal heat can gradually be expelled through the pores—how delightful! Many do not understand this principle; they rush to use rich and sweet flavors for supplementation. Although one may appear robust and vibrant in the moment, they fail to realize that the oily and greasy elements obstruct the meridians, preventing external heat from being released. Over time, this solidifies the internal constitution, with no prospect of release. The ancients recognized this and preferred to consume plain vegetables, knowing it would temporarily weaken the body, making it easier for pathogenic factors to exit—that should be regarded as valuable wisdom. In the case of edema linked to the spleen, using Ling and Bai Zhu is appropriate; for insomnia due to heart issues, one would use Suan Zao Ren and Fu Shen. Ultimately, the aim of tonifying deficiencies while clearing heat has not been well understood, hence the detailed discussion.[163p]
