For earwax, ear ringing, and deafness due to internal stagnant blood, Chai Hu Cong Er Tang should be used. Other symptoms like ear pain, itching, swelling, and cracking should reference the discussions by Xue Shi in conjunction with these treatments.[58p]

　　　　　耳疮

　　罗谦甫曰：耳内生疮者，为足少阴，是肾之经也。其气通于耳，其经虚，风热乘之，随脉入于耳与气相搏，故令耳门生疮也。曾青散主之，黄连散亦可，内服鼠粘子汤。
　　　　　脓耳

　　耳脓即聤耳，用红绵散、麝香散；内服柴胡聪耳汤、通气散。如壮盛之人，积热上攻，脓水不瘥，红绵散、麝香散不宜用，收敛太过也。宜三黄散效。
　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】

　　　　　论耳

　　耳属足少阴肾经。
　　 【《中藏经》曰：肾者精神之舍，性命之根，外通于耳。《素问》曰：肾在窍为耳，肾和则耳能闻五音矣。又曰：肾者主为外，使之远听，视耳好恶以知其性，故耳好前居牙车者，肾端正。注：牙车即颊车穴也，在耳下曲颔端陷中。耳偏高者肾偏倾，耳高者肾高，耳后陷者肾下，耳坚者肾坚，耳薄不坚者肾脆。《元珠》曰：耳薄而黑或白者，肾败也。】　　又属手少阴心经。[59p]

Ear Sores

Luo Qianfu said: Sores inside the ear are related to the Foot Shaoyin (Kidney) channel. Its energy communicates with the ear; if this channel is deficient, wind and heat can invade it, following the pulse into the ear and clashing with the qi, causing sores at the ear gate. The formula Zeng Qing San is used for treatment, and Huang Lian San can also be applicable, along with the internal administration of Shu Nian Zi Decoction.

Purulent Ear (Otitis)

Pus in the ear is known as "rong ear." Use Hong Mian San and She Xiang San; for internal use, prescribe Chai Hu Cong Er Decoction and Tong Qi San. In cases of vigorous individuals where accumulated heat attacks upward, and pus does not heal, it is inappropriate to use Hong Mian San and She Xiang San, as they may overly astringe. Three Huang San is recommended in this scenario.

Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment [Ming Dynasty - Wang Kengtang]

Discussion on the Ear

The ear belongs to the Foot Shaoyin Kidney channel. The "Zhong Zang Jing" states: The kidney is the dwelling of the spirit, the root of life, and externally connects to the ear. The "Suwen" states: The kidney opens in the ear; when the kidney is harmonious, it can perceive the five sounds. It further states: The kidney governs external hearing, perceiving the ear's preferences to infer its nature. Thus, if the ear appears to sit forward towards the teeth, the kidney is upright. Note: The "tooth car" refers to the Jia Che acupoint, located in the groove under the jaw beneath the ear. If one ear is higher, the kidney on that side is tilted; if the ear is high, the kidney is high; if the ear has a depression, the kidney is low; if the ear is firm, the kidney is firm; if the ear is thin and not firm, the kidney is fragile. The "Yuan Zhu" states: If the ear is thin and black or white, the kidney is failing. Additionally, it is also associated with the Hand Shaoyin Heart channel.[59p]

　　 【《素问》曰：南方赤色，入通于心，开窍于耳。又曰：手少阴之络，会于耳中。】　　又属手太阴肺经。
　　 【李东垣曰：耳本主肾而复能听声者，声为金，是耳中有肺，水土生于申也。王太仆曰：手太阴肺之脉，其络会于耳中。肺虚则少气，不能报息，是以耳聋也。】　　又属足厥阴肝经。
　　 【《素问》曰：肝病气逆，则耳聋不聪。朱丹溪曰：耳聋属热，少阳厥阴热多。】　　又属手足少阳三焦胆、手太阳小肠经之会。　　 【《灵枢》曰：少阳根于窍阴，结于窻笼，窻笼者其中也。《素问》曰：一阳独啸少阳厥也，其终者耳聋。啸，耳中鸣如啸声也。胆及三焦脉皆入于耳，故气逆上则耳中鸣。又曰：少阳主胆，其脉循胁络于耳，故伤寒三日，少阳受之，则胸胁痛而耳聋；九日少阳病衰，耳聋微闻也。又《灵枢》曰：手太阳所生病者，耳聋目黄。】　　又属手足阳明大肠胃经。[60p]

The "Suwen" states: The south is red, which connects to the heart and opens the orifices to the ears. It also mentions that the channels of the hand's shaoyin converge in the ears. Additionally, it relates to the hand taiyin lung meridian.

Li Dongyuan said: The ears are fundamentally governed by the kidneys, yet they are able to hear sounds because sound corresponds to metal, indicative of the presence of lung within the ears, since water and earth originate from the shen. Wang Taifu noted that the channels of the hand taiyin lung converge in the ears. When the lungs are deficient, there is insufficient qi, leading to an inability to respond to sounds, hence the condition of deafness. This also pertains to the foot jueyin liver meridian.

The "Suwen" states: In cases of liver disease with reversed qi, deafness occurs. Zhu Danxi indicated that deafness is associated with heat, primarily involving the lesser yang and jueyin heat. It also connects with the hand and foot shaoyang sanjiao and gallbladder, as well as the hand taiyang small intestine channels.

The "Lingshu" notes: The lesser yang roots in the qiao yin and converges in the window cage; the window cage refers to the interior. The "Suwen" states that one yang solely howls as the lesser yang's destiny, resulting in deafness at the end. Howling refers to the sound echoing in the ears. The gallbladder and sanjiao channels both enter the ears; therefore, if qi reverses upwards, a ringing in the ears occurs. It further states that the lesser yang governs the gallbladder, its channel winding at the ribs towards the ears; thus, after three days of cold damage, if the lesser yang is affected, pain in the chest and ribs ensues alongside deafness; after nine days of a weakened lesser yang, deafness becomes minimally perceived. Additionally, the "Lingshu" mentions that diseases arising from the hand taiyang lead to deafness and jaundiced eyes. This also correlates with the hand and foot yangming large intestine and stomach channels.[60p]

　　 【《素问》曰：头痛耳鸣，九窍不利，肠胃之所生也。《灵枢》曰：聋而痛者，取手阳明；聋而不痛者，取足少阳。又曰：耳者宗脉之所聚也，胃中空则宗脉虚，虚则下溜，脉有所竭者，故耳鸣。】　　又属足太阳膀胱经。
　　 【《素问》曰：太阳所谓耳鸣者，阳气万物盛上而跃，故耳鸣也。】　　又属手足少阴心肾、太阴肺脾、足阳明胃经之络。　　 【《素问》曰：此五络皆属于耳中，上络左角，邪客之则病。】　　耳前属手足少阳三焦胆、足阳明胃经之会。　　 【《素问》曰：上部入耳前之动脉，在耳前陷者中。动应于手，手少阳脉气之所行也。】　　耳后属手足少阳三焦胆经之会。[61p]

The "Su Wen" states: Headache and tinnitus arise from the dysfunction of the nine orifices, originating in the intestines and stomach. The "Ling Shu" explains: For deafness accompanied by pain, treat the hand's Yangming; for deafness without pain, treat the foot's Shaoyang. It also says: The ears are where the ancestral channel gathers; when the stomach is empty, the ancestral channel is weak, leading to a downward flow, causing a depletion in the channels and resulting in tinnitus. Furthermore, it is linked to the Foot Taiyang Bladder channel.

The "Su Wen" further states: The Taiyang's concept of tinnitus arises because the Yang qi is abundant and surges upward, hence the ear ringing. It is also connected to the Hand and Foot Shaoyin Heart and Kidney, Taiyin Lung and Spleen, and the Foot Yangming Stomach channels.

The "Su Wen" notes that all five channels are related to the ear, with the upper channel affecting the left ear and causing illness when disturbed by pathogens. The area in front of the ear is connected to the Hand and Foot Shaoyang Sanjiao and Gallbladder, and the Foot Yangming Stomach channels.

Additionally, according to the "Su Wen," the arteries entering the area before the ear are located in the depression just in front of the ear. The movement corresponds to the hand, as it is where the qi of the hand's Shaoyang circulates. Behind the ear, it pertains to the gathering of the Hand and Foot Shaoyang Sanjiao and Gallbladder channels.[61p]

　　 【李东垣曰：少阳者，斜出于耳前后也。】　　耳下曲颊，属足少阳胆、阳明大肠经之会，又属手太阳小肠经。　　 【《灵枢》曰：手太阳当曲颊。】　　曲颊前属足少阳胆、阳明大肠经之会。　　前寸许属手阳明大肠经。
　　曲颊后属足少阳胆经。
　　【《灵枢》曰：足少阳在耳下曲颊之后。】　　赵以德曰：耳者肾之窍，足少阴经之所主。然心亦寄窍于耳。在人身十二经络中，除足太阳手厥阴外，其余十经脉络皆入于耳中。盖肾治内之阴，心治外之阳，合天地之道，精气无处而不交通，故清凈精明之气上走空窍，耳受之而听斯聪矣。因此耳属二脏之窍也。于是诸经禀其阴阳五行，精明者皆上入之，所以宫商角征羽之五音从斯辨矣。经曰：积阳为天，积阴为地，清阳出上窍是也。若二气不调，则交通不表，故阳气者闭塞，地气者冒明。[62p]

Li Dongyuan said: "The Shaoyang refers to the area slanting out from the front and back of the ear." Below the ear, the curved cheek belongs to the convergence of the Foot Shaoyang Gallbladder and Yangming Large Intestine Channels, and also pertains to the Hand Taiyang Small Intestine Channel.

The "Lingshu" states: "The Hand Taiyang is at the curved cheek." The front part of the curved cheek corresponds to the convergence of the Foot Shaoyang Gallbladder and Yangming Large Intestine Channels, while the area about an inch in front pertains to the Hand Yangming Large Intestine Channel. The back of the curved cheek belongs to the Foot Shaoyang Gallbladder Channel.

The "Lingshu" notes: "The Foot Shaoyang is behind the curved cheek beneath the ear." Zhao Yide remarked: "The ear is the orifice of the kidneys, governed by the Foot Shaoyin Channel. However, the heart also has its orifice in the ear. Among the twelve channels in the human body, except for the Foot Taiyang and Hand Jueyin, the other ten channels all connect to the ear. The kidneys manage the internal yin, while the heart governs the external yang; combined, they reflect the way of heaven and earth, with essence and energy interconnected everywhere. Therefore, the pure and bright energy goes upwards to the orifices, allowing the ear to receive it and attain hearing. Thus, the ear belongs to the orifices of two organs.

In this way, the various channels embody their yin, yang, and five elements; those that are pure and bright all ascend into this. Hence, the five sounds of Gong, Shang, Jiao, Zheng, and Yu can be distinguished from this. The classic states: "Accumulation of yang is heaven; accumulation of yin is earth. Clear yang emerges from the upper orifices." If the two energies are unbalanced, then communication does not manifest, hence yang energy becomes obstructed and earth energy becomes muddled.[62p]

而阳气之闭塞者，或因烦劳阴虚气浮，或因卫气不下，循脉积聚于上，或得于邪风与阳并盛，或因热淫之胜，或因三焦之火独光，而耳中浑浑焞焞，或因经脏积热所致，或因大怒气上而不下。夫如是者，皆由心气虚实不调，虚则不能治其阳，下与阴交，实则恃阳强而与阴绝。经曰：至阴虚天气绝是也。而地气之冒明者，或忧愁不解，阴气闭塞，不与阳通，或内外湿饮，痞隔其气，不得升降，则耳中亦浑浑焞焞，或肾精脱。若热病之精脱，二者尺脉绝则死。或耳中因二气不和，结干耵聍塞之。夫如是皆由肾气不和，虚则阴气微，不能上交于阳，而阳是暴，实则阴气逆，不纳其阳也。　　暴聋之病，与阴阳隔绝之未甚，经脉欲行而未通，冲击其中，鼓动听户，随其气之微甚而作嘈嘈风雨诸声者，则可随其邪以为治，补不足，泻有余，务使阴阳和平，自然清凈之气上走耳中而听斯聪矣。[63p]

The blockage of Yang Qi may stem from fatigue causing Yin deficiency and Qi floating, or from Wei Qi not descending, circulating and accumulating above. It could arise from the simultaneous presence of external wind and Yang, or excessive heat, or the isolated brilliance of the fire of the Sanjiao. This results in muddiness and turbidity in the ears, possibly caused by heat accumulation in the organs, or due to great anger causing Qi to rise without descending. All these conditions are due to the disharmony of the heart's Qi; if it is deficient, it cannot govern Yang, and if it is excessive, it relies solely on the strength of Yang, cutting off Yin. The classics say: “The ultimate Yin’s deficiency leads to the cessation of the heavenly Qi.”

As for the invasion of Earth Qi by brightness, it may be due to unresolved sorrow causing closure of Yin Qi, which does not connect with Yang, or due to internal and external dampness obstructing the Qi, preventing it from rising or falling, thus also resulting in muddiness and turbidity in the ears, or the depletion of kidney essence. If the essence is depleted due to a heat illness, complete loss of both pulse indicators signifies death.

An ear condition due to disharmony of the two Qi can result in a blockage from accumulating earwax. All these issues arise from disharmony in kidney Qi; when deficient, Yin Qi is weak and cannot ascend to meet Yang, and when excessive, Yin Qi rises against Yang, rejecting it.

The condition of sudden deafness is not severed from the separation of Yin and Yang; the channels desire to flow but are not open. If they are struck and agitated internally, stimulating the auditory orifice, and depending on the subtlety of the Qi, various sounds like a tumultuous wind and rain may emerge. Thus, one can treat the condition by following the evil, supplementing the deficiency, and draining the excess, striving for Yin and Yang's harmony. Naturally, the clear and pure Qi will ascend to the ears, restoring hearing.[63p]

曰：若子所表，言水火同开此窍，何《原病式》之非温补耶？曰：心在窍为舌，以舌非孔窍，因寄窍于耳，则是肾为耳窍之主，心为耳窍之客。以五脏开窍于面部，分阴精阳气言之。在肾肝居阴，故耳目二窍，阴精主之；在心肺脾居阳，故口舌鼻三窍，阳气主之。所以阴精主者，贵清凉而恶烦热；阳气主者，贵温暖而恶寒凉。洁古老人尝有是论，信耳目之不可以温补也。　　风虚耳聋，排风汤、桂星散、羊肾羹、鱼脑膏、磁石丸、姜蝎散。　　风热耳聋，犀角饮子、芍药散、犀角散、茯神散。　　耳因郁聋轻者，吞来复丹，重者吞养正丹。凡治耳聋皆当调气。　　气逆耳聋有三，肝与手太阳、少阳也。经云：肝气逆，则头痛，耳聋不聪，颊肿。又云：太阳所谓浮为聋者，皆在气也。[64p]

It is said: If what you express indicates that water and fire open this orifice equally, how can the "Original Disease Formulas" not be considered warming and strengthening? It is said: The heart is connected to the orifice as the tongue; since the tongue is not an orifice, the orifice is related to the ears, thus the kidneys are the master of the ear orifice, and the heart is a guest of the ear orifice. The five organs open their orifices to the face, distinguishing between yin essence and yang qi. The kidneys and liver reside in yin, hence the ear and eye orifices are governed by yin essence; the heart, lungs, and spleen reside in yang, hence the mouth, tongue, and nose orifices are governed by yang qi. Therefore, those in charge of yin essence value clarity and coolness while rejecting heat and disturbance; those in charge of yang qi value warmth while rejecting coldness and chill. The ancient elders had such discussions, believing that the ears and eyes cannot be warmed and strengthened.

For deafness due to wind deficiency, use solutions such as Wind-Dispelling Decoction, Cinnamon Star Powder, Lamb Kidney Soup, Fish Brain Ointment, Magnetic Stone Pill, and Ginger Scorpion Powder.

For deafness due to wind heat, use remedies such as Rhinoceros Horn Decoction, Peony Powder, Rhinoceros Horn Powder, and Poria Powder.

For ear deafness arising from depression, for mild cases, take the Returning Elixir; for severe cases, take the Nurturing Right Elixir. For all treatments of ear deafness, it is essential to regulate qi.

There are three types of ear deafness due to reversed qi: those related to the liver, the hand taiyang, and the shaoyang. The classics state: When liver qi is reversed, it causes headaches, deafness, and facial swelling. It further states: When the taiyang is said to be "floating," it is all about qi.[64p]

罗谦甫云：手太阳气厥而耳聋者，其候聋而耳内气满也；手少阳气厥而耳聋者，其候耳内浑浑焞焞，此皆气逆而聋也。治法宜四物汤吞龙荟丸降火，及复元通气散调气是也。　　耳聋面颊黑者，为精脱肾虚。罗谦甫云：经曰：精脱者则耳聋。夫肾为足少阴之经，乃藏精而气通于耳。耳者宗脉之所聚也。若精气调和，则肾脏强盛耳闻五音。若劳伤气血，兼受风邪，损于肾脏而精脱者，则耳聋也。然五脏六腑，十二经脉，有络于耳者，其阴阳经气有相并时，并则脏气逆，名之曰厥。厥气相搏，入于耳之脉，则令聋。其肾病精脱耳聋者，其候颊颧色黑。手少阳之脉动，则气厥逆而耳聋者，其候耳内浑浑焞焞也。手太阳厥而耳聋者，其候聋而其内气满也，宜以烧肾散主之。　　烧肾散、益肾散、补肾丸、苁蓉丸、肉苁蓉丸、桑螵蛸汤，肾虚有寒者宜之。　　本事地黄汤，肾虚有热者宜之。[65p]

Luo Qianfu said: When the hand of the Taiyang channel experiences a blockage of qi causing deafness, the symptom is fullness of air in the ear; when the hand of the Shaoyang channel experiences a blockage of qi causing deafness, the symptom is a sensation of muddiness and confusion in the ear. All of these conditions arise from reversed qi leading to deafness. The treatment methods should include the Four Substance Decoction, the Longhui Pill for reducing fire, and the Recovery and Circulation Powder to regulate qi.

For those with deafness accompanied by a dark complexion on the cheeks, this indicates loss of essence and kidney deficiency. Luo Qianfu states: As the classics say, loss of essence leads to deafness. The kidneys belong to the Foot Shaoyin channel and store essence while the qi flows to the ears. The ears are where the ancestral vessels converge. If essence and qi are harmonized, the kidneys are strong, and one can hear the five tones. However, if one exhausts qi and blood through overwork, combined with invasion of wind pathogens damaging the kidneys, leading to loss of essence, then deafness occurs.

In this regard, all five organs, six bowels, and the twelve meridians that connect to the ears have their yin and yang qi mutually interacting; when they do interact, the organ’s qi may reverse, which is termed "jué" (blockage). When the qi of blockage collides and enters the meridian of the ear, it leads to deafness. In the case of kidney-related deafness with loss of essence, the characteristic is a blackish hue on the cheeks. In the case of the movement of the hand in the Shaoyang meridian causing blockage and deafness, the symptom is a muddled sensation in the ear. For the hand of the Taiyang channel experiencing blockage and deafness, the symptom is deafness along with fullness of inner qi; thus, it is appropriate to use the Shao Shen San to address it.

The Shao Shen San, Yi Shen San, Bu Shen Wan, Cong Rong Wan, Rou Cong Rong Wan, and Sang Piao Xiao Decoction are suitable for those with kidney deficiency and cold. The Ben Shi Di Huang Decoction is suitable for those with kidney deficiency and heat.[65p]

　　耳聋少气嗌干者，为肺虚。东垣曰：脏气法时论云，肺虚则少气不能报息，耳聋嗌干。注云，肺之络会于耳中，故聋。此说非也。盖气虚必寒，盛则气血俱濇滞而不行也。耳者宗气也，肺气不行，故聋也。宜生脉散嚼下蜡弹丸。　　劳聋，宜益气聪明汤。
　　头目不清，清神散。
　　气闭不通，通气散、秘传降气汤加菖蒲。[66p]

Deafness with little energy and a dry throat indicates lung deficiency. Dongyuan states: According to the theory of organ qi, when the lungs are deficient, there is insufficient energy to breathe, leading to deafness and a dry throat. The commentary explains that the lung's meridian connects to the ears, hence the deafness. However, this explanation is inadequate. In fact, when qi is deficient, it must be cold; if excessive, both qi and blood stagnate and fail to circulate. The ears are associated with the primordial qi; if lung qi does not circulate, deafness results. It is advisable to take Shengmai San and chew down wax pills. For labor-related deafness, one should use Yiqi Congming Tang.

For unclear vision and head fog, use Qingshen San.

For obstructed qi that does not flow, use Tongqi San, and add Xuanfu to Mijuan Jiangqi Tang.[66p]

　　　　　耳发

　　或问耳轮生疽何如？曰：是名耳发疽，属手少阳三焦经，风热所致，六七日渐肿如胡桃，或如蜂房之状，或赤或紫，热如火，痛彻心是也。十日刺出黄白脓者生，刺之无脓，时出鲜血，饮食不下，神昏狂躁者死。小儿耳窍旁生者，相传指月而生，恐未必然。大抵风湿热毒成疳，故名月蚀疳疮。
　　　　　耳内疮

　　或问耳中生毒何如？曰：耳中所患不同，皆由足少阴手少阳二经风热上壅而然。其证有五：曰聤耳，亦曰耳湿，常出黄脓；有耳风毒，常出红脓；有缠耳，常出白脓；有耳疳，生疮臭秽；有震耳，耳内虚鸣，常出清脓。虽有五般，其源一也，皆不寒热。有耳蕈、耳痔则不作脓，亦不寒热，外无拥肿，但耳塞不通。以上缠绵不已，令人耳聋，活命饮、黄连消毒饮治之，若寒热间作，内外红肿，疼痛日增者，为耳痈，用活命饮加升麻、桔梗、紫金丹、乌金丹。壮实者一粒金丹下之。若寒热大作，痛楚难禁者，疔也，作疔治之。[67p]

Ear Furuncle

Some ask what it means when a furuncle grows on the auricle. It is called "ear furuncle," related to the hand Shaoyang Sanjiao meridian, caused by wind and heat. After six or seven days, it gradually swells like a walnut, or takes on the shape of a honeycomb, either red or purple, hot like fire, with pain piercing the heart. If, after ten days, yellowish-white pus can be drained, the patient is likely to survive; if there is no pus, but fresh blood sometimes flows, and the patient cannot eat and shows signs of confusion and delirium, they may die. It is said that in children, if a furuncle grows beside the ear canal, it is attributed to pointing at the moon, but this may not be strictly true. Generally, wind, dampness, heat, and toxin congeal to form sores, hence it is called "lunar erosion sore."

Ear Ulcer

Some ask what happens when there is a toxic condition inside the ear. It is noted that conditions within the ear differ but are all due to wind and heat obstructing the foot Shaoyin and hand Shaoyang meridians. The symptoms can be classified into five types:

  1. "Tinnitus," also known as ear dampness, which frequently discharges yellow pus.
  2. "Ear wind toxin," which discharges red pus.
  3. "Ear entanglement," which discharges white pus.
  4. "Ear ulcer," associated with foul sores.
  5. "Ear tremor," characterized by a hollow ringing inside the ear, often discharging clear pus.

Though there are five types, they share a common root and none are associated with cold or heat. Conditions like ear fungus or ear hemorrhoids do not produce pus, are neither warm nor cold, and do not have swelling, but rather, there is a blockage in the ear. If these conditions persist, they can lead to deafness. Treatment involves drinks like "Vitality Drink" or "Huanglian Detoxifying Drink." If there are alternating cold and heat symptoms, with internal and external redness and swelling, and increasing pain, it is classified as ear abscess. In such cases, "Vitality Drink," combined with herbs like Shengma, Jiegeng, Zijingdan, and Wujindan, should be used. For strong patients, a single pill of gold pill can be administered. If there is severe cold and heat, with unbearable pain, it indicates a boil, which should be treated as such.[67p]

　　　　　耳后疽

　　或问耳后一寸三分生疽，古云不治之证。今有一人年二十四岁，耳后结块如拳，肉色不变，亦不甚痛，七日不食何如？曰：此名耳后毒，非瘿也。隔蒜灸之，活命饮加柴胡、桔梗、升麻，八阵散下之愈。
　　　　　耳根毒

　　或问耳根结核何如？曰：是名耳根毒，状如痰核，按之不动而微痛，属足少阳胆经，兼三焦经风热所致。用活命饮加升麻、柴胡，水酒煎服；或乌金散汗之。壮实者一粒金丹汗之；老弱者黄芪内托散、十宣散托之。[68p]

Ear Abscess

Someone asked about an abscess that forms one inch and three tenths behind the ear, which in ancient times was said to be a sign of not needing treatment. Now, there is a person aged twenty-four, with a lump the size of a fist behind the ear, the color of flesh, and not very painful. What if he does not eat for seven days? It was replied: This is called an ear poison, not a goiter. Use garlic for moxibustion, and the Huoxiang Zhengqi Decoction with Chaihu, Jiegeng, and Shengma. After taking the Bazhensi powder, he recovers.

Ear Root Poison

Someone asked about a nodule at the root of the ear. It was replied: This is called ear root poison, resembling a phlegm nodule, immovable upon pressing with slight pain. It pertains to the Gallbladder Meridian of the Lesser Yang and is caused by wind-heat from the Sanjiao Meridian. Use Huoxiang Zhengqi Decoction with Shengma and Chaihu, decocted in water and wine; or use Wujin San to induce sweating. For those who are strong, one pill of Jindan will cause sweating; for the old and weak, use Huangqi Neishu San and Shixuan San to assist.[68p]

　　　　医方考 【明　吴昆】

　　　　　耳病方论

　　耳以司听，匪听弗聪也。君子有思聪之责者，胡然而使褎如乎？故考方论。　　肾热，耳中脓血不闻人声者，千金肾热汤主之。盖耳者肾之窍，故肾热则令人病耳，生脓出血，不闻人声也。是方也，磁石能引肺金之气下降于肾，肾得母气，自然清肃而热日愈。生地汁、麦门冬、白芍药，所以滋肾阴而泻肾热。乃葱白者所以引肾气上通于耳也。牡蛎咸寒，能软坚而破结气，得葱白引之入耳，则能开听户而消脓血。乃白朮、甘草、大枣者，健脾之品也，所以培万物之母，益土气而制肾邪尔。　　劳聋、气聋、风聋、虚聋、毒聋、久聋、耳鸣者，千金补肾丸主之。盖劳聋者，劳火鼓其听户也；气聋者，经气滞塞于听户也；风聋者，风热闭其听户也；虚聋者，气血虚耗而神不用也；毒聋者，脓血障碍妨于听户也；久聋者，病非一日，邪气痹聚也。凡是聋者，势必耳鸣，故总系其耳鸣也。[69p]

Medical Formulas Examined

On Ear Diseases

The ear is responsible for hearing; if it cannot hear, it becomes deaf. A gentleman who has the responsibility of listening wisely would not allow this to happen. Thus, I examine the formulas.

For kidney heat, where there is pus and blood in the ear and one cannot hear human voices, the "Thousand Gold Kidney Heat Decoction" is the main treatment. The ear is an opening of the kidneys; therefore, when there is kidney heat, it causes ear ailments, leading to pus and bleeding, and one cannot hear. This formula uses magnetite to draw the metallic energy of the lungs down to the kidneys, allowing the kidneys to receive the maternal energy, which naturally clears the heat and improves the condition. The juices of raw rehmannia, Ophiopogon, and white peony root are used to nourish kidney yin and drain kidney heat. The green onion white parts are to guide the kidney energy upwards to the ears. The oyster is salty and cold, capable of softening hardness and breaking up stagnation. When combined with the green onion and applied to the ear, it opens the auditory passages and eliminates pus and blood. The rhizome of white atractylodes, licorice, and jujubes are ingredients that strengthen the spleen to nourish the maternal source of all, enhance earth energy, and control kidney evil.

For deafness due to labor, qi stagnation, wind, deficiency, toxins, prolonged conditions, and tinnitus, the "Thousand Gold Kidney Tonifying Pill" is the main remedy. Labor deafness occurs due to labor fire affecting the auditory passages; qi deafness results from stagnation in these passages; wind deafness arises when wind-heat obstructs the auditory pathways; deficiency deafness occurs from the exhaustion of qi and blood, leading to a lack of sensory responsiveness; toxic deafness results when pus and blood obstruct the auditory pathways; prolonged deafness ensues from illness persisting for a long time, causing evil energy to accumulate. Generally, any instance of deafness is likely accompanied by tinnitus; thus, it all relates back to the condition of tinnitus.[69p]

味之甘者，可以补虚，亦可却劳，人参、黄芪、羊肾、山萸、干地黄、菟丝、巴戟、苁蓉、泽泻、芍药、当归、茯苓、甘草，均之味甘之品也，能疗气虚聋劳聋。味之辛者，可以驱风，亦可以顺气，防风、细辛、菖蒲、远志，丹皮、石斛，均之味辛之品也，能疗聋风聋。性之毒者可以开结毒，亦可以疗久痹，蛇床、桂心、附子、干姜，均之辛温微毒之品也，能疗毒聋久聋。[70p]

The sweet-flavored substances can replenish deficiency and also dispel labor: ginseng, astragalus, sheep kidney, cornel, dried rehmannia, dodder, baijie, cortex cynomorii, alisma, peony, angelica, poria, and licorice—all are sweet-tasting items capable of treating qi deficiency and fatigue-induced deafness. The pungent-flavored substances can drive away wind and also regulate qi: saposhnikovia, asarum, calamus, polygala, moutan, and dendrobium—all are pungent items able to treat wind-induced deafness. Toxic substances can open blockages and also heal chronic numbness: cnidium, cinnamon heart, fuzi, and dried ginger—all are mildly toxic items that can treat toxic and long-standing deafness.[70p]

　　三十年久聋，用故铁三十斤，以水七斗浸三日，取汁，入曲酿米七斗，如常造酒法，候熟，取磁石一斤，研末浸酒中三日，乃以饮取醉，以绵裹磁石，内耳中，覆头一卧，酒醒去磁石即瘥。昆谓磁石引铁，物类之相感也。金石之性寒，可使主内热；金石之性重，可使镇祛气。共酿于酒，欲其无所不之，既饮其酒，复以磁石内耳，欲其内外交感而听户随开尔。　　耳脓用人发烧灰存性，每用分许，吹入耳中，即瘥。此湿者燥之之意，而必以人发者，近取诸身而自足也。他如白矾、赤石脂、鸽粪，皆可枯灰用之。[71p]

For thirty years, I have been deaf. I used thirty pounds of old iron, soaked in seven dou of water for three days, to extract the juice, and added it to seven dou of rice for brewing, following the usual method of making wine. After it ripens, I took one pound of magnetite, ground it into powder, and soaked it in the wine for three days. Then, I drank it to become intoxicated, wrapped the magnetite in cotton, placed it in my ear, and lay down with my head covered. When I sobered up, I removed the magnetite, and my hearing was restored. It is said that magnetite attracts iron, and this reflects the mutual influence of similar substances. The nature of metals and stones is cold, which can dispel internal heat; their heavy nature can help calm and expel qi. By brewing it in the wine, it is desired that there is no place it does not affect. After drinking the wine, placing the magnetite in the ear aims for a mutual interaction of internal and external sensations, allowing hearing to resume.

For treating ear pus, one can use ash from burned human hair. Each time, a small amount is blown into the ear to effect a cure. This is to dry out moisture, and it must be human hair, as it is derived from the body and thus self-sufficient. Other substances like white alum, red stone resin, and pigeon droppings can also be used as dry powders.[71p]

　　　　外科正宗 【明　陈实功】

　　　　　耳病

　　耳病乃三焦肝风妄动而成，大人有虚火实火之分，小儿有胎热胎风之别。虚火者耳内蝉鸣，或兼重听，出水作痒，外无焮肿，此属虚火妄动之证也。四物汤加牡丹皮、石菖蒲及肾气丸主之。实火者耳根耳窍俱肿，甚则寒热交作，疼痛无时，宜柴胡清肝汤治之。又有耳挺结于窍内，气脉不通，疼痛不止，以栀子清肝汤为治，外用黄线药插入挺肉缝旁，化尽乃愈。小儿胎热，或浴洗水灌窍中，亦致耳窍作痛生脓，初起月间不必擦药治早，项内生肿，候毒尽自愈。如月外不瘥，以红绵散治之，则安矣。
　　　　　百虫入耳

　　百虫入耳，乃偶然悞入之，如蝇蚊细虫入耳，以麻油数点滴入窍中，虫亦自死，取出。如蜈蚣等大虫入者，以肉炙香安耳边，其虫闻香自出。有虫夜间暗入者，切勿惊慌喊叫，逼虫内攻，宜正坐点灯，光向耳窍，其虫见光自出，对面有人见，其虫不出。[72p]

Ear Diseases

Ear diseases are caused by the erratic movement of liver wind in the three burners. In adults, there is a distinction between deficiency heat and excess heat; in children, there is a difference between fetal heat and fetal wind. Deficiency heat manifests as a ringing sensation in the ear, possibly accompanied by hearing loss, itching due to fluid discharge, with no swelling externally; this indicates errant movement of deficiency heat. One should treat this with Four Substance Decoction plus peony root, sweet flag, and Kidney Qi Pill. Excess heat presents as swelling in the ear root and ear canal, and can lead to alternating chills and fever, with persistent pain; it is advisable to treat this with Chai Hu Qing Gan Decoction. If there is a blockage in the ear canal causing continuous pain, one should use Gardenia Qing Gan Decoction for treatment, and externally insert a yellow line medicine beside the blocked tissue until it is resolved. For children with fetal heat, bathing or washing water entering the ear canal can also cause ear pain and pus formation; initially, there is no need to apply medicine for early stages, and if swelling occurs in the neck, one should wait for the toxin to subside naturally. If it does not heal by the end of the month, it should be treated with Hong Mian San, and all will be well.

Insects Entering the Ear

Insects entering the ear happen occasionally, such as flies or small worms. To remove them, place a few drops of sesame oil into the ear canal; the insect will die and can be extracted. For larger insects like centipedes that enter, heat fragrant meat near the ear; the insect will emerge due to the smell. If an insect enters in the dark at night, do not panic or shout, as this may push the insect further in. Instead, sit upright, light a lamp, and direct the light toward the ear canal; the insect, seeing the light, will come out. If there is someone else present, the insect may not come out.[72p]

　　　　　黑疔

　　黑疔生于耳窍之内，黑硬腐烂，破流血水，疼及腮颧，宜先针刺，次行发汗，仍照疔类调治。
　　　　医门法律 【清　喻昌】

　　　　　耳鸣

　　人身有九窍：阳窍七，眼耳鼻口是也；阴窍二，前后二阴是也。阳气走上窍而下入于阴位，则有溺泄腹鸣之候；阴气走下窍而上入于阳位，则有窒塞耳鸣之候。故人当五十以外，肾气渐衰于下，每每从阳上逆。而肾之窍开于耳，耳之聪司于肾，肾主闭藏，不欲外泄，因肝木为子，疏泄母气而散于外，是以谋虑郁怒之火一动，阴气从之上逆，耳窍窒塞不清，故能听之用不碍，而听远不无少碍。高年之体，大率类然。较之聋病，一天一渊。聋病者其窍中另有一膜，遮蔽外气，不得内入，故以开窍为主，而方书所用石菖蒲、麝香等药，及外填内攻等法者，皆为此而设。[73p]

Black Carbuncle

The black carbuncle occurs within the ear canal, appearing as a black hard lump that decays and bleeds. It causes pain in the jaw and cheek. It is advisable to first use a needle to pierce it, followed by inducing sweating, while still treating it according to carbuncle guidelines.
— Medical Texts of the Medical Profession [Qing Dynasty, Yu Chang]

Tinnitus

The human body has nine orifices: seven are yang orifices—namely the eyes, ears, nose, and mouth; two are yin orifices—these are the front and rear openings. When yang energy moves outward through the orifices and descends to the yin areas, symptoms such as urinary issues and abdominal sounds arise. Conversely, when yin energy moves downward through the orifices and rises to the yang areas, symptoms such as blocked ear ringing occur.

After the age of fifty, kidney energy gradually weakens; this often causes a reversal of yang energy. Since the kidney orifice opens to the ears and ear hearing is governed by the kidneys, which are responsible for storage and do not wish to leak externally, the liver, as the mother of wood, disperses the motherly energy outward. Thus, when thoughts and emotions cause an upsurge of fire and the yin energy reverses upwards, the ear orifice becomes blocked and unclear. Therefore, one can still hear without obstruction but may find distant sounds slightly impaired. Generally, this occurs in older individuals.

In contrast to deafness, which is more profound, deafness involves a membrane in the orifice that blocks external air from entering. Thus, the primary treatment is to open the orifices, with formulas containing ingredients like Acorus gramineus and musk, as well as external and internal remedies, designed specifically for this issue.[73p]

至于年高，阴气不自收摄，越出上窍之理，从无一人言及，反以治少壮耳聋药及发表散气药，兼带阴虚为治，是以百无一效。不知阴气至上窍，亦隔一膜，不能越出窍外，止于窍中汩汩有声，如蛙鼓蚊锣，鼓吹不已，以故外入之声为其内声所混，听之不清，若气稍不逆上，则听稍清，气全不逆上，则听全清矣。昌悟明此理，凡治高年逆上之气，屡有奇效。方中大意，全以磁石为主，以其重能达下，性主下吸，又能制肝木之上吸故也。而用地黄、龟胶群阴之药辅之，更用五味子、山茱萸之酸以收之，令阴气自旺于本宫，不上触于阳窍，繇是空旷无碍。耳之于声，似谷之受响，万籁之音，尚可细聆，岂更与人声相拒艰于远听耶？此实至理所在，但医术浅薄之辈，不能知之。[74p]

Regarding old age, the yin energy does not naturally gather and is said to overflow from the upper orifices; no one has mentioned this principle. Instead, treatments for the hearing of the young and for dispersing energy are applied, combined with remedies for yin deficiency, resulting in almost no effectiveness. They do not realize that the yin energy reaching the upper orifices is also separated by a membrane and cannot escape outside, only producing sounds within, akin to the croaking of frogs or the buzzing of mosquitoes, incessantly reverberating. Thus, external sounds mix with internal sounds, rendering the hearing unclear. If the energy slightly does not reverse upwards, the hearing becomes somewhat clearer; if the energy does not reverse upwards at all, the hearing becomes entirely clear. If one understands this principle, there can be extraordinary results in treating the upward reversing energy of the elderly. The essence of the treatment involves using magnetism as the main focus, as it can effectively pull downwards and suppress the upward aspect of the liver's wood energy. Additionally, it employs herbs like rehmannia and tortoise shell to support yin, along with the sourness of schisandra and cornelian cherry to gather it, ensuring that the yin energy thrives in its source without ascending to disturb the yang orifices, thus remaining unobstructed. Just as ears receive sound like valleys absorbing echoes, even amidst various sounds, one can still listen carefully; how could one struggle to hear distant human voices? This is indeed the underlying truth, but those with shallow medical knowledge cannot comprehend it.[74p]

试观人之收视而视愈明，返听而听愈聪者，然后知斯言非臆说也。　　人两肾之窍虽开于耳，而肾气上入耳际，亦为隔膜所蔽，不能越于耳外，止于耳根下，少则微鸣，多则大鸣，甚且将萦耳之筋触之跳动，直似撞穿耳轮之象者，然实必不可出也。设阴气能出耳外而走阳窍，则阴阳相混，非三才之理矣。故耳之用妙在虚而能受也，外入之气随大随小，至耳无碍，惟内触之气咶咶有声，所以外入之气仅通其半。若郁怒之火动，内气转增，则外入之气转混，必内气渐走下窍，上窍复其虚而能受之体，然后清清朗朗，声入即通，无壅碍也。[75p]

Try to observe that when a person collects their sight, it becomes clearer, and when they return to listen, they become more astute; then one can understand that these words are not mere speculation. Although the orifices of the two kidneys open at the ears, the kidney energy rises to the ear's edge, blocked by a membrane, preventing it from exceeding the ear's boundaries. It is confined below the roots of the ears, producing faint sounds if little and loud sounds if much, to the extent that the muscles around the ear may twitch as if piercing through the outer ear; nevertheless, it cannot actually escape. If the yin energy could exit the ears and traverse the yang orifices, then yin and yang would be mixed, which contradicts the principles of the Three Powers. Thus, the function of the ears is remarkably subtle; they are empty and receptive. The external energies vary in size; when they reach the ears, they encounter no obstruction, but the internal energies resonate audibly, hence the external energies only penetrate halfway. If the fire of pent-up anger stirs, the internal energy increases, blending with the external energy; then the internal energy gradually flows downward, restoring the upper orifices to their empty and receptive state, allowing sounds to enter clearly and unobstructed.[75p]

方书指为少阳胆、厥阴肝二经热多所致，是说左耳分部，然少阳之气能走上窍，其穴皆络于脑巅，无触筋冲耳之理，不当与厥阴混同立说。其通圣散一方汗下兼用，乃治壮火之法。丹溪所取，亦无确见，惟滚痰丸一方，少壮用之多效者，则以大黄、黄芩、沉香乏苦，最能下气，而礞石之重坠，大约与磁石之用相仿也。昌所以不用此方者，以其大损脾胃，且耗胸中氤氲之气也。至于肾虚耳鸣，指作膀胱相火上升，则阳火必能透出上窍而为鸣也，尤见丹溪无据之谈。《易》言水中有火。原说真火坎中一点真阳即真火也。高年之人肾水易竭，真火易露，故肾中之气易出难收，况有厥阴之子为之挹取乎？则壮水之主以制阳光，如盏中加油而灯焰自小，诚为良法。乃云作肾虚治不效者，知其泛论世人，不为老人立法也。夫收摄肾气，原为老人之先务，岂丹溪明哲而为此等议论乎？[76p]

The classical text indicates that the ailments related to the lesser yang gallbladder and the jueyin liver channels are largely due to excess heat, particularly affecting the left ear. However, the qi of the lesser yang can ascend to the orifices, with its acupoints all connecting to the crown of the head. There is no reason to conflate it with the jueyin. The Tongsheng Powder, which is used for sweating and purging, is a method for treating vigorous fire. Danxi's herbal choices are not clearly documented; however, the Rolling Phlegm Pill, particularly effective for the young, uses rhubarb, Scutellaria, and sandalwood which are not bitter but can descend qi effectively. The weight of calamine stone is somewhat analogous to the use of a magnet. Chang refrains from using this remedy because it significantly damages the spleen and stomach and depletes the vital energy within the chest.

As for ear ringing due to kidney deficiency, it is linked to the bladder's fire rising, where yang fire can infiltrate the orifices and cause the ringing. This is further unsupported in Danxi's claims. The Book of Changes states there is fire within water, implying that the true fire is a small point of genuine yang within the K’an. For elderly individuals, kidney water is prone to depletion, making genuine fire easier to reveal, and thus the qi within the kidneys tends to escape and is hard to gather again. One might question whether the jueyin’s offspring could assist in this. It is optimal to strengthen the water element to control the yang fire, akin to adding oil to a lamp to keep the flame small; this is indeed a good method. If there are claims about ineffective treatments for kidney deficiency, it is clear that these are generalized observations and not specifically applicable to the elderly. Gathering and securing kidney qi are fundamentally the priorities for the elderly, so would Danxi, known for his wisdom, truly engage in such discussions?[76p]

　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

　　　　　论证

　　耳聋证，诸家所论虽悉，然以余之见，大都其证有五：曰火闭，曰气闲，曰邪闭，曰窍闭，曰虚闭。　　凡火闭者，因诸经之火壅塞清道，其证必哄哄熇熇，或胀或闷，或烦或热，或兼头面红赤者是也。此证治宜清火，火清而闭自开也。　　气闭者，多因肝胆气逆，其证非虚非火，或因恚怒忧郁，气结而然。治宜顺气，气顺心舒而闭自开也。　　邪闭者，因风寒外感，乱其营卫也，解其邪而闭自开。　　窍闭者，必因损伤或挖伤，或雷炮震伤者，或患聤耳，溃脓不止而坏其窍者，宜用开通之法以治之也。[77p]

The Complete Book of Jingyue
(Ming Dynasty, Zhang Jieben)

Discussion of Symptoms

Regarding deafness, although various schools have discussed it, in my view, there are primarily five types of symptoms: Fire Closure, Qi Stagnation, Pathogenic Closure, Orifice Closure, and Deficiency Closure.

  1. Fire Closure arises from the obstruction of the clear pathways by the fire element in the channels. Its symptoms include a sensation of roaring or heat, swelling, tightness, agitation, or warmth, potentially accompanied by redness in the face. For this condition, treatment should focus on clearing the fire, as clearing the fire will naturally resolve the closure.

  2. Qi Stagnation typically results from the rebellious flow of liver and gallbladder qi, characterized by symptoms that are neither deficient nor fiery, often stemming from anger or melancholy, leading to qi stagnation. The treatment should aim to regulate the qi, as smooth qi will relax the heart and lead to the resolution of the closure.

  3. Pathogenic Closure is caused by external factors such as wind or cold affecting the body's protective mechanisms. Treatment should focus on dispersing these pathogenic influences to restore normal function.

  4. Orifice Closure usually occurs due to trauma or injury, such as lacerations or damage from loud noises, or persistent ear issues leading to discharge and deterioration of the orifice. This condition should be addressed with methods that promote opening and restoration.

Each of these types requires a specific approach to treatment based on their underlying causes and characteristics.[77p]

　　虚闭者，或以年衰，或以病后，或以劳倦过度，因致精脱肾亏，渐至聋闭，是非大培根本必不可也。　　凡此数者，有从外不能达者，其病在经；有从内不能通者，其病在脏。当各随其宜而治之，自无不愈者。然暴聋者多易治，久聋者最难为力也。　　耳聋证总因气闭不通耳。盖凡火邪风邪，皆令气壅，壅则闭也。怒则气逆，逆则闭也。窍伤则气窒，窒则闭也。虚则气不充，不充则闭也。凡邪盛气逆而闭者，实闭也。气有不及而闭者，虚闭也。然实闭者少而虚闭者多。且凡属实邪，固令耳窍不通，使果正气强盛，断不至此。[78p]

Those who suffer from deafness may do so due to aging, illness, or excessive fatigue, leading to the depletion of essence and kidney deficiency, which results in gradual hearing loss. It is essential to strengthen the foundation in order to remedy this condition.

Generally, there are cases where the problem cannot be reached externally, and the illness resides within the channels; in contrast, some cases cannot be resolved internally, indicating a problem with the organs. Each should be treated according to its specific nature, and there will inevitably be cures. However, sudden deafness is often easier to treat, while long-lasting deafness is much more challenging to remedy.

The condition of deafness is generally due to obstructed qi not reaching the ears. Indeed, various pathogenic factors like fire or wind can cause qi stagnation, leading to obstruction. Anger causes qi to rebel, which also leads to obstruction. Injury to the orifices can obstruct qi, consequently resulting in closure. Weakness leads to insufficient qi circulation, and insufficient flow leads to obstruction. In general, real obstruction occurs when pathogenic factors are prevalent and qi is rebelling, while virtual obstruction occurs when qi is insufficient. However, true obstruction is rare, while virtual obstruction is common. Furthermore, any condition associated with strong pathogenic influence typically causes deafness and, if the proper qi is robust, it should not reach this point.[78p]

惟经气不足，然后邪气得以夺之，此正邪之所凑，其气必虚之谓也。故即系实邪而病至聋闭者，亦无不有挟虚之象。所以凡治此证，不宜竣攻，如古法之用通圣散、神芎丸、凉膈散、木香槟榔丸之属，皆不可轻用。盖恐攻之未必能愈，反伤脾胃，则他变踵至矣。治此之法，凡火壅于上者，自宜清降，兼阴虚者，亦宜补阴，此阳证之治也。若无火邪，止由气闭，则或补或开，必兼辛温之剂，方可通行，此阴证之治也。然此二者，皆当以渐调理，但无欲速，庶乎尽善。[79p]

Only when the vital energy is insufficient can the evil energy seize it; this is precisely where the true and the false converge, and this energy must be regarded as empty. Therefore, even when the illness manifests as deafness and closure due to real evil, it still carries the appearance of deficiency. Thus, in treating this condition, it is unwise to forcefully attack it, similar to the ancient methods that use Tongsheng San, Shen Xiong Wan, Liang Ge San, and Mu Xiang Bing Lang Wan; these should not be used lightly. This is because attacking may not necessarily lead to recovery and could harm the spleen and stomach, resulting in further complications. In treating this, any fire obstruction above should be cleared and lowered; for those with yin deficiency, it should also be supplemented, as this is the treatment for yang conditions. If there is no fire evil, but only qi obstruction, one may either supplement or open up, but one must include warming and pungent remedies to facilitate passage; this is the treatment for yin conditions. Nonetheless, both approaches should be gradually adjusted, avoiding haste, to achieve the best outcomes.[79p]

　　耳鸣当辨虚实：凡暴鸣而声大者多实，渐鸣而声细者多虚；少壮热盛者多实，中衰无火者多虚；饮酒味厚素多痰火者多实，质清脉细素多劳倦者多虚。且耳为肾窍，乃宗脉之所聚。若精气调和，肾气充足，则耳目聪明；若劳伤血气，精脱肾惫，必至聋聩。故人于中年之后，每多耳鸣，如风雨、如蝉鸣、如潮声者，是皆阴衰肾亏而然。经曰：人年四十而阴气自半，半即衰之谓也。又以《易》义参之，其象尤切。《易》曰：坎为耳，盖坎之阳居中，耳之聪在内，此其所以相应也。今老人之耳，多见聪不内居，而声闻于外，此正肾元不固，阳气渐涣之征耳。欲求来复，其势诚难，但得稍缓即已幸矣。其惟调养得宜而日培根本乎？[80p]

Tinnitus should be discerned between the true and the false: Generally, loud and abrupt sounds are often due to excess, while soft and gradual sounds are more likely due to deficiency. For younger individuals with heat in the body, it tends to be excess; for those in middle age with no heat, it tends to be deficiency. Drinking rich alcoholic beverages and having thick flavors often leads to phlegm and heat, indicating excess, while having a clear quality and fine pulse often points to fatigue and deficiency. Additionally, the ears are the orifice of the kidneys, where the ancestral essence converges. When the vital energy is balanced and kidney energy is sufficient, the ears and eyes are sharp; if labor exhausts the blood and energy, leading to a depletion of essence and weakness of the kidneys, deafness will inevitably result. Therefore, after middle age, many people experience tinnitus that resembles the sound of wind, rain, cicadas, or tides, which is indicative of the decline of yin and deficiency of the kidneys. The classics state: "At forty, the yin energy is already half, which signifies decline." Furthermore, referring to the "I Ching," its symbolism is particularly relevant. The "I Ching" states: "Kan represents the ear," suggesting that the yang of Kan dwells in the center, and the clarity of the ear resides within, hence their correspondence. Nowadays, elderly individuals often have ears that do not hear internally but sound externally, which is precisely a sign of weakened kidney essence and gradually diminishing yang energy. Seeking recovery is indeed difficult, yet merely finding a way to ease the situation would be fortunate. Ultimately, proper nourishment and daily cultivation of the fundamentals are essential.[80p]

　　　　　论治

　　火盛而耳鸣耳闭者。当察火之微甚，及体质之强弱而清之降之。火之甚者宜抽薪饮、大分清饮、当归龙荟丸之类主之。火之微者宜徙薪饮；兼阴虚者，宜加减一阴煎、清化饮之类；兼痰者宜清膈饮主之。　　气逆而闭者，宜六安煎加香附、丹皮、厚朴、枳壳之类主之。　　气逆兼火者，宜加山栀、龙胆草、天花粉之类主之。　　气逆兼风寒者，加川芎、细辛、苏叶、菖蒲、蔓荆子、柴胡之类主之。　　伤寒外感，发热头痛不解而聋者，当于伤寒门察证治之，邪解而耳自愈也。但伤寒耳聋，虽属少阳之证，然必因虚所以有之，故仲景亦以为阳气虚也。[81p]

On Governance

When there is a strong fire resulting in tinnitus and ear blockage, one should carefully assess the nuances of the fire's intensity and the strength or weakness of the body, and then correspondingly clear or subdue it. For excessive fire, one should use methods such as withdrawing fuel, administering large quantities of clearing drinks, or employing formulas like Danggui Longhui Pills. For mild fire, shifting to lighter drinks is appropriate; if there is also a deficiency in yin, one should add or reduce with a Yin Decoction or Clearing Transformation Drink; if phlegm is present, a Clearing Barrier Drink should be used.

If there is upward-acting qi causing blockage, one should use Liu'an Decoction with the addition of Xiangfu, Danpi, Houpo, and Zhi Ke. In cases where qi is reversed along with fire, the addition of Shan Zhi, Longdancao, or Tianhuafen is advisable. If there is upward qi combined with wind and cold, one should add Chuanxiong, Xixin, Suye, Changpu, Manjingzi, and Chaihu.

For exogenous cold damage leading to fever, headache, and unrelieved deafness, one should examine and treat according to the cold damage category, as resolving the pathogen will lead to the natural healing of the ears. However, deafness from cold damage, although classified under the Shaoyang syndrome, must arise from deficiency; thus, Zhongjing also acknowledged it as a deficiency of yang energy.[81p]

是以凡遇此证，必当专顾元气，有邪者兼以散邪，且可因耳之轻重以察病之进退。若因治而聋渐轻者，其病将愈；聋渐甚者，病必日甚也。其有聋闭至极而丝毫无闻者，此其肾气已绝，最是大凶之兆。　　虚闭证，凡十二经脉皆有所主，而又惟肝肾为最。若老年衰弱及素禀阴虚之人，皆宜以大补元煎，或左归、右归丸、肉苁蓉丸，或十全大补汤之类主之。　　若忧愁思虑太过而聋者，宜平补镇心丹、辰砂妙香散之类主之。　　若阳虚于上者，宜补中益气汤、归脾汤之类，凡诸补剂中，或以川芎、石菖蒲、远志、细辛、升麻、柴胡之类，皆可随宜加用，但因虚而闭或已久者，终不易愈。　　窍闭证韭因气血之咎而病在窍也，当用法以通之。[82p]

Therefore, whenever encountering this syndrome, one must focus on nourishing the vital energy. If there are pathologies present, they should also dissipate the pathogenic factors, and one can assess the condition's progression based on the heaviness or lightness of the deafness. If the hearing gradually improves, the illness will likely recover; if the deafness worsens, the condition will certainly deteriorate. If there is complete deafness with no sound perceived at all, it indicates the essence of the kidneys has been utterly exhausted, which is an extremely ominous sign.

In the case of deafness due to deficiency, all twelve meridians have their respective influences, but the liver and kidneys are the most crucial. For the elderly who are weak or those with congenital Yin deficiency, it is advisable to use tonifying formulas such as "Great Nourishing Yuan Decoction," or "Left Return Pill," "Right Return Pill," "Cistanche Pill," or "Decoction of Complete Nutrients" to treat them.

If the deafness arises from excessive worry and contemplation, it is appropriate to use calming remedies like "Calming the Heart Pill" or "Mercury and Aromatic Powder."

If there is Yang deficiency in the upper body, formulas such as "Middle Tonifying and Qi Invigorating Decoction" or "Returning the Spleen Decoction" should be used. Among various tonics, one may consider adding herbs like Chuanxiong, Acorus, Polygala, Asarum, Schizonepeta, or Bupleurum as needed. However, when the deficiency and blockage have persisted for a long time, recovery is difficult.

In cases of blockage affecting the orifices, the disease results from issues with Qi and blood, and treatment should aim to unblock these pathways.[82p]

　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

　　　　　耳聋

　　耳聋者，肾经病也。论理该用六味地黄丸，内加柴胡五钱，甘菊、白芍各二两，当归、枸杞、麦冬各三两，北五味三钱。今不用此而用鼠胆一枚，龙齿、冰片、麝香、朱砂各一分，乳香、潮脑各半分，各研为绝细末，以人乳为丸，如梧子大，外用丝绵裹之，不可太大，塞入耳之深处，至不可受而止。塞三日取出，即耳聪，永不再聋，不必三丸。但鼠胆最难得，觅一大鼠，先以竹笼养之，后以纸为匣子，引其藏身，内用果品，令其自食，久之忽然用棒椎击死，立时取胆，则胆在肝中也，否则再不可得也。干者可用，只消用水调化，俱入药末中，则一样也。实耳聋者，亦用此方神效。又方用珍珠一粒，外用龙骨末一分，以蜜调之，丸在珠上，外用丹砂为衣，绵裹塞其中即愈，神方也。一月后取出，再用六味地黄丸一料，永不再聋。[83p]

Secret Formula of the Stone Chamber
Qing Dynasty, Chen Shiduo

Deafness

Deafness is a disease of the kidney meridian. In principle, it should be treated with Liuwei Dihuang Wan (Six-Flavor Rehmannia Pill), adding five qian of Chaihu (Bupleurum), two liang each of Ganju (sweet chrysanthemum) and Baishao (white peony), three liang each of Danggui (angelica) and Gouqi (goji berries), and three qian of Beiwuweizi (five-flavored) as well. However, instead of this, one uses a rat's gallbladder, one piece, along with one fen each of Longchi (dragon tooth), Bingpian (borneol), Musk, and Zhushā (cinnabar), half a fen each of Ruxiang (frankincense) and Chaosha (amber). Grind them into an extremely fine powder, form into pills the size of a nut using human milk, and wrap them in silk wadding. They should not be too large and must be inserted deep into the ear until it can no longer be tolerated. After three days, remove them, and the hearing will be restored, never to be deaf again; three pills are not necessary.

However, acquiring the rat's gallbladder is quite difficult. One should find a large rat, first raise it in a bamboo cage, then use paper to create a box that lures it to hide inside, placing food inside so it eats. After some time, suddenly strike it on the head to kill it, and immediately obtain the gallbladder; it is located in the liver, otherwise, it cannot be acquired again. If it is dried, it can still be used; just dissolve it in water, and mix it into the medicinal powder. This method is indeed effective for those with true deafness.

Additionally, one can use a grain of pearl, with one fen of Longgu (dragon bone) powdered, mixed with honey to form a pill over the pearl, wrapping it in powdered cinnabar before inserting it; this is also a miraculous method. After a month, take it out and then use a dose of Liuwei Dihuang Wan to ensure that one will never be deaf again.[83p]

　　　　　耳痒

　　耳中作痒，以木刺之，尚不足以安其痒，必以铁刀刺其底，铮铮有声，始觉快然，否则痒极欲死。此肾肝之火，结成铁底于耳中，非汤药可救。予立一方，用龙骨一钱，皂角刺一条，烧灰存性，冰片三分，雄鼠胆一枚，先将前药为末，后以鼠胆水调匀，而后以人乳再调，如厚糊一般，将此药尽抹入耳孔内，必然痒不可当，必须人执其两手，痒定而自愈矣。愈后服六味丸三十斤可也。[84p]

Itchy Ears

When one experiences itchiness in the ears, using a wooden splinter is not sufficient to soothe the itch. One must use an iron tool to pierce it deeply, producing a clear sound, before one can feel relief; otherwise, the itch can be unbearably intense. This is due to the fire from the kidneys and liver, which forms an iron-like substance in the ears, and cannot be treated with simple herbal remedies. I have devised a prescription: use one qian of dragon bone, one stalk of soap pod, burn them to ash while retaining their properties, three fen of borneol, and one male mouse gall. First, grind the initial ingredients into a fine powder, then mix with the mouse gall in water, and finally blend with human milk until it resembles thick paste. This mixture should be thoroughly applied into the ear canal; the itch will be overwhelming, and one must have someone hold their hands down until the itch subsides and self-healing occurs. After recovery, one may take thirty jin of Liuwei Wan.[84p]

　　　　　耳鸣

　　耳中闻蚂蚁战鬬之声者，此则非祟，乃肾水耗尽，又加怒气伤肝所致。方用柴胡、白芥子、栀子各三钱，熟地、山茱萸、白芍各三两，麦冬一两，水煎服。方中纯是补肾平肝之圣药，饮之数日，其战鬬之声渐远，服一月即愈。
　　　　方

　　补中益气汤 【东垣】 　治气虚，清气下陷，浊气上升，耳聋不闻声。　　黄芪一钱　白朮　人参各三分　炙甘草五分　当归身酒制　橘皮　升麻　柴胡各二分　水二盏，煎至一盏，温服。咳嗽去人参。
　　四物汤　治血虚耳聋。
　　熟地二钱　川芎八分　当归身　白芍各一钱　右为粗末，水煎。
　　四君子汤　治气虚耳聋。
　　白朮二钱　人参　茯苓各一钱　炙甘草五分　姜枣水煎。
　　八珍汤　治气血两虚而聋者。
　　人参　白朮　茯苓　炙甘草　熟地黄　当归　白芍　川芎　水煎服。[85p]

Tinnitus

Hearing the sounds of ants battling in the ears is not a spirit affliction; rather, it is caused by the depletion of kidney water, further exacerbated by anger harming the liver. The prescription includes three qian each of Chai Hu, Bai Jie Zi, and Zhi Zi, along with three liang each of Shu Di, Shan Zhu Yu, and Bai Shao, one liang of Mai Dong, boiled in water for consumption. This formula contains purely tonic ingredients for nourishing the kidneys and soothing the liver. After a few days of taking it, the battling sounds will gradually fade, and one month of use will lead to recovery.

Formula

Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction [from Dong Yuan] Treats qi deficiency, clears downward-escaping qi, and alleviates upward-rising turbid qi, aiding hearing loss. Contains one qian of Huang Qi, three fen each of Bai Zhu and Ren Shen, five fen of roasted Gan Cao, two fen each of Dang Gui (prepared with alcohol), Chen Pi, Sheng Ma, and Chai Hu, boiled in two bowls of water until reduced to one bowl, and taken warm. Omit Ren Shen for cough.

Si Wu Decoction Treats blood deficiency hearing loss. Contains two qian of Shu Di, eight fen of Chuan Xiong, and one qian each of Dang Gui and Bai Shao, ground into coarse powder and boiled in water.

Si Jun Zi Decoction Treats qi deficiency hearing loss. Contains two qian of Bai Zhu, one qian each of Ren Shen and Fu Ling, five fen of roasted Gan Cao, boiled with ginger and dates.

Ba Zhen Decoction Treats dual deficiencies of qi and blood with hearing loss. Contains equal parts of Ren Shen, Bai Zhu, Fu Ling, roasted Gan Cao, Shu Di, Dang Gui, Bai Shao, and Chuan Xiong, boiled and taken as a decoction.[85p]

　　六味丸　治肾经不足，头运耳聋等证。　　熟地黄八两　山茱萸肉　干山药　牡丹皮　白茯苓　泽泻各三两　右各另为末，和地黄膏加炼蜜丸，桐子大，每服七八十丸，空心食前滚汤下。
　　大安肾丸　治肾经久积阴寒，膀胱虚冷，下元衰惫耳重，常服补元阳益肾气。　　肉桂去粗皮，不见火　川乌头炮去皮脐，各一斤　桃仁麸炒　白蒺藜炒，去刺　巴戟去心　山药　茯苓　肉苁蓉酒浸，炙　石斛去根，炙　萆薢　白朮　破故纸各四十八两　右为末，炼蜜为丸，如梧桐子大，每服三十丸，温酒或盐汤下，空心食前。
　　小安肾丸　治肾气虚乏，下元冷惫，精神昏愦，耳作蝉鸣等证。　　川练子盐四两，水四升同煮，候干切焙　香附子　川乌头各一斤　蘹香十二两　熟地黄八两　川椒去目及闭口者，微炒出汗，四两右六味为细末，酒糊为丸，如桐子大，每服二十丸，空心临卧盐汤酒任下。[86p]

Liuwéi Wán: Treats deficiency in the kidney channel, symptoms such as dizziness and hearing loss. Ingredients: eight taels of cooked Rehmannia, three taels each of Schisandra, dried yam, peony root, white poria, and water plantain. Grind all separately into powder, mix with Rehmannia paste and honey to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take seventy to eighty pills with hot soup before meals on an empty stomach.

Dà'ān Shèn Wán: Treats long-standing accumulation of cold in the kidney channel, bladder deficiency and cold, fatigue in the lower regions, and heaviness in the ears. Regular use can tonify the original yang and enhance kidney energy. Ingredients: one pound each of rough-skinned cinnamon (removed) and processed Aconite (skinned), pan-fried peach kernels, pan-fried white thistle (spines removed), barren-wort (heart removed), yam, poria, and alcohol-soaked, roasted Cistanche, along with Dendrobium (roots removed and roasted), bittersweet herb, and processed paper mulberry, each four and a half taels. Grind all into powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take thirty pills with warm wine or salty soup before meals on an empty stomach.

Xiǎo'ān Shèn Wán: Treats kidney energy deficiency, cold fatigue in the lower regions, mental confusion, and symptoms like tinnitus. Ingredients: four taels of salt from river pepper, cooked with four sheng (about eight pints) of water, then dried and baked. One pound each of nutmeg and processed Aconite, twelve taels of aromatic cyperus, eight taels of cooked Rehmannia, four taels of pepper (seeds and closed ones removed and lightly fried), and six other ingredients powdered finely, mixed with a wine paste to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take twenty pills with salty soup or wine before bedtime on an empty stomach.[86p]

　　滚痰丸　治耳聋、耳鸣、耳痒等证之由于痰火实盛者。　　大黄蒸少顷，翻过再蒸少顷，取出，不可过　黄芩各八两　沉香　青蒙石煅如金色　百药煎，各五钱　右为末，水丸，如梧桐子大，白汤食后空心服。此方用百药煎，乃得之方外秘传。盖此丸得此药，乃能收摄周身顽涎聚于一处，然后利下，甚有奇功。
　　沉香降气散　治阴阳壅滞，气不升降，耳窍闭塞。　　沉香二钱八分　砂仁七钱五分　香附子盐水炒，去毛，六两二钱五分　甘草炙，五钱五分　右为极细末，每服二钱，入盐少许，沸汤调服，不拘时。
　　指迷七气汤　治七情相干，阴阳不得升降，气道壅滞，耳窍闭塞。　　香附子二钱　青皮去瓤　陈皮去白　桔梗　蓬朮　官桂　藿香　益智仁　半夏汤洗七次　甘草炙，各一钱　水二锺，生姜三片，红枣二枚，煎一锺，食远服。[87p]

Phlegm Pill: Treats ear deafness, tinnitus, and ear itching caused by excessive phlegm-heat. Steep rhubarb for a short time, turn it over and steep again for a moment, take it out, and do not exceed. Eight taels of both rhubarb and Scutellaria; agarwood and calamine, calcined to a golden color; brew with a hundred herbs, five qian each. Grind the above into powder, make into pills as big as wu-tong seeds, and take with clear soup on an empty stomach after meals. This formula uses the hundred herbs brew, obtained from secret transmission outside of the standard methods. The pill, from this medicine, can gather stubborn phlegm throughout the body in one place, then it can be purged downwards, which has remarkable effects.

Agarwood Qi-Descending Powder: Treats the stagnation of yin and yang, where qi does not rise or fall and ear passages are blocked. Two taels and eight fen of agarwood, seven taels and five fen of cardamom, six taels and two and a half fen of cyperus roasted in salty water and fur removed, five taels and five fen of honey-fried licorice. Grind the above into a very fine powder, take two taels each time, add a little salt, and mix with boiling soup for taking, at any time.

Seven Emotions Confusion Decoction: Treats the disturbance of the seven emotions, the inability for yin and yang to rise or fall, stagnation of qi pathways, and blocked ear passages. Two taels of cyperus, peel and remove the pulp of orange peel, remove the white part of dried tangerine peel, prepare platycodon, wormwood, cassia, patchouli, wolfberry, washed with half summer for seven times, and honey-fried licorice, one qian each. Use two zhongs of water, three slices of fresh ginger, and two red dates to decoct one zhòng, and take it after meals.[87p]

　　流气饮子　治五脏不和，三焦气壅，耳闭无闻。　　紫苏叶　青皮去白　当归　芍药　半夏汤洗　乌药　茯苓　桔梗　川芎　黄芪　枳实麸炒，各一钱　木香　防风去芦　槟榔　陈皮去白　炙甘草　大腹子连皮　枳壳麸炒，各五分　生姜三片，红枣一枚，水煎，不拘时服。
　　苏子降气汤　治虚阳上攻，气不升降，上盛下虚，耳聋等证。　　紫苏子炒　半夏汤泡，各二钱五分　前胡去芦　炙甘草　厚朴去皮，姜炙炒　陈皮去白，各一钱　当归去芦，一钱五分　沉香七分水二锺，生姜三片，煎至一锺，不拘时服。
　　养正丹　治上盛下虚，气不升降，元阳亏损。　　水银　黑锡去滓，净秤，与水银结砂子　磺黄研　朱砂研细，各一两　右用黑盏一只，火上镕黑铅成汁；次下水银，以柳条搅；次下朱砂，搅令不见星子，放下少时方入硫黄，急搅成汁和匀。如有焰，以酢洒之。候冷取出，研极细末，煮糯米糊丸，绿豆大，每三十丸，盐汤枣汤任下。[88p]

Liuqi Yinzi: For treating disharmonies of the five organs, stagnation in the three burners, and deafness. Ingredients: a qian of perilla leaves, green tangerine peel (white part removed), angelica, peony, half summer, washed, costus, poria, platycodon, ligusticum, astragalus, and fried immature bitter orange; each one qian. Additionally, half qian each of saussurea, siler (reed part removed), betel nut, and dried tangerine peel (white part removed); three slices of fresh ginger, one red date; boil in water and consume at any time.

Suzizi Jiangqi Tang: For treating hyperactive Yang deficiency, failure of Qi to rise or descend, excess above with deficiency below, and deafness among other symptoms. Ingredients: two qian five fen each of fried perilla seeds and half summer soaked; one qian each of prepared fritillaria (reed part removed), licorice, and dried magnolia bark (peel removed, ginger roasted); one qian five fen of angelica (reed part removed); seven fen of agarwood, two chong of water; three slices of fresh ginger; boil until reduced to one chong, consume at any time.

Yangzheng Dan: For treating excess above with deficiency below, failure of Qi to rise or descend, and loss of original Yang. Ingredients: one liang of mercury, lead (dross removed), cleaned and weighed, combined with mercury to create a sand-like substance; one liang of finely ground yellow sulfur; one liang of finely ground cinnabar. Method: Take a black bowl, melt lead over fire to form a juice, then add mercury and stir with willow branches; add cinnabar, stirring until it is no longer visible. Leave for a short time before adding sulfur and stir vigorously to blend. If flames appear, sprinkle vinegar on it. Allow to cool, take out, grind to a very fine powder, and prepare ball-shaped pills the size of green beans with glutinous rice paste; consume thirty pills with either salt water or jujube soup as desired.[88p]

　　复原通气散　治气不宣流，或成疮疖，耳聋耳痒。　　舶上茴香炒　穿山甲蛤粉炒　延胡索　陈皮　白牵牛炒　甘草炙，各一两　木香不见火，两半　右为细末，每服二钱，用热酒调，食后服。不用酒者煎南木香汤调下。
　　防风通圣散　治证同上。
　　防风　川芎　当归　白芍药　大黄　薄荷叶　麻黄去节　连翘　芒硝各五钱　石膏　黄芩　桔梗各一两　滑石三两甘草二两　荆芥穗　白朮　栀子各二钱半　右为末，每服二钱，水一大盏，生姜三片，煎六分，温服。
　　排风汤　治风虚冷湿，邪气入脏，重耳不闻人声。此汤聪耳明目，通脏腑。　　白藓皮　当归酒浸一宿　肉桂去粗皮　防风　白芍药　杏仁去皮尖，麸炒　炙甘草　芎藭　白朮各二两　独活　麻黄去节　茯苓各三两　右为粗末，每服三钱，水一盏半，姜四片，煎八分，去滓，温服，不拘时。[89p]

Fuyuan Tongqi San: Treats unexpressed qi, which may lead to sores and boils, as well as ear deafness and itching. Ingredients: roasted fennel from overseas, fried pangolin powder, Yanhusuo, dried tangerine peel, fried white morning glory, and prepared licorice, each 1 liang; wood fragrance not burned, in half. Grind into a fine powder. Take 2 qian each time, mixed with hot wine after meals. For those who do not use wine, brew with Namu Xiang decoction instead.

Fangfeng Tongsheng San: Treats the same symptoms as above.

Ingredients: Fangfeng, Chuanxiong, Angelica, Bai Shao Yao, Dahuang, mint leaves, Ma Huang (with joints removed), Lianqiao, Mangxiao each 5 qian; gypsum, Huangqin, and Jiegeng each 1 liang; talcum powder 3 liang and licorice 2 liang; Jingjie, Bai Zhu, and Zhi Zi each 2.5 qian. Grind into a powder. Take 2 qian each time, boiled in a large cup of water with 3 slices of ginger, decocted to 6 parts, and take warm.

Paifeng Tang: Treats wind deficiency, cold, and dampness, with evil qi entering the organs, leading to a heavy ear that cannot hear human voices. This soup clears the ears, sharpens eyesight, and opens the organs. Ingredients: white lichen skin, Angelica soaked in wine overnight, cassia bark (with rough skin removed), Fangfeng, Bai Shao Yao, peeled apricot kernels roasted, fried licorice, Chuanxiong, and Bai Zhu each 2 liang; Duhuo, Ma Huang (with joints removed), and Fuling each 3 liang. Grind into a coarse powder. Take 3 qian each time, with 1.5 cups of water, 4 slices of ginger, decocted to 8 parts, strain, and take warm at any time.[89p]

　　不换金正气散　治耳疮出脓水。
　　苍朮炙　橘皮去白　半夏曲　厚朴姜炙　藿香各二钱　甘草炙，一钱　生姜五片，红枣二枚，煎服。
　　正元散　治证同上。
　　红豆炒　干姜泡　陈皮去白，各三钱　人参　白朮　炙甘草　茯苓去皮，各二两　乌药去木　附子炮，去皮尖　山药姜汁浸炒川芎　干葛各一两　黄芪炙，一两五钱　肉桂去粗皮　川乌炮去皮，各五钱　右为细末，每服三钱，姜三片，枣一枚，盐少许，煎七分，食前温服。
　　木香槟榔丸　御药　治证同上
　　木香　槟榔　枳壳麸炒　杏仁去皮尖，炒研　青皮去瓤，各一两　半夏曲　皂角去白，酥炙　(木郁)李仁去皮，各二两　右为细末，别以皂角四两，用浆水一碗，槎揉熬膏，更入熟蜜少许，和丸梧子大，每服五十丸，食后姜汤下。[90p]

Here is the translated text:

"No Change Golden Vitality Powder"
Treats ear ulcers producing pus.
Ingredients: 2 qian each of dried Atractylodes, roasted tangerine peel (without white part), Pinellia ternata, roasted Magnolia bark, and patchouli; 1 qian of roasted licorice; 5 slices of fresh ginger; 2 red dates. Decoct and take.

"Zhengyuan Powder"
Treats the same symptoms as above.
Ingredients: 3 qian each of fried adzuki beans, soaked dried ginger, and tangerine peel (without white part); 2 liang each of ginseng, white Atractylodes, roasted licorice, and peeled Poria; 1 liang each of Sichuan angelica, fried wild ginger, and dried kudzu; 1.5 liang of roasted astragalus; 5 qian each of cassia (without thick skin) and fried Aconite (peeled); Adjust each into a fine powder. Take 3 qian each time with 3 slices of ginger, 1 date, and a pinch of salt, decoct until reduced to 7 parts, and take warm before meals.

"Wood Fragrance Betel Nut Pill"
Imperial medicine for the same symptoms as above.
Ingredients: 2 liang each of wood fragrance, betel nut, fried bitter orange peel, peeled and roasted almond (tip removed), and peeled green tangerine (without pulp); 2 liang each of Pinellia ternata and soapberry (without white part), roasted, with the addition of 2 liang of (Mu Yu) plum kernels (peeled). All are to be ground into fine powder. Keep aside 4 liang of soapberry, used with 1 bowl of liquid, knead to make a paste, then add a little cooked honey, and form into balls the size of walnuts. Take 50 pills after meals with ginger soup.**[90p]

　　越鞠丸　治证同上。
　　香附炒　苍朮米泔水浸一宿，炒　川芎各二两　山栀炒　神曲各一两五钱　右为末，滴水丸梧子大，每服一百丸，白汤下。
　　平补镇心丹 【《和剂》】 　治虚人耳聋。　　酸枣仁去皮炒，二钱半　车前子　白茯苓去皮　麦门冬去心　肉桂去粗皮，不见火　五味子　茯神去木，各一两二钱半　龙齿　熟地黄酒蒸　天门冬去心　山药姜汁炒　远志去心，甘草水煮，各一两半　人参　朱砂细研为衣，各五钱　右为末，炼蜜丸，如桐子大，每服三十丸，空心米汤温酒任下。

Yue Ju Wan: Treatment evidence as above.

Xiang Fu Chao: Soak Cang Zhu in rice wash overnight, then fry. Mix with Chuan Xiong, each two taels, with fried Shan Zhi and Shen Qu, each one tael and five qian. This is ground into powder. Form into pills the size of a nut, take one hundred pills each time, with warm water.

Ping Bu Zhen Xin Dan (from "He Ji"): Treats hearing loss in the weak. The following ingredients are used: Xu Zao Ren, peeled and fried, two and a half qian; Che Qian Zi, Bai Fu Ling, peeled; Mai Men Dong, heart removed; Rou Gui, coarse skin removed, uncooked; Wu Wei Zi; Fu Shen, wood removed, each one tael and two and a half qian; Long Chi; Shou Di Huang steamed in wine; Tian Men Dong, heart removed; Shan Yao fried with ginger juice; Yuan Zhi, heart removed; and Gan Cao boiled in water, each one tael and five qian. Ren Shen and Zhu Sha finely ground for coating, each five qian. This is ground into powder, formed into honey pills the size of a sycamore seed; take thirty pills each time, with warm rice soup or warm wine.

Wu Ling San (Zhong Jing): Treats phlegm and water rising, ear deafness and buzzing. Ingredients include: Zhu Ling, Fu Ling, Bai Zhu, each eighteen qian; Rou Gui, half a tael; Ze Xie, one tael and six qian and a half. This is ground into powder. Take three qian each time. After taking, drink plenty of hot water; sweating will lead to recovery.[91p]

　　二陈汤　治痰火耳聋。
　　茯苓　陈皮　半夏各一钱　甘草五分　生姜二片，水煎服。
　　青木香丸　治痰水耳聋。

　　一粒金丹 【东垣】 　治耳鸣耳聋，或耳中生疮。　　荜茇以猪胆汁拌匀，入胆内悬，待阴干　青黛　延胡索　白芷　川芎各一两　右为细末，用无根水为丸，每用一丸，以无根水化开口　畜鼻内，更以铜钱咬口内出涎。[92p]

Er Chen Decoction: Treats phlegm-fire deafness.
Ingredients:

  • Poria (Fu Ling) - 1 qian
  • Chen Pi (dried tangerine peel) - 1 qian
  • Ban Xia - 1 qian
  • Licorice - 0.5 qian
  • Fresh Ginger - 2 slices
    Prepare by boiling these in water.

Qing Mu Xiang Pill: Treats water-phlegm deafness.
Ingredients:

  • Black Qian Niu (cowherb) - 240 liang, stir-fried until fragrant, take 120 liang of the head powder.
  • Betel Nut wrapped in sour corn rice, wet paper bag, roasted in fire until the paper chars, remove rice.
  • Bu Gu Zhi (Psoralea fruit) stir-fried until fragrant - 40 liang
  • Bi Cheng Qie (fragrant herb) - 40 liang
  • Mu Xiang (costus root) - 20 liang
    Grind the above into fine powder, combine with clear water to form pills the size of mung beans. Take 30 pills at a time, with hot tea or soup.

Xiao Chai Hu Decoction: Treats deafness from liver fire in deficient individuals.
Ingredients:

  • Chai Hu - 8 liang
  • Ban Xia - 8 liang
  • Ren Shen (ginseng) - 3 liang
  • Huang Qin (scutellaria) - 3 liang
  • Fresh Ginger - 3 liang
  • Licorice - 3 liang
  • Da Zao (dates) - 12 pieces, split
    Prepare by boiling these seven ingredients in 1 dou 2 sheng of water to yield 6 sheng, strain, then re-boil to obtain 3 sheng. Warmly take 1 sheng, 3 times a day.

One Grain Golden Pill: Treats tinnitus, deafness, or ulcers in the ear.
Ingredients:

  • Bi Jiao (pepper) mixed with pig bile, placed inside a bile sack to dry in the shade.
  • Qing Dai (indigo) - 1 liang
  • Yan Hu Suo (corydalis) - 1 liang
  • Bai Zhi (angelica) - 1 liang
  • Chuan Xiong (ligusticum) - 1 liang
    Grind the above into fine powder, use rootless water to form pills. When using, dissolve one pill with rootless water, use to moisten the nostrils, then bite the pill with a copper coin to produce saliva.[92p]

　　人参散
　　人参　炙甘草　龙齿各二两　犀角屑　生地　白茯苓去皮，各一两　麦门冬去心，一两五钱　右口　父咀，每服五钱，水一中盏，煎至七分，去滓，温服，不拘时。
　　妙香散 【《良方》】

　　人参　茯神　黄芪炙　酸枣仁炒研　龙眼肉　白朮各二钱五分　木香　炙甘草各五分　水二锺　生姜五片，红枣一枚，煎一锺服。薛新甫加远志、当归各一钱。[93p]

Ginseng Powder
Ginseng, roasted licorice, and dragon teeth, each two taels; rhinoceros horn powder, fresh ground earth, and white coix, all peeled, each one tael; wheat kernel heart, one tael and five qian. For each dose, take five qian, with one medium cup of water, decoct until reduced to seven-tenths, then strain. Take warm, without regard to time.

Miao Xiang Powder (from Liang Fang)
Yam, stir-fried with ginger juice; poria, spirit of poria, fried astragalus, and fried polygala, each one tael; ginseng, balloon flower root, and roasted licorice, each five qian; wood aromatic, two taels and five qian; cinnabar three taels; musk one tael, ground separately. The above shall be finely powdered. For each dose, take two qian, at any time, with warm wine.

Wujin Powder (from San Yin)
Yellow lead, stir-fried; fine ink, burned, each one tael. The above is finely powdered and mixed evenly. For each dose, take three qian. After eating, rinse the mouth with water, and when feeling heat in the heart and thirst, take with cold water.

Gui Pi Decoction (from Ji Sheng)
Ginseng, spirit of poria, roasted astragalus, stir-fried sour jujube seed, longan flesh, and white atractylodes, each two taels and five qian; wood aromatic and roasted licorice, each five qian; water two zhong; five slices of fresh ginger, and one red date. Decoct until one zhong remains for consumption. Xue Xinfu adds one qian each of polygala and angelica.[93p]

　　四生散 【《和剂》】
　　黄芪　川羌活　蒺藜　白附子各等分，生用　右为末，每服二钱，薄荷酒调下。
　　凉膈散
　　栀子　连翘　薄荷　黄芩　甘草各一两五钱　大黄　芒硝各五钱　右为粗末，每一两水二盏，竹叶七片，煎至一盏，去滓，入蜜少许，食后服。
　　逍遥散 【《元戎》】
　　当归　白芍　白朮　柴胡　甘草　茯神各等分　右，姜水煎服。
　　紫金丹 【《本事》】
　　淡豆豉好者二钱，用水略润少时，以纸挹干，研膏　白砒水飞，半钱　右用豉膏子和砒，同杵，极匀，如麻子大，每服五丸至十丸，量大小与之，并用腊茶清极冷吞下，临卧以知为度。
　　调中益气汤 【东垣】
　　黄芪一钱　人参　甘草　当归　白朮各五分　五味子十五粒　白芍　柴胡　升麻各三分　橘皮二分　右，水二盏，煎一盏，去滓，服食前。[94p]

Si Sheng San
Huang Qi, Chuan Qiang Huo, Jili, and Bai Fu Zi, all equal parts, to be used fresh. Grind into a powder. Take two qian mixed with mint wine.

Liang Ge San
Zhi Zi, Lian Qiao, Bo He, Huang Qin, and Gan Cao each five qian; Da Huang and Mang Xiao each five qian. This is coarsely ground. For each one liang, use two zhan of water, seven bamboo leaves, boil until one zhan remains, strain, add a little honey, and take after meals.

Xiao Yao San
Dang Gui, Bai Shao, Bai Zhu, Chai Hu, Gan Cao, and Fu Shen, all in equal parts. Take with ginger water decoction.

Zi Jin Dan
Use two qian of good Dan Dou Chi, moisten with water for a short time, then dry with paper. Grind into a paste. Half qian of white arsenic, mix the arsenic with the paste until very uniform, about the size of a sesame seed. Take five to ten pills each time, depending on size, and swallow with very cold wax tea just before lying down.

Tiao Zhong Yi Qi Tang
One qian of Huang Qi, five fen each of Ren Shen, Gan Cao, Dang Gui, Bai Zhu, fifteen grains of Wu Wei Zi, and three fen each of Bai Shao, Chai Hu, and Sheng Ma, with two fen of Ju Pi. Add to two zhan of water, boil down to one zhan, strain, and take before meals.[94p]

耳门

　　　　方

　　桂星散 【《准绳》，下同】 　治风火闭塞，耳窍不闻。　　辣桂　川芎　当归　石菖蒲　细辛　木通　木香　白蒺藜炒，去刺　麻黄　甘草炙，各一钱　白芷梢　天南星煨制，各一钱五分　右，水二锺，葱白二根，紫苏五叶，姜五片，煎至一锺，食后服。一方加全蝎去毒一钱。
　　磁石羊肾丸　治风虚不爽，时有重听，或有风痹之状。　　磁石二两，火煅醋淬七次，用葱子一合，木通三两入水同煎，一昼夜去葱并木通　川椒去目　防风　石枣去核　远志肉　白朮炒　白茯苓　细辛　菟丝子酒浸　川芎　山药炒　木香　当归身　鹿茸酒浸一宿，炙　黄芪制　川乌炮，各一两　石菖蒲一两五钱　肉桂六钱五分　熟地黄九蒸，二两　右为细末，用羊肾两对去膜，以酒煮烂，和诸药末捣，以煮肾酒打糊和丸，如梧子大，每服百十丸，空心温酒盐汤任下。仍服清神散，二药相间服。忌牛肉鸡鸭子。[95p]

Complete Compilation of Ancient and Modern Books, Volume 136

Ear Gate

Formula

Cinnamon Star Powder
For treating wind-heat obstruction and inability to hear.
Ingredients:

  • Spicy cinnamon
  • Chuanxiong
  • Angelica
  • Acorus
  • Asarabacca
  • Akebia
  • Saussurea (white thistle, roasted and de-spined)
  • Ephedra
  • Licorice (prepared)
    Each 3 grams.
  • White atractylodes (tips)
  • Tian nanxing (processed)
    Each 4.5 grams.

Combine with two cups of water, two scallions, five leaves of perilla, and five slices of ginger, and decoct to one cup. Take after meals. One variant adds one de-toxified whole scorpion (3 grams).

Magnetic Stone and Sheep Kidney Pill
For treating wind deficiency with intermittent hearing loss and symptoms of wind-damp phlegm.
Ingredients:

  • Magnetic stone (20 grams, calcined and vine-washed seven times)
  • One bunch of scallions
  • Akebia (30 grams), decocted in water with scallions for a full day
  • Chuanjiao (dried pepper, de-seeded)
  • Fangfeng (literally, wind protection)
  • Stone jujube (de-seeded)
  • Polygala root
  • White atractylodes (roasted)
  • White poria
  • Asarabacca
  • Cuscuta seeds (wine-soaked)
  • Chuanxiong
  • Yam (roasted)
  • Saussurea (wood fragrance)
  • Angelica root
  • Deer antler (wine-soaked overnight, roasted)
  • Astragalus (processed)
  • Chuanwu (poisoned, prepared)

Each 30 grams, except for Saussurea (37.5 grams) and cooked reishi mushroom (60 grams, steamed and dried).

Grind all to a fine powder, using two pairs of de-membraned sheep kidneys, boil in wine until tender, match with the ground herbs to form pills the size of a walnut. Take 100-110 pills with warm wine and salt soup on an empty stomach. Continue with Qing Shen Powder, taking the two medicines alternately. Avoid beef, chicken, and duck.[95p]

　　清神散　治气壅，头目不清，耳常重听。　　甘菊花　白僵蚕炒，各半两　羌活　荆芥穗　木通　川芎　防风各四钱　木香一钱　甘草　石菖蒲各一钱五分　右为细末，每服二钱，食后茶清调服。
　　磁石浸酒方　治风邪之气干于脑，或入于耳，久而不散，经络痞塞，不能宣利，使人耳中悾悾然，或作旋运。　　磁石五两，捣碎，水淘，去赤汁　山茱萸　天雄炮去皮脐，各二两　木通　防风　薯蓣　远志去心　菖蒲　芎藭　细辛　蔓荆子　白茯苓　肉桂干姜炮　甘菊花各一两　熟地黄三两　右銼细和匀，以生绢袋盛，用酒二斗浸七日，每日任性饮之，以瘥为度。[96p]

Qing Shen San: For treating Qi stagnation, when the head feels unclear and the ears often feel heavy with sound. Ingredients: Equal amounts of sweet chrysanthemum and white silkworm, each half a tael; four qians each of qianghuo, jinjie heads, mutong, and chuanxiong; one qian each of muxiang, licorice, and shi chang pu, and one and a half qians each. Crush into a fine powder, and take two qians after meals mixed with clear tea.

Ci Shi Jin Jiu Fang: For treating wind-cold that affects the brain, possibly entering the ears, lingering for a long time, causing blockage in the meridians and preventing smooth flow, leading to a feeling of dullness in the ears or causing vertigo. Ingredients: Five taels of magnetite, crushed and rinsed to remove the red juice; two taels each of shanzhuyu and tianxiong (peeled and with the navel removed); one tael each of mutong, fangfeng, shuyu, yuanzhi (seed removed), changpu, chuanxiong, xixin, and manjingzi; one tael of baifuling, and one tael each of cassia and dried ginger (prepared); three taels of cooked rehmannia. Grind and mix finely, store in a fine silk pouch, and soak in two dou of wine for seven days. Drink freely daily until recovery is achieved.[96p]

　　鱼脑膏　治风聋，年久及耳鸣。
　　鲤鱼脑二两　当归焙　白芷　菖蒲　细辛　附子炮去皮脐，各半两　右除鱼脑外为细末，以鱼脑置银器中，入药在内，微火煎候香，滤去滓，倾入磁器中，候凝，丸如枣核大，绵裹塞耳中。一方无菖蒲，有羊肾脂同鱼脑先熬，次下诸药。
　　羊肾羹　治证同上。
　　杜仲去粗皮，炙黄　黄芪各半两　磁石五两，捣碎，水淘，去赤汁，绵裹悬煎，不得到铛底　羊肾一只，去脂膜，切　肉苁蓉一两，酒浸一宿，去皮炙干　右以水三大碗，先煮磁石，取汁二大碗，下杜仲等又煎，取一盏半，去滓，入羊肾、粳米一合，葱白姜椒盐酢，一如作羹法，空心服。[97p]

Fish brain paste treats wind deafness, which over time leads to tinnitus.

Use two taels of carp brain, and half a tael each of angelica, white atractylodes, sweet flag, fine green onion, and prepared aconite that has had the skin and navel removed. Excluding the fish brain, grind the rest into a fine powder. Place the fish brain in a silver container, add the powdered herbs inside, and simmer on low heat until fragrant. Strain out the residue, pour into a ceramic vessel, let it cool and congeal, then form into pills the size of jujube pits and stuff them into the ears. For a recipe without sweet flag, substitute with sheep kidney fat and stew it with the fish brain before adding the other herbs.

Sheep kidney soup treats the same condition.

Remove the coarse skin from eucommia and roast it until yellow. Use half a tael of astragalus and five taels of magnetite, crush them, rinse with water to remove the red juice, and wrap in cloth for hanging and simmering without touching the bottom of the pot. Take one sheep kidney, remove the fat membrane, and slice. Use one tael of flesh from cistanche, soak in alcohol overnight, peel and dry. Boil three large bowls of water, first cooking the magnetite to extract two bowls of juice, then add eucommia and the others and simmer to obtain one and a half cups, strain out the residues, add the sheep kidney, one fist of glutinous rice, green onion, ginger, pepper, salt, and vinegar, prepared just like making soup, to be taken on an empty stomach.[97p]

　　磁石丸
　　磁石煅，酢淬，七次　防风　羌活　木通　白芍　黄芪盐水浸焙　桂心各一两　人参半两　右为末，用羊肾一对，去脂膜捣烂，打酒糊为丸如桐子大，每服五十丸，空心温酒盐汤下。
　　姜蝎散　治耳聋，气塞肾虚等证。
　　全蝎四十九个，去毒，泡湿　右以糯米半升，于大瓦上铺平，将蝎铺米上焙，令米黄为度，去米不用；又切生姜四十九片，每片置蝎，再焙，姜焦为度，去姜不用，将蝎研为细末。三五日前，每日先服黑锡丹三五服，临服药时，令夜饭半饱，服时看其人酒量，勿令大醉，服已，令熟睡勿得叫醒，却令人轻唤，如不听得，浓煎葱白汤一碗，令饮，五更耳中闻百十攒笙响，便自此闻声。一方无糯米制银石器中炒。
　　犀角饮子　治风热上壅，耳内聋闭，臖肿掣痛，脓血流出。　　犀角镑　木通　石菖蒲　甘菊花　赤芍药　元参　赤小豆炒，各二钱　甘草炙一钱　右，水二锺，姜五片，煎至一锺，不拘时服。[98p]

Magnetic Pill
Calcine the magnetic stone, quench in vinegar seven times. Add equal parts of Fangfeng, Qianghuo, Muxiong, Baishao, Huangqi soaked and baked in salt water, and Gui Xin, each weighing one tael; half a tael of Ren Shen. Use this mixture to grind with a pair of lamb kidneys, removing the fat membrane and smashing it into a paste. Form into pills the size of a tung seed, taking fifty pills each time, with warm wine and salty soup on an empty stomach.

Jiang Xie Powder
For treating deafness, qi blockage, and kidney deficiency.
Use forty-nine whole scorpions, detoxified and soaked. Take half a sheng of glutinous rice, spread it flat on a large tile, and place the scorpions on the rice to bake until the rice turns yellow; discard the rice. Cut forty-nine slices of fresh ginger, placing one slice on each scorpion, then bake until the ginger is charred; discard the ginger. Grind the scorpions into a fine powder. For three to five days prior, take three to five doses of Heixi Dan, and on the day of taking this medicine, ensure to have a half-full meal for dinner. When taking the medicine, observe the person’s alcohol tolerance and avoid overwhelming drunkenness. After taking, allow for restful sleep without waking; if needed, lightly call them. If there’s no response, give a bowl of strong boiled scallion white soup to drink. By dawn, they will hear sounds like a hundred flutes playing, and from then on, their hearing improves. If glutinous rice is not available, stir-fry in a silver vessel instead.

Rhinoceros Horn Drink
For treating wind-heat obstruction, deafness in the ears, swollen pain, and the discharge of pus and blood.
Use powdered rhinoceros horn, Muxiong, Shichangpu, sweet chrysanthemum flowers, Chi Shaoyao, Yuanshen, and roasted red adzuki beans, each weighing two qian; one qian of honey-fried licorice. Combine with two pots of water and five slices of ginger, decoct until reduced to one pot. There are no time restrictions on when to take it.[98p]

Paeony Powder: Used to treat heat and blockage causing wind, with ear pain connected to the head and pus or blood flowing out. Ingredients: Red peony, white peony, Chuanxiong, Mu Biezi, Angelica, Rhubarb, and Licorice, each 1.5 taels. Add water (2 cups), boil down to 1 cup, and take after meals.

Rhinoceros Horn Powder: Used to treat wind toxin and heat obstruction, with phlegm stagnation in the chest, temporary deafness in both ears, heaviness of the head, and dizziness. Ingredients: Rhinoceros horn shavings, sweet chrysanthemum, Qianhu, fried bitter orange, Qianghuo, Acorus, ZeXie, Mu Tong, and raw Rehmannia, each 5 taels. Fu Shen Powder: Used to treat upper Jiao wind heat with sudden deafness and tinnitus, fullness and urgency in the limbs, and chest discomfort with poor digestion. Ingredients: Fu Shen and Mai Dong, each 100 grams; Qianghuo, Fangfeng, Vitex fruit, Job's tears, Acorus, Schisandra, and Huangqi, each 5 taels; mint and Licorice, each 2.5 taels. Grind into a powder. Each dose is 3 taels, with three slices of ginger, boiled in water and strained, taken warm after meals.

Jie Cang Drink: Used to treat qi deficiency and heat obstruction, possibly from hunger and summer heat, with wind heat obstructing upward, resulting in deafness and severe pain in the ears, with pus or blood flowing out. Ingredients: Red peony and white peony, each 5 taels; Angelica, roasted Licorice, steamed Rhubarb, and shelled Mu Biezi, each 100 grams. Grind into a powder. Each dose is 4 taels, boiled in water, and taken warm before lying down after meals.[99p]
